\definecolor{codeborder}{rgb}{0.5,0.5,0.5} % Gray for code box border

    backgroundcolor=\color{codebg}, % Light gray background

% Begin the document
\begin{document}

% Main Heading
\textbf{\huge Java Basics for Spring Boot (Hinglish Me)} % \huge for large font size
\vspace{0.5cm} % Add spacing after the heading
\hrule % Horizontal line to separate sections
\vspace{0.5cm}

% Section 1: Java Kya Hai?
\textbf{\Large 1. Java Kya Hai?} % \Large for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

Java ek \textbf{object-oriented programming (OOP)} language hai. \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\textcolor{examplecolor}{Iska use mainly backend development, web applications, aur mobile apps (Android) banane ke liye hota hai.} \\ % red for examples
\textcolor{warningcolor}{Java platform-independent hai, matlab tum ek baar code likho aur usse kisi bhi platform (Windows, Linux, Mac) pe run kar sakte ho.} \\ % Red for important points

% Section 2: Java Setup
\textbf{\Large 2. Java Setup} % \Large for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

\textbf{JDK (Java Development Kit):} Java code likhne aur run karne ke liye JDK install karna zaroori hai. \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\textbf{IDE (Integrated Development Environment):} IntelliJ IDEA, Eclipse, ya VS Code use kar sakte ho. \textcolor{examplecolor}{Spring Boot ke liye IntelliJ IDEA best hai.} \\ % red for examples

% Section 3: Java Syntax Basics
\textbf{\Large 3. Java Syntax Basics} % \Large for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

\textbf{Class:} Java me har cheez ek class me hoti hai. Class ek blueprint hota hai objects banane ka. \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

% Code Snippet: HelloWorld Example
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{HelloWorld.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}
public class HelloWorld {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        System.out.println("Hello, World!");
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:} % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item \texttt{public}: Access modifier, matlab yeh class sabko accessible hai.
    \item \texttt{class}: Keyword jo class define karta hai.
    \item \textcolor{warningcolor}{\texttt{main}: Yehi se program execution shuru hota hai.} % Red for important points
    \item \texttt{System.out.println}: Console pe print karne ke liye.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Variables:} Data store karne ke liye. \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

% Code Snippet: Variables Example
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{Variables.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}
int age = 25; // Integer
String name = "Rahul"; // String
double price = 99.99; // Decimal
boolean isJavaFun = true; // Boolean
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Data Types:} % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item \textbf{Primitive:} \texttt{int}, \texttt{double}, \texttt{boolean}, \texttt{char}, etc.
    \item \textcolor{warningcolor}{\textbf{Non-Primitive:} \texttt{String}, \texttt{Array}, \texttt{Class}, etc.} % Red for important points
\end{itemize}

% Section 4: Object-Oriented Programming (OOP)
\textbf{\Large 4. Object-Oriented Programming (OOP)} % \Large for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

Java OOP principles follow karta hai. Ye principles hain: \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

\textbf{Encapsulation:} Data aur methods ko ek unit me bandhna. \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

% Code Snippet: Encapsulation Example
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{Person.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}
class Person {
    private String name; // Private variable
    public String getName() { // Getter
        return name;
    }
    public void setName(String name) { // Setter
        this.name = name;
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Inheritance:} Ek class dusri class ke properties aur methods inherit kar sakti hai. \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

% Code Snippet: Inheritance Example
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{Animal.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}
class Animal {
    void eat() {
        System.out.println("Eating...");
    }
}
class Dog extends Animal { // Dog inherits Animal
    void bark() {
        System.out.println("Barking...");
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Polymorphism:} Ek hi method ka alag-alag tarike se use karna. \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

\textbf{Method Overloading:} Same method name but different parameters. \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

% Code Snippet: Method Overloading Example
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{MethodOverloading.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}
void add(int a, int b) { System.out.println(a + b); }
void add(double a, double b) { System.out.println(a + b); }
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

% Section 5: Method Overriding
\textbf{\Large 5. Method Overriding} % \Large for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

\textbf{Meaning:} Child class me parent class ke method ko \textbf{redefine} karna. \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\textbf{Use:} Jab child class me parent class ke method ka \textbf{new implementation} chahiye. \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

% Code Snippet: Method Overriding Example
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{Animal.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}
class Animal {
    void sound() { 
        System.out.println("Animal sound"); 
    }
}

class Dog extends Animal {
    @Override
    void sound() { 
        System.out.println("Bark"); 
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:} % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item \texttt{Animal} class ka \texttt{sound()} method "Animal sound" print karta hai.
    \item \textcolor{warningcolor}{\texttt{Dog} class (child class) ne \texttt{sound()} method ko \textbf{override} kiya aur "Bark" print karaya.} % Red for important points
\end{itemize}

\textbf{@Override Annotation:} % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item \textbf{What:} Ye Java me ek \textbf{hint} hai compiler ko batane ke liye ki method override ho raha hai.
    \item \textcolor{warningcolor}{\textbf{Optional:} Use karna zaruri nahi hai, lekin accha practice hai.} % Red for important points
    \item \textbf{Benefit:} Agar method ka naam ya signature galat hai, toh error dega.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Key Points:} % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Method Overriding me \textbf{method name} aur \textbf{signature} same hona chahiye.
    \item \textcolor{warningcolor}{\texttt{@Override} use karna safe hai, lekin mandatory nahi hai.} % Red for important points
    \item Child class ka method parent class ke method ko \textbf{replace} karta hai.
\end{itemize}

===============================

\definecolor{headingcolor}{rgb}{0,0,1} % Blue for headings
\definecolor{examplecolor}{rgb}{0,0.5,0} % red for examples

}

% Begin the document
\begin{document}

% Main Heading
\textbf{\huge Abstraction and Interfaces in Java (Hinglish Me)} % \huge for large font size
\vspace{0.5cm} % Add spacing after the heading
\hrule % Horizontal line to separate sections
\vspace{0.5cm}

% Section 1: Abstraction
\textbf{\Large Abstraction} % \Large for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

\textbf{Meaning:} Complex details ko \textbf{hide} karna aur sirf simple interface provide karna. \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\textcolor{examplecolor}{Example: Car chalane ke liye aapko ye nahi pata ki engine kaise kaam karta hai, bas accelerator dabana hai.} \\ % red for examples

% Section 2: Abstract Class
\textbf{\Large Abstract Class} % \Large for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

1. \textbf{Keyword:} `abstract` \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
2. \textbf{Use:} Jab aap kuch methods ka implementation child class pe chhodna chahte hain. \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
3. \textcolor{warningcolor}{\textbf{Cannot create object:} Abstract class ka object nahi banaya ja sakta.} \\ % Red for important points
4. \textbf{Can have:} \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
   - Abstract methods (without body). \\
   - Concrete methods (with body). \\

% Code Snippet: Abstract Class Example
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{Vehicle.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}
abstract class Vehicle {
    abstract void run(); // Abstract method (no body)
    void stop() { 
        System.out.println("Vehicle stopped"); // Concrete method
    }
}

class Car extends Vehicle {
    void run() { 
        System.out.println("Car is running"); 
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:} % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item \texttt{Vehicle} class ek abstract class hai.
    \item \textcolor{warningcolor}{\texttt{run()} method ka implementation \texttt{Car} class me diya gaya hai.} % Red for important points
    \item \texttt{stop()} method ka implementation already hai, ise directly use kar sakte hain.
\end{itemize}

% Section 3: Interface
\textbf{\Large Interface} % \Large for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

1. \textbf{Keyword:} `interface` \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
2. \textbf{Use:} Jab aap pure abstraction chahate hain (sirf method signature, no implementation). \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
3. \textcolor{warningcolor}{\textbf{Cannot create object:} Interface ka object nahi banaya ja sakta.} \\ % Red for important points
4. \textbf{All methods are abstract:} Java 8 se default methods allow hain (method with body). \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
5. \textbf{Keyword for implementation:} `implements` \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

% Code Snippet: Interface Example
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{Vehicle.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}
interface Vehicle {
    void run(); // Abstract method (no body)
    default void stop() { 
        System.out.println("Vehicle stopped"); // Default method (Java 8+)
    }
}

class Car implements Vehicle {
    public void run() { 
        System.out.println("Car is running"); 
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:} % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item \texttt{Vehicle} interface me \texttt{run()} method ka koi implementation nahi hai.
    \item \textcolor{warningcolor}{\texttt{stop()} method ka implementation already hai (Java 8+ me default methods allow hain).} % Red for important points
    \item \texttt{Car} class ne \texttt{run()} method ko implement kiya hai.
\end{itemize}

% Section 4: Default Keyword in Interface
\textbf{\Large Default Keyword in Interface} % \Large for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

\textbf{Meaning:} Java 8 se interfaces me \textbf{default methods} allow hain. \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\textbf{Use:} Agar aap interface me ek method ka implementation provide karna chahte hain, lekin usko override karne ki zarurat nahi hai. \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

% Code Snippet: Default Method Example
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{Vehicle.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}
interface Vehicle {
    void run(); // Abstract method (no body)
    default void stop() { 
        System.out.println("Vehicle stopped"); // Default method (Java 8+)
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:} % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item \texttt{stop()} method ka implementation already hai, ise override karne ki zarurat nahi hai.
\end{itemize}

% Section 5: Abstract Class vs Interface
\textbf{\Large Abstract Class vs Interface} % \Large for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

\begin{tabular}{|p{6cm}|p{6cm}|}
    \hline
    \textbf{Abstract Class} & \textbf{Interface} \\ \hline
    Can have \textbf{abstract + concrete} methods. & Only \textbf{abstract} methods (Java 8 se default methods allow hain). \\ \hline
    \textcolor{warningcolor}{\textbf{Single inheritance} (1 class extend).} & \textcolor{warningcolor}{\textbf{Multiple inheritance} (1 class multiple interfaces implement kar sakti hai).} \\ \hline
    `extends` keyword use hota hai. & `implements` keyword use hota hai. \\ \hline
\end{tabular}

% Section 6: Key Points
\textbf{\Large Key Points} % \Large for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item \textbf{Abstract Class:} Partial abstraction, `extends` keyword, object nahi ban sakta.
    \item \textbf{Interface:} Full abstraction, `implements` keyword, object nahi ban sakta.
    \begin{itemize}
    \item \begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]
    \item \textcolor{warningcolor}{\textbf{Static Method:} Object banaye bina call kar sakte hain.}
     \end{tcolorbox}
    % Red for important points
    \item \textcolor{warningcolor}{\textbf{Abstract Method:} Must be overridden in child class.} % Red for important points
\end{itemize}

% Section 7: Example in Short
\textbf{\Large Example in Short} % \Large for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

% Code Snippet: Abstract Class Example
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{Vehicle.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}
abstract class Vehicle {
    abstract void run(); // No body
    void stop() { 
        System.out.println("Vehicle stopped"); 
    }
}
class Car extends Vehicle {
    void run() { 
        System.out.println("Car is running"); 
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

% Code Snippet: Interface Example
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{Vehicle.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}
interface Vehicle {
    void run(); // No body
    default void stop() { 
        System.out.println("Vehicle stopped"); 
    }
}
class Car implements Vehicle {
    public void run() { 
        System.out.println("Car is running"); 
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\definecolor{blueHead}{RGB}{0,102,204}
\definecolor{redEx}{RGB}{0,153,76}
\definecolor{redWarn}{RGB}{204,0,0}
\definecolor{lightBlue}{RGB}{173,216,230}
\definecolor{lightred}{RGB}{144,238,144}
\definecolor{yellowHeader}{RGB}{255,204,0}

% Java code styling
\lstdefinestyle{javaStyle}{
  language=Java,
  basicstyle=\ttfamily\footnotesize,
  keywordstyle=\bfseries\color{blueHead},
  commentstyle=\itshape\color{gray},
  stringstyle=\color{redWarn},

  numberstyle=\tiny\color{gray},
  stepnumber=1,

  backgroundcolor=\color{lightBlue},
  frame=single
}

% Custom example box
\newtcolorbox{examplebox}{colback=lightred!10!white,colframe=redEx,title=\textbf{Example}}

% Title Page
\title{\textbf{\textcolor{blueHead}{Abstraction in Web Development (Real-Time Example in Hindi)}}}
\author{}
\date{}

\begin{document}

\maketitle

\section*{\textcolor{blueHead}{Abstraction kya hota hai?}}
Abstraction ka matlab hota hai \textbf{complexity ko hide karna aur sirf zaroori details dikhana}.
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{Car ka example:} Aap car chalate ho to sirf steering, accelerator aur brake ka use karte ho.
    \item Aapko ye nahi pata hota ki engine andar kaise kaam kar raha hai.
    \item Car manufacturer ne complexity hide kar di hai aur ek simple interface diya hai.
\end{itemize}

\section*{\textcolor{blueHead}{Real-Time Example: E-Commerce Website}}
Maan lo \textbf{Amazon ka ek product listing page} hai jo user ko products dikhata hai.
\begin{itemize}
    \item User sirf \texttt{/products} API call karta hai aur sirf products ka data dekhta hai.
    \item \textbf{Lekin usko ye nahi pata chalega ki:}
    \begin{itemize}
        \item Data kaha se aa raha hai?
        \item Database kaunsa use ho raha hai?
        \item Backend ka structure kaisa hai?
    \end{itemize}
\end{itemize}

\begin{examplebox}
\textbf{Yahi abstraction hai!} User sirf API call karta hai aur response leta hai bina backend ki complexity samjhe.
\end{examplebox}

\section*{\textcolor{blueHead}{Spring Boot me Abstraction ka Use}}
\subsection*{Step 1: Abstract Class (Service Layer)}
\textbf{ProductService.java (Abstract Class)}
\begin{lstlisting}[style=javaStyle]
abstract class ProductService {
    abstract List<String> getAllProducts();
    void logRequest() {
        System.out.println("Request logged for product API");
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{Step 2: Implementation Class (Product Service)}
\begin{lstlisting}[style=javaStyle]
class ProductServiceImpl extends ProductService {
    @Override
    List<String> getAllProducts() {
        logRequest();
        return Arrays.asList("Laptop", "Mobile", "Headphones");
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{Step 3: API Controller (User Ko Response Dikhana)}
\begin{lstlisting}[style=javaStyle]
@RestController
@RequestMapping("/products")
class ProductController {
    private final ProductService productService = new ProductServiceImpl();

    @GetMapping
    public List<String> getProducts() {
        return productService.getAllProducts();
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\section*{\textcolor{blueHead}{Final Output}}
Agar user \textbf{browser ya Postman} me API call karega:
\begin{verbatim}
GET http://localhost:8080/products

Response:
["Laptop", "Mobile", "Headphones"]
\end{verbatim}

\section*{\textcolor{blueHead}{Interface ka Real Use in Web Development}}
\subsection*{Step 4: Interface for Database (Product Repository)}
\begin{lstlisting}[style=javaStyle]
interface ProductRepository extends JpaRepository<Product, Integer> {
    // Spring Boot khud implementation handle karega (Abstraction)
}
\end{lstlisting}

\section*{\textcolor{blueHead}{Conclusion}}
\begin{tabular}{|p{4cm}|p{4cm}|p{4cm}|}
\hline
\rowcolor{lightBlue}
\textbf{Layer} & \textbf{Role} & \textbf{Abstraction ka Use} \\
\hline
\textbf{Service Layer} & Business logic handle karta hai & Abstract class se reusability badhti hai \\
\rowcolor{lightred}
\textbf{Controller Layer} & User ke request ko process karta hai & User ko backend ki complexity nahi dikhai jati \\
\hline
\end{tabular}

\section*{\textcolor{blueHead}{Summary (Key Learnings)}}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{Abstract Class} - Common logic reuse karne ke liye.
    \item \textbf{Interface} - Backend complexity hide karne ke liye.
    \item \textbf{Spring Boot} me abstraction ka use \textbf{Service Layer \& Repository Layer} me hota hai.
    \item \textbf{User ko sirf API ka response milta hai bina backend ki complexity samjhe.}
\end{itemize}


===============================

% Begin the document
\begin{document}

% Main Heading
\textcolor{headingcolor}{\textbf{\huge Java Collections Framework and More (Hinglish Me)}} % Blue for main heading
\vspace{0.5cm} % Add spacing after the heading
\hrule % Horizontal line to separate sections
\vspace{0.5cm}

% Section 1: Collections Framework
\textcolor{subheadingcolor}{\textbf{\Large Collections Framework}} % Light blue for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

\textbf{Meaning:} Java me data structures (jaise list, set, map) ko handle karne ke liye ek framework hai. \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\textbf{Use:} Data ko store, retrieve, aur manipulate karne ke liye. \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

% Section 2: List
\textcolor{subheadingcolor}{\textbf{\Large 1. List}} % Light blue for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

\textbf{Meaning:} Ordered collection of elements. \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\textbf{Properties:} \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Elements can be \textbf{duplicate}.
    \item Elements are stored in \textbf{sequence} (order).
\end{itemize}
\textbf{Common Implementations:} \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item \texttt{ArrayList}: Dynamic array (fast access, slow insertion/deletion).
    \item \texttt{LinkedList}: Doubly linked list (fast insertion/deletion, slow access).
\end{itemize}

% Code Snippet: List Example
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{Main.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}
import java.util.ArrayList;
import java.util.List;

public class Main {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        List<String> names = new ArrayList<>(); // List banaya
        names.add("Rahul"); // Element add kiya
        names.add("Amit");  // Element add kiya
        System.out.println(names); // Output: [Rahul, Amit]
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:} % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item \texttt{names.add()} se elements add hote hain.
    \item \textcolor{warningcolor}{\texttt{System.out.println(names)} se pure list print hota hai.} % Red for important points
\end{itemize}

% Section 3: Set
\textcolor{subheadingcolor}{\textbf{\Large 2. Set}} % Light blue for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

\textbf{Meaning:} Collection of \textbf{unique} elements. \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\textbf{Properties:} \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Elements cannot be \textbf{duplicate}.
    \item No specific order (unordered collection).
\end{itemize}
\textbf{Common Implementations:} \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item \texttt{HashSet}: Uses hashing for fast access.
    \item \texttt{TreeSet}: Stores elements in sorted order.
\end{itemize}

% Code Snippet: Set Example
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{Main.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}
import java.util.HashSet;
import java.util.Set;

public class Main {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        Set<Integer> numbers = new HashSet<>(); // Set banaya
        numbers.add(1); // Element add kiya
        numbers.add(2); // Element add kiya
        numbers.add(1); // Duplicate element (add nahi hoga)
        System.out.println(numbers); // Output: [1, 2]
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:} % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item \texttt{numbers.add(1)} do baar call kiya, lekin \texttt{Set} me duplicate allow nahi hai.
    \item \textcolor{warningcolor}{\texttt{System.out.println(numbers)} se unique elements print hote hain.} % Red for important points
\end{itemize}

% Section 4: Map
\textcolor{subheadingcolor}{\textbf{\Large 3. Map}} % Light blue for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

\textbf{Meaning:} Collection of \textbf{key-value pairs}. \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\textbf{Properties:} \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Keys are \textbf{unique}.
    \item Values can be duplicate.
\end{itemize}
\textbf{Common Implementations:} \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item \texttt{HashMap}: Uses hashing for fast access.
    \item \texttt{TreeMap}: Stores keys in sorted order.
\end{itemize}

% Code Snippet: Map Example
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{Main.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}
import java.util.HashMap;
import java.util.Map;

public class Main {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        Map<String, Integer> map = new HashMap<>(); // Map banaya
        map.put("Rahul", 25); // Key-Value pair add kiya
        map.put("Amit", 30);  // Key-Value pair add kiya
        System.out.println(map); // Output: {Rahul=25, Amit=30}
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:} % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item \texttt{map.put("Rahul", 25)} se key-value pair add hota hai.
    \item \textcolor{warningcolor}{\texttt{System.out.println(map)} se pure map print hota hai.} % Red for important points
\end{itemize}

% Section 5: Key Differences
\textcolor{subheadingcolor}{\textbf{\Large Key Differences}} % Light blue for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

\begin{tabular}{|p{4cm}|p{4cm}|p{4cm}|}
    \hline
    \textbf{Feature} & \textbf{List} & \textbf{Set} & \textbf{Map} \\ \hline
    \textbf{Order} & Ordered (sequence) & Unordered (no sequence) & Unordered (no sequence) \\ \hline
    \textbf{Duplicates} & Allowed & Not allowed & Keys: Not allowed, Values: Allowed \\ \hline
    \textbf{Example} & \texttt{ArrayList}, \texttt{LinkedList} & \texttt{HashSet}, \texttt{TreeSet} & \texttt{HashMap}, \texttt{TreeMap} \\ \hline
\end{tabular}

% Section 6: Common Methods
\textcolor{subheadingcolor}{\textbf{\Large Common Methods}} % Light blue for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item \textbf{List:} \\
          - \texttt{add(element)}: Element add karna. \\
          - \texttt{get(index)}: Element access karna. \\
          - \texttt{remove(index)}: Element remove karna.
    \item \textbf{Set:} \\
          - \texttt{add(element)}: Element add karna. \\
          - \texttt{contains(element)}: Check karna ki element hai ya nahi. \\
          - \texttt{remove(element)}: Element remove karna.
    \item \textbf{Map:} \\
          - \texttt{put(key, value)}: Key-value pair add karna. \\
          - \texttt{get(key)}: Value access karna. \\
          - \texttt{remove(key)}: Key-value pair remove karna.
\end{itemize}

% Section 7: Example in Short
\textcolor{subheadingcolor}{\textbf{\Large Example in Short}} % Light blue for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

% Code Snippet: List Example
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{Main.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}
List<String> names = new ArrayList<>();
names.add("Rahul");
names.add("Amit");
System.out.println(names); // Output: [Rahul, Amit]
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

% Code Snippet: Set Example
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{Main.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}
Set<Integer> numbers = new HashSet<>();
numbers.add(1);
numbers.add(2);
numbers.add(1); // Duplicate (add nahi hoga)
System.out.println(numbers); // Output: [1, 2]
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

% Code Snippet: Map Example
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{Main.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}
Map<String, Integer> map = new HashMap<>();
map.put("Rahul", 25);
map.put("Amit", 30);
System.out.println(map); // Output: {Rahul=25, Amit=30}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

% Section 8: Key Points
\textcolor{subheadingcolor}{\textbf{\Large Key Points}} % Light blue for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item \textbf{List:} Ordered, duplicates allowed.
    \item \textbf{Set:} Unordered, no duplicates.
    \item \textbf{Map:} Key-value pairs, keys unique.
\end{itemize}

% Section 9: Exception Handling
\textcolor{subheadingcolor}{\textbf{\Large 6. Exception Handling}} % Light blue for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

Errors ko handle karne ke liye \texttt{try-catch} block use karte hain. \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

% Code Snippet: Exception Handling Example
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{Main.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}
try {
    int result = 10 / 0; // ArithmeticException
} catch (ArithmeticException e) {
    System.out.println("Cannot divide by zero");
} finally {
    System.out.println("This will always execute");
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:} % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item \texttt{try} block me error-prone code likha jata hai.
    \item \texttt{catch} block me error handle kiya jata hai.
    \item \textcolor{warningcolor}{\texttt{finally} block hamesha execute hota hai, chahe exception ho ya nahi.} % Red for important points
\end{itemize}

% Section 10: Keywords in Java
\textcolor{subheadingcolor}{\textbf{\Large 7. Keywords in Java}} % Light blue for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

\begin{itemize}
    \item \begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]
\textbf{static:} \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\texttt{static} keyword ka matlab hai ki wo method ya variable class ka part hai, object ka nahi. \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

 \end{tcolorbox}

% Code Snippet: static Example
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{Example.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}
class Example {
    static int count = 0; // Static variable
    static void print() { // Static method
        System.out.println("Hello");
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:} % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item \texttt{count} aur \texttt{print} ko object banaye bina use kar sakte hain: \texttt{Example.count} ya \texttt{Example.print()}.
\end{itemize}

\begin{itemize}
    \item \begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]

\textbf{final:} \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\texttt{final} keyword ka matlab hai ki uski value change nahi ki ja sakti. \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

 \end{tcolorbox}

% Code Snippet: final Example
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{Example.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}
final int age = 25; // Ab age ki value change nahi kar sakte
final class Animal { // Ab Animal class ko inherit nahi kar sakte
    // Class content
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{this:} \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\texttt{this} keyword current object ko refer karta hai. \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

% Code Snippet: this Example
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{Person.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}
class Person {
    String name;
    Person(String name) {
        this.name = name; // Current object ka name set karo
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}
    \item \begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]

% Section 11: Constructor
\textcolor{subheadingcolor}{\textbf{\Large 8. Constructor}} % Light blue for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

Constructor ek special method hai jo object banate waqt automatically call hota hai. \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
Iska use object ki initial state set karne ke liye hota hai. \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
Constructor ka naam class ke naam jaisa hi hota hai, aur yeh kuch return nahi karta. \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

% Code Snippet: Constructor Example

\begin{lstlisting}
class Car {
    String name;
    // Constructor
    Car(String name) {
        this.name = name;
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Types of Constructors:} \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item \textbf{Default Constructor:} Agar tum koi constructor nahi banate, toh Java apne aap ek default constructor banata hai.
    \item \textbf{Parameterized Constructor:} Jo parameters leta hai.
    \item \textbf{Constructor Overloading:} Ek se zyada constructors hona.
\end{itemize}

% Code Snippet: Constructor Overloading Example
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{Car.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}
class Car {
    String name;
    int speed;
    Car() { // Default constructor
        this.name = "Unknown";
    }
    Car(String name) { // Parameterized constructor
        this.name = name;
    }
    Car(String name, int speed) { // Another parameterized constructor
        this.name = name;
        this.speed = speed;
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

% Section 12: Methods in Java
\textcolor{subheadingcolor}{\textbf{\Large 9. Methods in Java}} % Light blue for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

Methods functions hote hain jo class ke andar define hote hain. \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

% Code Snippet: Method Example
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{Calculator.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}
class Calculator {
    int add(int a, int b) {
        return a + b;
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Method Overloading:} \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
Ek se zyada methods ka naam same hona, lekin parameters alag hona. \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

% Code Snippet: Method Overloading Example
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{Calculator.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}
class Calculator {
    int add(int a, int b) {
        return a + b;
    }
    double add(double a, double b) {
        return a + b;
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

% Section 13: Access Modifiers
\textcolor{subheadingcolor}{\textbf{\Large 10. Access Modifiers}} % Light blue for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

Ye batate hain ki kaun class, method, ya variable ko access kar sakta hai. \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

% Code Snippet: Access Modifiers Example
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{Example.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}
class Example {
    public int publicVar = 1;
    private int privateVar = 2;
    protected int protectedVar = 3;
    int defaultVar = 4; // Default
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:} % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{itemize}
    \item \begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]
    \item \texttt{public}: Sabko accessible.
    \item \texttt{private}: Sirf class ke andar accessible.
    \item \texttt{protected}: Same package aur child classes ke liye accessible.
    \item \texttt{default}: Sirf same package me accessible.
     \end{tcolorbox}
\end{itemize}

% Section 14: Inheritance
\textcolor{subheadingcolor}{\textbf{\Large 11. Inheritance}} % Light blue for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

Inheritance ka matlab hai ki ek class dusri class ke properties aur methods ko inherit kar sakti hai. \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\texttt{extends} keyword ka use hota hai. \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

% Code Snippet: Inheritance Example
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{Animal.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}
class Animal {
    void eat() {
        System.out.println("Eating...");
    }
}
class Dog extends Animal { // Dog inherits Animal
    void bark() {
        System.out.println("Barking...");
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

% Section 15: Polymorphism
\textcolor{subheadingcolor}{\textbf{\Large 12. Polymorphism}} % Light blue for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

Polymorphism ka matlab hai "ek se zyada forms". \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

\textbf{Method Overloading:} Same method name, different parameters. \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

% Code Snippet: Method Overloading Example
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{Example.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}
void add(int a, int b) { System.out.println(a + b); }
void add(double a, double b) { System.out.println(a + b); }
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Method Overriding:} Child class me parent class ke method ko redefine karna. \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

% Code Snippet: Method Overriding Example
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{Animal.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}
class Animal {
    void sound() { System.out.println("Animal sound"); }
}
class Dog extends Animal {
    @Override
    void sound() { System.out.println("Bark"); }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

===============================

\title{\color{headingblue}\textbf{Spring Boot Project from Scratch (Step-by-Step) in Hinglish (For Beginners)}}
\author{Your Name}

\begin{document}

\maketitle

% Introduction
\section{Introduction}
This guide provides a step-by-step tutorial for creating a Spring Boot project from scratch. It is designed to be beginner-friendly and includes Hinglish explanations for better understanding.

\textbf{Hinglish Explanation:} Yeh guide Spring Boot project banane ka step-by-step tarika batata hai. Isme folder structure, database setup, CRUD operations, aur IntelliJ IDEA me project setup kaise karna hai, sab kuch cover kiya gaya hai.

% Step 1: Install Java aur IntelliJ IDEA
\section{Step 1: Install Java aur IntelliJ IDEA}
\subsection{Install Java JDK (Java Development Kit)}
Spring Boot project run karne ke liye Java install hona zaroori hai.

\textbf{Download Java JDK:} \href{https://www.oracle.com/java/technologies/javase-jdk17-downloads.html}{Oracle Java JDK Download}  
Install hone ke baad check karne ke liye command run karo:  
\begin{lstlisting}[language=bash]
java -version
\end{lstlisting}

% Step 2: Create New Spring Boot Project
\section{Step 2: Create New Spring Boot Project}
\subsection{IntelliJ IDEA me Project Create Karo}
Agar IntelliJ IDEA me Spring Initializr ka option nahi hai, toh manually Spring Boot project download karo.

\textbf{Spring Initializr Website:} \href{https://start.spring.io/}{Spring Initializr}  
Ye details fill karo:
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{Project:} Maven
    \item \textbf{Language:} Java
    \item \textbf{Spring Boot Version:} Latest Stable Version
    \item \textbf{Packaging:} Jar
    \item \textbf{Java Version:} 17
     % Add this package at the beginning

% Define a colored box style
\tcbset{
    myboxstyle/.style={
        colback=blue!10, % Light blue background
        colframe=blue!60, % Darker blue border
        fonttitle=\bfseries, % Bold title
        coltitle=white, % White title text
        boxrule=1mm, % Border thickness
        arc=4mm, % Rounded corners
        width=\textwidth, % Full width
        enhanced
    }
}

% Inside the document
\begin{tcolorbox}[title={\textbf{click on ADD Required Dependencies}}, myboxstyle]
    \begin{itemize}
        \item \textbf{Spring Web} → REST API banane ke liye
        \item \textbf{Spring Boot DevTools} → Auto Restart ke liye
        \item \textbf{Spring Data JPA} → Database ke liye
        \item \textbf{MySQL Driver} → MySQL Database ke liye
        \item \textbf{Lombok} → Code short aur clean banane ke liye
    \end{itemize}
\end{tcolorbox}

% Step 3: Project Structure Samjho
\section{Step 3: Project Structure Samjho}
\begin{lstlisting}
SpringBootApp/
│── src/
│   ├── main/
│   │   ├── java/com/example/springbootapp/
│   │   │   ├── controller/      <-- (Express.js ke routes jaise)
│   │   │   ├── service/         <-- (Business logic ka layer)
│   │   │   ├── repository/      <-- (Database operations, like Mongoose)
│   │   │   ├── entity/          <-- (Database Models, like Mongoose Schema)
│   │   │   ├── dto/             <-- (Data Transfer Objects)
│   │   │   ├── config/          <-- (Configurations, like middleware)
│   │   │   ├── SpringBootApp.java  <-- (Main server file, like app.js)
│   │   ├── resources/
│   │   │   ├── application.properties  <-- (Database config)
│── pom.xml   <-- (Dependencies list, like package.json)
\end{lstlisting}

\begin{document}

\title{\textbf{\color{headingcolor}Step-by-Step Guide to Creating a Spring Boot Folder Structure in IntelliJ IDEA}}

\maketitle

\section*{Introduction}
This document explains how to create a well-structured Spring Boot project in IntelliJ IDEA with all necessary folders and files.

\section*{Step-by-Step Guide}




\subsection*{\textbf{Creating the Folder Structure Manually}}
If some folders are missing, follow these steps:

\begin{enumerate}
    \item Go to \textbf{src/main/java/com/yourcompany/yourproject} in IntelliJ IDEA.
    \item Right-click on \textbf{yourproject} → \textbf{New → Package}.
    \item Name the packages:
          \begin{itemize}
              \item \textbf{controller}
              \item \textbf{service}
              \item \textbf{repository}
              \item \textbf{model}
          \end{itemize}
    \item Inside each package, create the following files:
          \begin{itemize}
              \item \textbf{controller}: \textcolor{warningcolor}{YourController.java}
              \item \textbf{service}: \textcolor{warningcolor}{YourService.java}
              \item \textbf{repository}: \textcolor{warningcolor}{YourRepository.java}
              \item \textbf{model}: \textcolor{warningcolor}{YourEntity.java}
          \end{itemize}
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{\textbf{4. Purpose of Each Folder}}
\textbf{Controller (controller/)} - Handles HTTP requests:
\begin{lstlisting}
@RestController
@RequestMapping("/api")
public class YourController {
    @GetMapping("/hello")
    public String sayHello() {
        return "Hello, Spring Boot!";
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{Service (service/)} - Contains business logic:
\begin{lstlisting}
@Service
public class YourService {
    public String processData() {
        return "Processed Data";
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{Repository (repository/)} - Interfaces with the database:
\begin{lstlisting}
@Repository
public interface YourRepository extends JpaRepository<YourEntity, Long> {
}
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{Model (model/)} - Represents the database table:
\begin{lstlisting}
@Entity
@Table(name = "your_table")
public class YourEntity {
    @Id
    @GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY)
    private Long id;
    private String name;
}
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{\textbf{5. Running the Spring Boot Application}}
- Open \textbf{YourApplication.java} and click the red \textbf{Run} button in IntelliJ.

\section*{✅ Summary}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textcolor{warningcolor}{Follow the standard package structure.}
    \item \textcolor{warningcolor}{Use @Controller, @Service, @Repository, @Entity annotations.}
    \item \textcolor{warningcolor}{Run the application from YourApplication.java.}
    \item \textcolor{warningcolor}{Test REST API using Postman or browser: http://localhost:8080/api/hello.}
\end{itemize}






% Step 4: Configure Database (MySQL)
\section{Step 4: Configure Database (MySQL)}
\textbf{Database Configuration}  
\textbf{Location:} \texttt{src/main/resources/application.properties}  
\begin{lstlisting}
server.port=8080
spring.datasource.url=jdbc:mysql://localhost:3306/springboot_db
spring.datasource.username=root
spring.datasource.password=your_password

spring.jpa.hibernate.ddl-auto=update
spring.jpa.show-sql=true
spring.jpa.database-platform=org.hibernate.dialect.MySQL8Dialect
\end{lstlisting}

% Step 5: Run Server in IntelliJ
\section{Step 5: Run Server in IntelliJ}
1. \textbf{\texttt{SpringBootApp.java} file open karo}  
2. \textbf{Right Click → Run}  
3. Console me \texttt{"Tomcat started on port(s): 8080"} likha aayega.

\textbf{Test API using Postman}  
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{GET Users} → \texttt{http://localhost:8080/users}
    \item \textbf{POST User} → \texttt{http://localhost:8080/users}
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Example JSON Request:}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=json]
{
  "name": "John Doe",
  "email": "john@example.com"
}
\end{lstlisting}





\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item \textbf{JDK Install} karo.
    \item \textbf{IDE Install} karo (IntelliJ IDEA ya Eclipse).
    \item \textbf{Spring Boot Project} banayo (Spring Initializr se).
    \item \textbf{Controller} banayo aur `@GetMapping` se API banayo.
    \item \textbf{Run} karo aur API test karo.
\end{itemize}

\usepackage{xcolor}
\usepackage{listings}
\usepackage{tcolorbox}
\usepackage{hyperref}

% Custom Colors
\definecolor{codegray}{gray}{0.9}
\definecolor{keywordcolor}{RGB}{255,69,0}
\definecolor{commentcolor}{RGB}{0,128,0}
\definecolor{stringcolor}{RGB}{0,0,255}
\definecolor{bgcolor}{rgb}{0.95,0.95,0.95}

% Code Block Settings
\lstdefinestyle{mystyle}{
    backgroundcolor=\color{codegray},
    commentstyle=\color{commentcolor},
    keywordstyle=\color{keywordcolor},
    stringstyle=\color{stringcolor},
    basicstyle=\ttfamily\footnotesize,
    breaklines=true,
    frame=single,
    showstringspaces=false
}
\lstset{style=mystyle}

\begin{document}

\section{\textbf{\textcolor{red}{\faRocket \ Spring Boot ko MySQL Workbench se Connect Karna}}}

Agar tum \textbf{Spring Boot application ko MySQL database (MySQL Workbench) se connect} karna chahte ho, toh \texttt{application.properties} file me \textbf{database configuration} set karna hoga.  

\subsection{\textbf{\textcolor{blue}{Configuration File Location:}}}
Ye file \textbf{Spring Boot project ke andar hoti hai}:  
\texttt{src/main/resources/application.properties}  

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=bgcolor,title=\textbf{Note}]
\textbf{Yeh file Express.js ke \texttt{config/database.js} jaisi hoti hai}, jisme \textbf{database ka URL, username, password, aur configurations hoti hain}.
\end{tcolorbox}

\section{\textbf{\textcolor{orange}{Step-by-Step Database Connection Setup}}}

\subsection{Step 1: MySQL Workbench Me Database Create Karo}
Sabse pehle \textbf{MySQL Workbench open karo} aur ek \textbf{naya database (schema) create karo}:  
\begin{enumerate}
    \item Workbench Open Karo
    \item SQL Editor me jao
    \item Query likho aur run karo:
    \begin{lstlisting}[language=SQL]
    CREATE DATABASE springboot_db;
    \end{lstlisting}
    \item Refresh karo aur ensure karo ki \texttt{springboot_db} create ho gaya hai.
\end{enumerate}

\begin{itemize}
    \item \begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]

\subsection{Step 2: Spring Boot Ke \texttt{application.properties} Me Database Configure Karo}
Ab \textbf{Spring Boot ko batana padega ki kis database se connect hona hai}.  
\textbf{Open karo:}  
\texttt{src/main/resources/application.properties}  
Aur ye configuration likho:

\begin{lstlisting}[language=properties]
# Spring Boot server ka port set karo
server.port=8080

# MySQL Database ka connection URL set karo
spring.datasource.url=jdbc:mysql://localhost:3306/springboot_db

# MySQL ka username aur password set karo
spring.datasource.username=root
spring.datasource.password=your_password

# Hibernate (ORM) ka setup karo
spring.jpa.hibernate.ddl-auto=update

# Console me SQL queries dikhane ke liye
spring.jpa.show-sql=true

# MySQL 8 dialect set karo
tspring.jpa.database-platform=org.hibernate.dialect.MySQL8Dialect
\end{lstlisting}


 
        \item \textbf{\texttt{server.port=8080}} - Spring Boot ka server kis port pe chalega.
        \item \textbf{\texttt{spring.datasource.url}} - Database connection URL.
        \item \textbf{\texttt{spring.datasource.username=root} \& \texttt{spring.datasource.password}} - MySQL ka login credentials.
        \item \textbf{\texttt{spring.jpa.hibernate.ddl-auto=update}} - Hibernate ORM ka setup.
        \item \textbf{\texttt{spring.jpa.show-sql=true}} - Console me SQL queries dikhane ke liye.
        \item \textbf{\texttt{spring.jpa.database-platform=org.hibernate.dialect.MySQL8Dialect}} - MySQL 8 ke liye dialect.
        \end{tcolorbox}
    \end{itemize}



\section{\textbf{Step 3: Server Run Karo aur Check Karo Ki Database Connect Ho Raha Hai}}
\begin{enumerate}
    \item IntelliJ IDEA ya VS Code me project open karo.
    \item \texttt{SpringBootApp.java} file me jao (jo \texttt{main} class hai).
    \item Run button click karo ya ye command run karo:
    \begin{lstlisting}[language=bash]
    mvn spring-boot:run
    \end{lstlisting}
    \item Agar sab sahi hai toh console me yeh message aayega:
    \begin{lstlisting}
    Tomcat started on port(s): 8080
    \end{lstlisting}
\end{enumerate}

\section{\textbf{\textcolor{purple}{Bonus: Check Connection Using Postman}}}
Agar tumne \textbf{CRUD API banayi hai} toh check karne ke liye \textbf{Postman use kar sakte ho}:  
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{GET Users:} \texttt{http://localhost:8080/users}
    \item \textbf{POST User:} \texttt{http://localhost:8080/users}
\end{itemize}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=json]
{
  "name": "John Doe",
  "email": "john@example.com"
}
\end{lstlisting}

\section{\textbf{�� Conclusion}}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{Step 1:} MySQL Workbench me \textbf{database create karo}.
    \item \textbf{Step 2:} \texttt{application.properties} me \textbf{database URL, username, aur password set karo}.
    \item \textbf{Step 3:} \textbf{Spring Boot server run karo aur ensure karo ki MySQL connect ho raha hai}.
    \item \textbf{Step 4:} \textbf{Postman ya log messages check karo connection verify karne ke liye}.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{�� Ab tumhara Spring Boot application MySQL Workbench se successfully connect ho gaya! ��}















% Section 4: Express.js vs Spring Boot Comparison
\textcolor{subheadingcolor}{\textbf{\Large Express.js vs Spring Boot Comparison}} % Light blue for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

\begin{tabular}{|p{5cm}|p{5cm}|p{5cm}|}
    \hline
    \textbf{Feature} & \textbf{Express.js} & \textbf{Spring Boot} \\ \hline
    \textbf{Language} & JavaScript & Java \\ \hline
    \textbf{Framework} & Lightweight & Enterprise-level \\ \hline
    \textbf{Routes} & `app.get()`, `app.post()` & `@GetMapping`, `@PostMapping` \\ \hline
    \textbf{Server Start} & `node app.js` & `DemoApplication.java` run karo \\ \hline
    \textbf{Port} & Default: 3000 & Default: 8080 \\ \hline
\end{tabular}

% Section 5: Example Code
\textcolor{subheadingcolor}{\textbf{\Large Example Code}} % Light blue for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

% Code Snippet: HelloController.java
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{HelloController.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
package com.example.demo;

import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.GetMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RestController;

@RestController
public class HelloController {

    @GetMapping("/hello")
    public String sayHello() {
        return "Hello, Spring Boot!";
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

% Code Snippet: DemoApplication.java
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{DemoApplication.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
package com.example.demo;

import org.springframework.boot.SpringApplication;
import org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.SpringBootApplication;

@SpringBootApplication
public class DemoApplication {

    public static void main(String[] args) {
        SpringApplication.run(DemoApplication.class, args);
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\section{Maven Kya Hai? (NPM ki tarah kaam karta hai?)}
Maven ek build automation tool hai jo Java projects ke liye use hota hai. Yeh NPM (Node Package Manager) ke jaise kaam karta hai lekin Java ecosystem ke liye hota hai. NPM Node.js ke dependencies aur scripts ko manage karta hai, jabki Maven Java projects me dependencies, project structure, aur build process ko automate karta hai.

\subsection{Maven Ke Fayde}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{Dependency Management}: Jaise NPM me \texttt{package.json} hota hai, waise hi Maven me \texttt{pom.xml} hota hai jisme dependencies define hoti hain.
    \item \textbf{Project Structure Standardization}: Java projects ka structure organize aur standardized rehta hai.
    \item \textbf{Build \& Deployment Automation}: Code compile karna, test cases run karna, aur project ka .jar ya .war file generate karna easy hota hai.
    \item \textbf{Plugin Support}: Alag-alag plugins ka use karke testing, packaging, aur deployment automate kiya ja sakta hai.
\end{itemize}

\subsection{Example (Maven vs NPM)}
\begin{longtable}
    \hline
    \textbf{Feature} & \textbf{NPM (Node.js)} & \textbf{Maven (Java)} \\
    \hline
    Dependency File & \texttt{package.json} & \texttt{pom.xml} \\
    \hline
    Install Dependencies & \texttt{npm install} & \texttt{mvn install} \\
    \hline
    Run Project & \texttt{npm start} & \texttt{mvn spring-boot:run} \\
    \hline
    Build Project & \texttt{npm run build} & \texttt{mvn package} \\
    \hline
\end{longtable}

\section{Maven Install Karna Aur Environment Variable Set Karna}

\subsection{Step 1: Download Maven}
Official Website: \url{https://maven.apache.org/download.cgi}

.zip ya .tar.gz file download karo aur extract karo.

\subsection{Step 2: Environment Variable Set Karo (Windows ke liye)}
Extracted Folder ka Path Copy Karo

\textbf{Example:} \texttt{C:\textbackslash apache-maven-3.8.6\textbackslash bin}

Environment Variable Me Add Karo:
\begin{itemize}
    \item Windows Search \rightarrow "Environment Variables" search karo
    \item System Properties \rightarrow Advanced \rightarrow Environment Variables
    \item System Variables section me Path select karo \rightarrow Edit \rightarrow New \rightarrow \texttt{C:\textbackslash apache-maven-3.8.6\textbackslash bin} paste karo \rightarrow OK.
\end{itemize}

\subsection{Check Installation}
CMD open karo aur run karo:
\begin{lstlisting}[language=bash]
mvn -version
\end{lstlisting}
Agar Apache Maven 3.x.x show ho raha hai, toh setup sahi hai.

\subsection{Linux/Mac Ke Liye}
Terminal Open Karo:
\begin{lstlisting}[language=bash]
sudo apt install maven  # (Ubuntu)
brew install maven  # (Mac)
\end{lstlisting}
Check Version:
\begin{lstlisting}[language=bash]
mvn -version
\end{lstlisting}

\section{Spring Boot Java 17 Pe Kyun Chal Raha Hai, Java 23 Pe Nahi?}
Spring Boot projects ke liye Java ka supported version important hota hai. Spring Boot ka latest stable version Java 17 LTS (Long-Term Support) ko officially support karta hai, lekin Java 23 ek non-LTS version hai jo backward compatibility issues create kar sakta hai.

\subsection{Java 17 vs Java 23 in Spring Boot}
\begin{longtable}
    \hline
    \textbf{Feature} & \textbf{Java 17 (LTS)} & \textbf{Java 23 (Non-LTS)} \\
    \hline
    Stability & Stable \& widely used & Frequent updates, no long-term support \\
    \hline
    Spring Boot Compatibility & Officially supported & Not officially supported \\
    \hline
    Backward Compatibility & Ensured & Breaking changes expected \\
    \hline
\end{longtable}

\subsection{Kaise Check Kare Ki Kaunsi Java Version Use Ho Rahi Hai?}
\textbf{Command Line Check Karo:}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=bash]
java -version
\end{lstlisting}
Agar \texttt{java 17.x.x} show ho raha hai, toh aap Java 17 use kar rahe ho.

\subsection{Spring Boot Configuration Me Java Version Set Karo}
Maven Project (\texttt{pom.xml}) me ensure karo ki yeh lines included ho:
\begin{lstlisting}[language=xml]
<properties>
    <java.version>17</java.version>
</properties>
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection{Agar aap Java 23 use karna chahte ho, toh aapko manually dependencies aur compatibility issues fix karne padenge.}

\title{\textbf{Spring Boot Me Debugging (Django ke breakpoint() jaise)}}
\author{}
\date{}
\maketitle

\section*{Breakpoint Kya Hai?}
Breakpoint ek aisa point hota hai jahan aapka code execution ruk jata hai aur aap uss point pe variables, expressions, aur program flow ko inspect kar sakte ho. Breakpoint set karne ke baad, aap code ko step-by-step execute kar sakte ho aur dekhte ho ki kya ho raha hai.

\section*{Breakpoint Set Karne Ka Tarika}
\subsection*{IntelliJ IDEA/Eclipse Me Breakpoint Set Karo}
Code editor me line number ke left side pe click karo. Ek red dot show hoga jo breakpoint ko represent karta hai.

\textbf{Example:}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
public void greet() {
    String name = "John";  // Yahan breakpoint set karo
    System.out.println("Hello, " + name);
}
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{Debug Mode Me Run Karo}
\textbf{IntelliJ:} Run → Debug 'Application'

\textbf{Eclipse:} Right Click on Application → Debug As → Java Application

\begin{itemize}
    \item \begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]

\section*{Step Over, Step Into, Aur Step Out Kya Hai?}
\subsection*{Step Over (F8)}
Current line ko execute karo aur next line pe move karo. Agar current line me function call hai, toh uss function ke andar nahi jayega.

\textbf{Example:}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
public void greet() {
    String name = "John";  // Step Over karne pe next line pe move hoga
    System.out.println("Hello, " + name);
}
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{Step Into (F7)}
Current line ko execute karo aur agar uss line me function call hai, toh uss function ke andar jayega.

\textbf{Example:}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
public void greet() {
    String name = "John";
    printName(name);  // Step Into karne pe printName function ke andar jayega
}

public void printName(String name) {
    System.out.println("Name: " + name);
}
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{Step Out (Shift + F8)}
Agar aap kisi function ke andar ho aur uss function se bahar aana chahte ho, toh Step Out ka use karo. Yeh aapko function ke end tak execute karke wapas caller function pe le jayega.

\section*{Debug Mode Me Server Start Karo}
Command line se debug mode enable karne ke liye:
\begin{lstlisting}
mvn spring-boot:run -Ddebug
\end{lstlisting}

 \end{tcolorbox}

Ya manually application.properties file me add karo:
\begin{lstlisting}
debug=true
\end{lstlisting}

Isse detailed logs console me show honge.

\section*{Remote Debugging Enable Karo}
Agar aap server remotely debug karna chahte ho:
\begin{lstlisting}
java -agentlib:jdwp=transport=dt_socket,server=y,suspend=n,address=*:5005 -jar yourapp.jar
\end{lstlisting}

Phir IntelliJ ya Eclipse me Remote Debug Configuration set karke Port 5005 pe connect karo.

% Section 1: Spring Boot Folder Structure
\textcolor{subheadingcolor}{\textbf{\Large Spring Boot Folder Structure}} % Light blue for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

Express.js me hum generally ye structure follow karte hain: \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{lstlisting}[basicstyle=\ttfamily\small, backgroundcolor=\color{codebg}]
project/
├── routes/       (API routes)
├── controllers/  (Business logic)
├── models/       (Database models)
├── middleware/   (Middleware functions)
└── app.js        (Main server file)
\end{lstlisting}

Spring Boot me iska equivalent structure kuch aisa hota hai: \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{lstlisting}[basicstyle=\ttfamily\small, backgroundcolor=\color{codebg}]
src/
├── main/
│   ├── java/
│   │   └── com/
│   │       └── example/
│   │           └── demo/
│   │               ├── controller/   (API endpoints)
│   │               ├── service/      (Business logic)
│   │               ├── repository/   (Database operations)
│   │               ├── model/        (Database models)
│   │               └── DemoApplication.java  (Main server file)
│   └── resources/
│       ├── static/   (Static files like CSS, JS)
│       ├── templates/ (HTML templates)
│       └── application.properties  (Configuration file)
└── test/
    └── java/
        └── com/
            └── example/
                └── demo/
                    └── DemoApplicationTests.java  (Test file)
\end{lstlisting}

% Section 2: `controller/` Folder
\textcolor{subheadingcolor}{\textbf{\Large 1. `controller/` Folder}} % Light blue for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

\textbf{Express.js Comparison:} \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Express.js me `routes/` folder me API routes define kiye jate hain.
    \item Example:
\end{itemize}

% Code Snippet: Express.js Example
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{Express.js Example}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=JavaScript]
app.get('/hello', (req, res) => {
    res.send('Hello, Express!');
});
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Spring Boot me:} \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item `controller/` folder me API endpoints define kiye jate hain.
    \item Ye folder \textbf{REST APIs} handle karta hai.
    \item Example:
\end{itemize}

\begin{itemize}
    \item \begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]
        `controller/` folder me API endpoints define kiye jate hain.
    \end{tcolorbox}
    \item Ye folder \textbf{REST APIs} handle karta hai.
\end{itemize}

% Code Snippet: Spring Boot Example
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{HelloController.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
package com.example.demo.controller;

import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.GetMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RestController;

@RestController
public class HelloController {

    @GetMapping("/hello")
    public String sayHello() {
        return "Hello, Spring Boot!";
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

    \item Example:
\end{itemize}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=JavaScript]
const getData = () => {
    return "Some data";
};
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Spring Boot me:} \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item \begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]
        `service/` folder me \textbf{business logic} likha jata hai.
    \end{tcolorbox}
    \item \begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]
        Ye folder \textbf{reusable code} aur complex logic handle karta hai.
    \end{tcolorbox}
    \item Example:
\end{itemize}

import org.springframework.stereotype.Service;

@Service
public class HelloService {

    public String getMessage() {
        return "Hello from Service!";
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]
\section{Step 1: Repository Folder Ka Role}
Spring Boot me \texttt{repository} folder database ke saath interaction handle karta hai. Ye Express.js ke \texttt{Mongoose Model} jaisa kaam karta hai, jo CRUD (Create, Read, Update, Delete) operations perform karta hai.
\end{tcolorbox}


\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]
\textbf{Hinglish Explanation:} Repository folder ka kaam database se interact karna hota hai. Ye Express.js ke \texttt{models/User.js} (Mongoose Model) jaisa hota hai.
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{table}[h]
    \centering
    \renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3} % Adjust row height for better spacing
    \setlength{\arrayrulewidth}{0.5mm} % Thicker border lines
    \arrayrulecolor{black} % Border color
    \begin{tabular}{|p{3cm}|p{5cm}|p{6cm}|} % Column width adjusted
        \hline
        \rowcolor% Header color
        \textbf{Folder} & \textbf{Express.js Equivalent} & \textbf{Role} \\
        \hline
        \cellcolor \texttt{repository/} & \cellcolor \texttt{models/User.js} (Mongoose Model) & Database se CRUD operations handle karta hai. \\
        \hline
        \cellcolor \texttt{entity/} & \cellcolor \texttt{models/User.js} (Schema) & Database table ka structure define karta hai. \\
        \hline
    \end{tabular}
    \caption{Spring Boot Repository vs Express.js Mongoose Model}
    \label{tab:repository-role}
\end{table}



\textbf{Spring Boot me:} \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item `repository/` folder me \textbf{database operations} likhe jate hain.
    \item Ye folder \textbf{database se data fetch ya save} karne ka kaam karta hai.
    \item Example:
\end{itemize}

% Code Snippet: Spring Boot Example
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{UserRepository.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
package com.example.demo.repository;

import com.example.demo.model.User;
import org.springframework.data.jpa.repository.JpaRepository;

public interface UserRepository extends JpaRepository<User, Long> {
    // Custom queries yahan likh sakte hain
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{document}

\section{Repository Ki Zaroorat Kyun Hai?}

Spring Boot me \textbf{Repository} ek important component hai jo database aur application ke beech ka bridge ka kaam karta hai. Agar repository na ho, toh aap directly database queries nahi likh sakte, aur \texttt{.findById()}, \texttt{.save()}, \texttt{.deleteById()} jaise methods use nahi kar sakte.

\begin{examplebox}{Without Repository, You Cannot Use These Methods}
\textbf{Agar repository na ho, toh ye methods direct use nahi ho sakte:}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \texttt{findById(id)} - ID ke basis pe data fetch karne ke liye.
    \item \texttt{save(entity)} - Data save/update karne ke liye.
    \item \texttt{deleteById(id)} - Record delete karne ke liye.
    \item \texttt{findByEmail(email)} - Email ke basis pe search karne ke liye.
\end{itemize}
\end{examplebox}

\subsection{Repository Ki Importance}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{Bridge Between Database and Service Layer:} Repository database aur \texttt{Service} / \texttt{Controller} layer ke beech mediator ka kaam karta hai.
    \item \textbf{Auto-Generated SQL Queries:} Spring Boot ka \texttt{JpaRepository} automatically SQL queries generate karta hai, based on method names. Iska matlab hai ki aapko manually queries likhne ki zaroorat nahi hoti.
    \item \textbf{Less Boilerplate Code:} Agar aap \texttt{JpaRepository} use karte hain, toh CRUD operations likhne ki zaroorat nahi hoti, kyunki Spring Boot khud inhe generate kar leta hai.
\end{itemize}




% Section 5: `model/` Folder
\textcolor{subheadingcolor}{\textbf{\Large 4. `model/` Folder}} % Light blue for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

\textbf{Express.js Comparison:} \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Express.js me `models/` folder me database schemas define kiye jate hain.
    \item Example:
\end{itemize}

% Code Snippet: Express.js Example
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{Express.js Example}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=JavaScript]
const userSchema = new mongoose.Schema({
    name: String,
    age: Number
});
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Spring Boot me:} \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item `model/` folder me \textbf{database entities} define kiye jate hain.
    \item Ye folder \textbf{database tables} ko represent karta hai.
    \item Example:
\end{itemize}

% Code Snippet: Spring Boot Example
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{User.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
package com.example.demo.model;

import jakarta.persistence.Entity;
import jakarta.persistence.GeneratedValue;
import jakarta.persistence.GenerationType;
import jakarta.persistence.Id;

@Entity
public class User {

    @Id
    @GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY)
    private Long id;
    private String name;
    private int age;

    // Getters and Setters
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

% Section 6: `resources/` Folder
\textcolor{subheadingcolor}{\textbf{\Large 5. `resources/` Folder}} % Light blue for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

\textbf{Express.js Comparison:} \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Express.js me static files (CSS, JS, images) ko root folder me rakha jata hai.
    \item Example:
\end{itemize}

% Code Snippet: Express.js Example
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{Express.js Example}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=JavaScript]
app.use(express.static('public'));
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Spring Boot me:} \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item `resources/` folder me \textbf{static files} aur \textbf{configuration files} rakhe jate hain.
    \item Ye folder \textbf{static content} aur \textbf{application settings} handle karta hai.
    \item Sub-folders:
    \begin{itemize}
        \item `static/`: CSS, JS, images rakhe jate hain.
        \item `templates/`: HTML templates rakhe jate hain.
        \item `application.properties`: Configuration settings rakhe jate hain.
    \end{itemize}
\end{itemize}

import org.springframework.boot.SpringApplication;
import org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.SpringBootApplication;

@SpringBootApplication
public class DemoApplication {

    public static void main(String[] args) {
        SpringApplication.run(DemoApplication.class, args);
    }

    \hline
    \textbf{Folder/File} & \textbf{Express.js Comparison} & \textbf{Spring Boot Role} \\ \hline
    `controller/` & `routes/` & API endpoints handle karta hai. \\ \hline
    `service/` & `controllers/` ya modules & Business logic handle karta hai. \\ \hline
    `repository/` & `models/` (database operations) & Database operations handle karta hai. \\ \hline
    `model/` & `models/` (database schemas) & Database entities define karta hai. \\ \hline
    `resources/` & Static files (CSS, JS, images) & Static files aur configuration rakhta hai. \\ \hline
    `DemoApplication.java` & `app.js` & Server start karta hai. \\ \hline
\end{tabular}

% Section 1: Main Application File
\textcolor{subheadingcolor}{\textbf{\Large 1. Main Application File}} % Light blue for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

\textbf{File Name:} `DemoApplication.java` \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\textbf{Location:} `src/main/java/com/example/demo/` \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

% Code Snippet: DemoApplication.java
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{DemoApplication.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
package com.example.demo;  // Package declaration (folder structure ke hisab se)

import org.springframework.boot.SpringApplication;
import org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.SpringBootApplication;

@SpringBootApplication  // Ye batata hai ki yeh Spring Boot application hai
public class DemoApplication {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        SpringApplication.run(DemoApplication.class, args);  // Application start karta hai
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:} % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item \texttt{@SpringBootApplication}: Ye annotation Spring Boot ko batata hai ki yeh application ka main class hai. Isme \textbf{3 annotations} hote hain:
    \begin{itemize}
        \item \texttt{@SpringBootConfiguration}: Configuration define karta hai.
        \item \texttt{@EnableAutoConfiguration}: Automatic configuration enable karta hai.
        \item \texttt{@ComponentScan}: Package me components (controllers, services, etc.) ko scan karta hai.
    \end{itemize}
    \item \textcolor{warningcolor}{\texttt{SpringApplication.run()}: Ye method Spring Boot application ko start karta hai.} % Red for important points
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Express.js Me Relate Karo:} \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
Express.js me \texttt{app.listen(3000)} ka kaam Spring Boot me \textbf{\texttt{SpringApplication.run()}} karta hai.

% Section 2: Creating a REST Controller
\textcolor{subheadingcolor}{\textbf{\Large 2. Creating a REST Controller}} % Light blue for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

\textbf{File Name:} `HelloController.java` \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\textbf{Location:} `src/main/java/com/example/demo/controller/` \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

% Code Snippet: HelloController.java
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{HelloController.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
package com.example.demo.controller;  // Package declaration

import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.GetMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RestController;

@RestController  // Ye batata hai ki yeh class ek REST controller hai
public class HelloController {

    @GetMapping("/hello")  // GET request ke liye endpoint
    public String sayHello() {
        return "Hello, Spring Boot!";  // Response return karta hai
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:} % \textbf{} for bold text
\documentclass{article}
\usepackage{tcolorbox}
\usepackage{xcolor} % For custom colors

\begin{document}


\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]
    \item \texttt{@RestController}: Ye annotation batata hai ki yeh class ek REST controller hai. Yeh \texttt{@Controller} aur \texttt{@ResponseBody} ka combination hai.
    \item \texttt{@GetMapping("/hello")}: Ye batata hai ki \texttt{/hello} endpoint pe GET request handle karna hai.
    \item 
        \texttt{sayHello()}: Ye method \texttt{/hello} endpoint pe request aane par call hota hai aur response return karta hai.
    \end{tcolorbox}
\end{itemize}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]

\textbf{Express.js Me Relate Karo:} \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
Express.js me \texttt{app.get('/hello')} ka kaam Spring Boot me \textbf{\texttt{@GetMapping("/hello")}} karta hai.

\end{tcolorbox}

% Section 3: Adding a Service Layer
\textcolor{subheadingcolor}{\textbf{\Large 3. Adding a Service Layer}} % Light blue for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

\textbf{File Name:} `HelloService.java` \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\textbf{Location:} `src/main/java/com/example/demo/service/` \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

% Code Snippet: HelloService.java
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{HelloService.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
package com.example.demo.service;  // Package declaration

import org.springframework.stereotype.Service;  // Service annotation

@Service  // Ye batata hai ki yeh class ek service hai
public class HelloService {
    public String getHelloMessage() {
        return "Hello from Service!";  // Business logic
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:} % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]
    \item \texttt{@Service}: Ye annotation batata hai ki yeh class ek service hai. Isme business logic likha jata hai.
    


\textbf{Express.js Me Relate Karo:} \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
Express.js me tum \texttt{services} folder me business logic likhte ho, wahi kaam Spring Boot me \textbf{\texttt{@Service}} karta hai.

\end{tcolorbox}

% Section 4: Using Service in Controller
\textcolor{subheadingcolor}{\textbf{\Large 4. Using Service in Controller}} % Light blue for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

\textbf{File Name:} `HelloController.java` \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\textbf{Location:} `src/main/java/com/example/demo/controller/` \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

% Code Snippet: HelloController.java
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{HelloController.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
package com.example.demo.controller;

import com.example.demo.service.HelloService;  // Service import karo
import org.springframework.beans.factory.annotation.Autowired;  // Dependency injection
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.GetMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RestController;

@RestController
public class HelloController {

    @Autowired  // Service ko inject karo
    private HelloService helloService;

    @GetMapping("/hello")
    public String sayHello() {
        return helloService.getHelloMessage();  // Service ka method call karo
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:} % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]
    \item \texttt{@Autowired}: Ye annotation Spring Boot ko batata hai ki \texttt{HelloService} ko automatically inject kare. Isse hume manually object banane ki zaroorat nahi hoti.


\textbf{Express.js Me Relate Karo:} \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
Express.js me tum manually \texttt{require('./services/HelloService')} karte ho, wahi kaam Spring Boot me \textbf{\texttt{@Autowired}} karta hai.
\end{tcolorbox}

% Section 5: Database Connection
\textcolor{subheadingcolor}{\textbf{\Large 5. Database Connection}} % Light blue for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

\textbf{File Name:} `application.properties` \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\textbf{Location:} `src/main/resources/` \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

% Code Snippet: application.properties
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{application.properties}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}
spring.datasource.url=jdbc:mysql://localhost:3306/mydb  # Database URL
spring.datasource.username=root  # Database username
spring.datasource.password=password  # Database password
spring.jpa.hibernate.ddl-auto=update  # Automatically update database schema
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{File Name:} `User.java` (Entity Class) \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\textbf{Location:} `src/main/java/com/example/demo/model/` \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

% Code Snippet: User.java
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{User.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
package com.example.demo.model;

import javax.persistence.Entity;  // Ye batata hai ki yeh class database table ke saath map hogi
import javax.persistence.GeneratedValue;  // Auto-increment ke liye
import javax.persistence.GenerationType;  // Generation strategy ke liye
import javax.persistence.Id;  // Primary key ke liye

@Entity  // Ye batata hai ki yeh class database table ke saath map hogi
public class User {
    @Id  // Primary key
    @GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY)  // Auto-increment
    private Long id;
    private String name;

    // Getters and Setters
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{File Name:} `UserRepository.java` (Repository Interface) \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\textbf{Location:} `src/main/java/com/example/demo/repository/` \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

% Code Snippet: UserRepository.java
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{UserRepository.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
package com.example.demo.repository;

import com.example.demo.model.User;
import org.springframework.data.jpa.repository.JpaRepository;  // JpaRepository provide karta hai CRUD operations

public interface UserRepository extends JpaRepository<User, Long> {
    // Yaha pe custom methods likh sakte hain
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:} % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]
    \item \texttt{@Entity}: Ye annotation batata hai ki yeh class database table ke saath map hogi.
    \item \texttt{@Id}: Ye annotation batata hai ki yeh field primary key hai.
    \item \texttt{@GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY)}: Ye batata hai ki primary key auto-increment hogi.
    \item \textcolor{warningcolor}{\texttt{JpaRepository}: Ye interface provide karta hai CRUD operations (Create, Read, Update, Delete).} % Red for important points


\textbf{Express.js Me Relate Karo:} \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
Express.js me tum \texttt{mongoose.model()} aur \texttt{User.find()} ka use karte ho, wahi kaam Spring Boot me \textbf{\texttt{@Entity}} aur \textbf{\texttt{JpaRepository}} karte hain.

\end{tcolorbox}
% Section 6: Testing the Application
\textcolor{subheadingcolor}{\textbf{\Large 6. Testing the Application}} % Light blue for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

\textbf{File Name:} `DemoApplicationTests.java` \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

package com.example.demo;

import org.junit.jupiter.api.Test;
import org.springframework.boot.test.context.SpringBootTest;

@SpringBootTest  // Ye annotation Spring Boot context load karta hai testing ke liye
class DemoApplicationTests {
    @Test
    void contextLoads() {
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:} % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item \texttt{@SpringBootTest}: Ye annotation Spring Boot context load karta hai testing ke liye.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Express.js Me Relate Karo:} \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
Express.js me tum \texttt{Jest} ya \texttt{Mocha} use karte ho, wahi kaam Spring Boot me \textbf{\texttt{@SpringBootTest}} karta hai.
