% Document begins
\begin{document}

% Title
\begin{center}
  {\bfseries\Huge\color{headingblue} Spring Boot Interceptors or Middleware: A Hinglish Guide \par}




  
\end{center}

% Introduction
\section{Introduction}
Agar aap Express.js se Spring Boot aa rahe hain aur middleware ka concept samajhna chahte hain, toh ye guide aapke liye hai. Spring Boot me middleware ka kaam **Interceptors** karte hain. Ye guide aapko step-by-step interceptor banana aur use karne ka tarika samjhayega.

---

% Step 1: Middleware (Interceptor) ka Concept
\section{Step 1: Middleware (Interceptor) ka Concept}
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]
  \item \textbf{Express.js me middleware} ka kaam hota hai request aur response ke beech me kuch kaam karna, jaise logging, authentication, ya error handling. Ye `app.use()` se implement hota hai.
  \item \textbf{Spring Boot me} yehi kaam **Interceptor** karta hai. Interceptor bhi request aur response ke beech me kuch logic execute kar sakta hai.
\end{tcolorbox}

---

% Step 2: Express.js Middleware vs Spring Boot Interceptor
\section{Step 2: Express.js Middleware vs Spring Boot Interceptor}
\begin{center}
  \begin{tabular}{|>{\columncolor{headingblue!30}}p{4cm}|>{\columncolor{examplered!30}}p{4cm}|>{\columncolor{yellow!30}}p{4cm}|}
    \hline
    \textbf{Feature} & \textbf{Express.js Middleware} & \textbf{Spring Boot Interceptor} \\
    \hline
    Definition & `app.use()` function & `HandlerInterceptor` interface \\
    \hline
    Purpose & Request ko modify ya filter karna & Request ko modify ya filter karna \\
    \hline
    Execution & Request ke pehle ya response ke baad & Request ke pehle ya response ke baad \\
    \hline
    Example Use & Logging, Authentication, JWT Validation & Logging, Authentication, JWT Validation \\
    \hline
  \end{tabular}
\end{center}

---

% Step 3: Middleware (Interceptor) Banana
\section{Step 3: Middleware (Interceptor) Banana}
Spring Boot me middleware banana **`HandlerInterceptor` interface** ke through hota hai. Isme **3 methods** hote hain:
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]
  \item \textbf{`preHandle()`} → Request ke process hone se pehle chalega (Express.js ke `app.use()` jaisa).
  \item \textbf{`postHandle()`} → Controller ka kaam hone ke baad chalega.
  \item \textbf{`afterCompletion()`} → Response bhejne ke baad chalega.
\end{tcolorbox}

---

% Step 4: LoggingInterceptor Banana
\section{Step 4: LoggingInterceptor Banana}
Yeh ek simple middleware hai jo har request ko log karega.

\begin{examplebox}{LoggingInterceptor.java}
\begin{lstlisting}
package com.example.project.interceptor;

import org.springframework.stereotype.Component;
import org.springframework.web.servlet.HandlerInterceptor;

import javax.servlet.http.HttpServletRequest;
import javax.servlet.http.HttpServletResponse;

@Component  // Ye Spring Boot ko batata hai ki ye ek component hai
public class LoggingInterceptor implements HandlerInterceptor {

    // ✅ Step 1: preHandle() → Request aane se pehle chalega
    @Override
    public boolean preHandle(HttpServletRequest request, HttpServletResponse response, Object handler) {
        System.out.println("�� Incoming Request: " + request.getMethod() + " " + request.getRequestURI());
        return true;  // \textcolor{red}{Agar false return kare to request abort ho jayegi}
    }

    // ✅ Step 2: postHandle() → Controller ka kaam hone ke baad chalega
    @Override
    public void postHandle(HttpServletRequest request, HttpServletResponse response, Object handler, org.springframework.web.servlet.ModelAndView modelAndView) {
        System.out.println("✅ Response Status: " + response.getStatus());
    }

    // ✅ Step 3: afterCompletion() → Response bhejne ke baad chalega
    @Override
    public void afterCompletion(HttpServletRequest request, HttpServletResponse response, Object handler, Exception exception) {
        System.out.println("�� Request Completed!");
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

---

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]

% Step 5: Middleware ko Register Karna
\section{Step 5: Middleware ko Register Karna}
Middleware ko use karne ke liye use **register** karna padta hai. Ye kaam **`WebMvcConfigurer`** interface karta hai.

\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{examplebox}{WebConfig.java}
\begin{lstlisting}
package com.example.project.config;

import com.example.project.interceptor.LoggingInterceptor;
import org.springframework.beans.factory.annotation.Autowired;
import org.springframework.context.annotation.Configuration;
import org.springframework.web.servlet.config.annotation.InterceptorRegistry;
import org.springframework.web.servlet.config.annotation.WebMvcConfigurer;

@Configuration  // Ye batata hai ki ye ek configuration file hai
public class WebConfig implements WebMvcConfigurer {

    @Autowired
    private LoggingInterceptor loggingInterceptor;  // Middleware ko inject kar rahe hain

    @Override
    public void addInterceptors(InterceptorRegistry registry) {
        registry.addInterceptor(loggingInterceptor);  // Middleware ko register kar rahe hain
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

---

% Step 6: Middleware ko Test Karna
\section{Step 6: Middleware ko Test Karna}
Ab middleware kaam kar raha hai ya nahi, ye check karne ke liye ek simple API banate hain.

\begin{examplebox}{UserController.java}
\begin{lstlisting}
package com.example.project.controller;

import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.GetMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RequestMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RestController;

@RestController
@RequestMapping("/users")
public class UserController {

    @GetMapping("/test")
    public String testEndpoint() {
        return "Middleware is working!";
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

---

% Step 7: JWT Authentication Middleware Banana
\section{Step 7: JWT Authentication Middleware Banana}
Agar tum **JWT Token validation** ka middleware banana chahte ho, to `preHandle()` me JWT check kar sakte ho.

\begin{examplebox}{JwtInterceptor.java}
\begin{lstlisting}
package com.example.project.interceptor;

import io.jsonwebtoken.Claims;
import io.jsonwebtoken.Jwts;
import org.springframework.stereotype.Component;
import org.springframework.web.servlet.HandlerInterceptor;

import javax.servlet.http.HttpServletRequest;
import javax.servlet.http.HttpServletResponse;

@Component
public class JwtInterceptor implements HandlerInterceptor {

    private static final String SECRET_KEY = "mySecretKey";  // JWT Secret Key

    @Override
    public boolean preHandle(HttpServletRequest request, HttpServletResponse response, Object handler) {
        String token = request.getHeader("Authorization");

        if (token == null || !token.startsWith("Bearer ")) {
            response.setStatus(HttpServletResponse.SC_UNAUTHORIZED);
            return false;  // {❌ Unauthorized request abort ho jayegi}
        }

        try {
            token = token.substring(7);  // "Bearer " hata rahe hain
            Claims claims = Jwts.parser().setSigningKey(SECRET_KEY).parseClaimsJws(token).getBody();
            request.setAttribute("userId", claims.getSubject());
        } catch (Exception e) {
            response.setStatus(HttpServletResponse.SC_UNAUTHORIZED);
            return false;
        }

        return true;
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

---

% Final Summary
\section{Final Summary}
\begin{itemize}
  \item \textbf{Express.js ka `app.use()` = Spring Boot ka `Interceptor`.}
  \item \textbf{Interceptor ke 3 methods hote hain:}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item `preHandle()` → Request se pehle.
      \item `postHandle()` → Controller ke baad.
      \item `afterCompletion()` → Response ke baad.
    \end{itemize}
  \item \textbf{Middleware ko register karne ke liye `WebMvcConfigurer` use karte hain.}
  \item \textbf{JWT validation jaise advanced tasks ke liye bhi interceptor use kar sakte hain.}
\end{itemize}

---

<dependencies>
    <!-- Spring Boot Starter Web -->
    <dependency>
        <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
        <artifactId>spring-boot-starter-web</artifactId>
    </dependency>

    <!-- Spring Boot Starter Data JPA -->
    <dependency>
        <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
        <artifactId>spring-boot-starter-data-jpa</artifactId>
    </dependency>

    <!-- H2 Database (In-memory database for testing) -->
    <dependency>
        <groupId>com.h2database</groupId>
        <artifactId>h2</artifactId>
        <scope>runtime</scope>
    </dependency>

    <!-- JWT Library -->
    <dependency>
        <groupId>io.jsonwebtoken</groupId>
        <artifactId>jjwt</artifactId>
        <version>0.9.1</version>
    </dependency>

    <!-- Lombok (Optional, for reducing boilerplate code) -->
    <dependency>
        <groupId>org.projectlombok</groupId>
        <artifactId>lombok</artifactId>
        <scope>provided</scope>
    </dependency>
</dependencies>
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

    \item \texttt{spring-boot-starter-web}: REST APIs banane ke liye.
    \item \texttt{spring-boot-starter-data-jpa}: Database operations ke liye.
    \item \texttt{h2}: In-memory database for testing.
    \item \texttt{jjwt}: JWT generate aur validate karne ke liye.
    \item \texttt{lombok}: Boilerplate code kam karne ke liye (optional).
\end{itemize}

% Step 3: Create User Entity Section
\textcolor{subheadingcolor}{\textbf{\Large Step 3: Create User Entity}} % Light blue for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

\textbf{File Name:} `User.java` \newline
\textbf{Location:} `src/main/java/com/example/demo/model/` \newline

% Code Snippet: User.java
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{User.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
package com.example.demo.model;

import javax.persistence.Entity;
import javax.persistence.GeneratedValue;
import javax.persistence.GenerationType;
import javax.persistence.Id;

@Entity  // Marks this class as a JPA entity, meaning it will be mapped to a database table
public class User {
    @Id  // Defines this field as the primary key
    @GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY)  // Specifies that the ID should auto-increment
    private Long id;
    
    private String name; // Field for storing user name
    private String email; // Field for storing user email
    
    // Default Constructor (Required by JPA)
    public User() {}
    
    // Parameterized Constructor
    public User(String name, String email) {
        this.name = name;
        this.email = email;
    }
    
    // Getters and Setters
    public Long getId() { return id; }
    public void setId(Long id) { this.id = id; }
    
    public String getName() { return name; }
    public void setName(String name) { this.name = name; }
    
    public String getEmail() { return email; }
    public void setEmail(String email) { this.email = email; }
    
    // toString() Method (For Debugging and Logging)
    @Override
    public String toString() {
        return "User{" +
                "id=" + id +
                ", name='" + name + '\'' +
                ", email='" + email + '\'' +
                '}';
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:}
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]
    \item \texttt{@Entity}: This annotation marks the class as a database entity, allowing it to be mapped to a table.
    \item \texttt{@Id}: Specifies that the field is the primary key.
    \item \texttt{@GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY)}: Ensures that the primary key auto-increments with each new record.
    \item \textbf{Default Constructor}: Required by JPA for entity initialization.
    \item \textbf{Parameterized Constructor}: Allows creating a `User` object with specific values.
    \item \textbf{Getters and Setters}: Used to access and modify private fields.
    \item \textbf{toString() Method}: Useful for debugging and logging user information.
\end{tcolorbox}

% Horizontal Line
\noindent\rule{\textwidth}{1pt}
\vspace{0.5cm}

    // Yaha pe custom methods likh sakte hain

% Step 5: Create User Service Section
\textcolor{subheadingcolor}{\textbf{\Large Step 5: Create User Service}} % Light blue for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

\textbf{File Name:} `UserService.java` \newline
\textbf{Location:} `src/main/java/com/example/demo/service/` \newline

% Code Snippet: UserService.java
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{UserService.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
package com.example.demo.service;

import com.example.demo.model.User;
import com.example.demo.repository.UserRepository;
import org.springframework.beans.factory.annotation.Autowired;
import org.springframework.stereotype.Service;

import java.util.List;
import java.util.Optional;

@Service  // Ye batata hai ki yeh class ek service hai jo business logic handle karegi
public class UserService {

    @Autowired  // Ye automatically UserRepository ka instance inject karega
    private UserRepository userRepository;

    // Naya user create karne ke liye method
    public User createUser(User user) {
        return userRepository.save(user);  // User ko database me save karta hai
    }

    // Sabhi users ko retrieve karne ke liye method
    public List<User> getAllUsers() {
        return userRepository.findAll();  // Database se sabhi users fetch karega
    }

    // Specific user ko ID ke basis pe retrieve karne ka method
    public Optional<User> getUserById(Long id) {
        return userRepository.findById(id);  // Agar user milta hai to return karega, nahi to empty Optional
    }

    // User ko update karne ka method
    public User updateUser(Long id, User userDetails) {
        User user = userRepository.findById(id).orElseThrow(() -> new RuntimeException("User not found"));
        user.setName(userDetails.getName());
        user.setEmail(userDetails.getEmail());
        return userRepository.save(user);  // Updated user ko database me save karega
    }

    // User ko delete karne ka method
    public void deleteUser(Long id) {
        userRepository.deleteById(id);  // ID ke basis pe user ko delete karega
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:}
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]
    \item \texttt{@Service}: Ye annotation batata hai ki yeh class ek service component hai jo application ki business logic handle karegi.
    \item \texttt{@Autowired}: Ye annotation Spring Boot ko batata hai ki `UserRepository` ka object automatically inject kiya jaye.
    \item \texttt{User user}: Ye ek `User` class ka object hai jo ek particular user ka data store karega.
    \item \texttt{public List<User> getAllUsers()}: Ye method database se sabhi `User` objects ki list return karega.
    \item \texttt{public Optional<User> getUserById(Long id)}: Ye method `Optional<User>` return karega, jo ya to ek user object hoga agar user mil gaya, ya phir empty hoga agar user nahi mila.
    \item \texttt{Long id}: Ye `Long` datatype ka ek variable hai jo user ki unique ID store karega.
    \item \texttt{User userDetails}: Ye ek `User` object hai jo naye details store karega jab user update hoga.
    \item \texttt{userRepository.save(user)}: Ye method user object ko database me save karega.
    \item \texttt{userRepository.findById(id).orElseThrow()}: Ye database me ID ke basis pe user dhoondta hai. Agar nahi milta to exception throw karega.
    \item \texttt{userRepository.deleteById(id)}: Ye method user ko ID ke basis pe delete karega.

\end{tcolorbox}

% Horizontal Line
\noindent\rule{\textwidth}{1pt}
\vspace{0.5cm}








% Horizontal Line
\noindent\rule{\textwidth}{1pt}
\vspace{0.5cm}

% Step 6: Create User Controller Section
\textcolor{subheadingcolor}{\textbf{\Large Step 6: Create User Controller}} % Light blue for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

\textbf{File Name:} `UserController.java` \newline
\textbf{Location:} `src/main/java/com/example/demo/controller/` \newline

% Code Snippet: UserController.java
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{UserController.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
package com.example.demo.controller;

import com.example.demo.model.User;
import com.example.demo.service.UserService;
import org.springframework.beans.factory.annotation.Autowired;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.*;

import java.util.List;
import java.util.Optional;

@RestController  // Ye batata hai ki yeh class ek REST controller hai
@RequestMapping("/users")  // Base URL for all endpoints in this controller
public class UserController {

    @Autowired  // UserService ko inject karo
    private UserService userService;

    // Create user
    @PostMapping  // POST request ke liye endpoint
    public User createUser(@RequestBody User user) {
        return userService.createUser(user);  // User create karo
    }

    // Get all users
    @GetMapping  // GET request ke liye endpoint
    public List<User> getAllUsers() {
        return userService.getAllUsers();  // Sabhi users ko fetch karo
    }

    // Get user by ID
    @GetMapping("/{id}")  // GET request ke liye endpoint with ID
    public Optional<User> getUserById(@PathVariable Long id) {
        return userService.getUserById(id);  // User ko ID se fetch karo
    }

    // Update user
    @PutMapping("/{id}")  // PUT request ke liye endpoint with ID
    public User updateUser(@PathVariable Long id, @RequestBody User userDetails) {
        return userService.updateUser(id, userDetails);  // User ko update karo
    }

    // Delete user
    @DeleteMapping("/{id}")  // DELETE request ke liye endpoint with ID
    public void deleteUser(@PathVariable Long id) {
        userService.deleteUser(id);  // User ko delete karo
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=warningcolor!10, colframe=warningcolor, title=\textbf{\textcolor{warningcolor}{Important Explanation}}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item \texttt{@RestController}: \textbf{\textcolor{warningcolor}{Ye annotation batata hai ki yeh class ek REST controller hai jo API endpoints handle karegi.}} 
    \item \texttt{@RequestMapping("/users")}: \textbf{\textcolor{warningcolor}{Iska matlab hai ki is class ke sare endpoints `/users` URL path se start honge.}} 
    \item \texttt{@Autowired}: \textbf{\textcolor{warningcolor}{Ye automatically `UserService` ka instance inject karega, jisse hum database operations perform kar sake.}} 
    \item \texttt{@PostMapping}, \texttt{@GetMapping}, \texttt{@PutMapping}, \texttt{@DeleteMapping}: \textbf{\textcolor{warningcolor}{Yeh annotations define karte hain ki kis HTTP method se request aayegi.}} 
    \item \texttt{@PathVariable Long id}: \textbf{\textcolor{warningcolor}{Iska use hota hai URL me diye gaye `id` ko method ke parameter me fetch karne ke liye.}} 
    \item \texttt{@RequestBody User user}: \textbf{\textcolor{warningcolor}{Iska use hota hai incoming JSON data ko `User` object me convert karne ke liye.}} 
\end{itemize}
\end{tcolorbox}

% Horizontal Line
\noindent\rule{\textwidth}{1pt}
\vspace{0.5cm}






% Horizontal Line
\noindent\rule{\textwidth}{1pt}
\vspace{0.5cm}

% Step 7: Create JWT Interceptor Section
\textcolor{subheadingcolor}{\textbf{\Large Step 7: Create JWT Interceptor}} % Light blue for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

\textbf{File Name:} `JwtInterceptor.java` \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\textbf{Location:} `src/main/java/com/example/demo/interceptor/` \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

% Code Snippet: JwtInterceptor.java
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{JwtInterceptor.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
package com.example.demo.interceptor;

import io.jsonwebtoken.Claims;
import io.jsonwebtoken.Jwts;
import org.springframework.stereotype.Component;
import org.springframework.web.servlet.HandlerInterceptor;

import javax.servlet.http.HttpServletRequest;
import javax.servlet.http.HttpServletResponse;

@Component  // Ye batata hai ki yeh class ek Spring component hai
public class JwtInterceptor implements HandlerInterceptor {

    private static final String SECRET_KEY = "mySecretKey";  // JWT secret key

    @Override  // Ye method har request ke pehle call hota hai
    public boolean preHandle(HttpServletRequest request, HttpServletResponse response, Object handler) throws Exception {
        String token = request.getHeader("Authorization");  // Request se token fetch karo

        if (token == null || !token.startsWith("Bearer ")) {
            response.sendError(HttpServletResponse.SC_UNAUTHORIZED, "Invalid token");  // Invalid token
            return false;
        }

        token = token.substring(7);  // "Bearer " ko remove karo
        try {
            Claims claims = Jwts.parser().setSigningKey(SECRET_KEY).parseClaimsJws(token).getBody();  // Token validate karo
            request.setAttribute("userId", claims.getSubject());  // User ID ko request me set karo
        } catch (Exception e) {
            response.sendError(HttpServletResponse.SC_UNAUTHORIZED, "Invalid token");  // Invalid token
            return false;
        }

        return true;  // Request ko agle interceptor ya controller ko pass karo
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:} % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item \texttt{@Component}: Ye annotation batata hai ki yeh class ek Spring component hai.
    \item \texttt{HandlerInterceptor}: Ye interface provide karta hai methods jo har request ke pehle, baad me, ya completion pe call hote hain.
    \item \texttt{preHandle()}: Ye method har request ke pehle call hota hai. Agar ye \texttt{true} return kare, toh request agle interceptor ya controller tak jayegi. Agar \texttt{false} return kare, toh request ruk jayegi.
\end{itemize}

% Horizontal Line
\noindent\rule{\textwidth}{1pt}
\vspace{0.5cm}

% Step 8: Register JWT Interceptor Section
\textcolor{subheadingcolor}{\textbf{\Large Step 8: Register JWT Interceptor}} % Light blue for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

\textbf{File Name:} `WebConfig.java` \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\textbf{Location:} `src/main/java/com/example/demo/config/` \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

% Code Snippet: WebConfig.java
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{WebConfig.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
package com.example.demo.config;

import com.example.demo.interceptor.JwtInterceptor;
import org.springframework.beans.factory.annotation.Autowired;
import org.springframework.context.annotation.Configuration;
import org.springframework.web.servlet.config.annotation.InterceptorRegistry;
import org.springframework.web.servlet.config.annotation.WebMvcConfigurer;

@Configuration  // Ye batata hai ki yeh class ek configuration hai
public class WebConfig implements WebMvcConfigurer {

    @Autowired  // JwtInterceptor ko inject karo
    private JwtInterceptor jwtInterceptor;

    @Override  // Ye method interceptors ko register karta hai
    public void addInterceptors(InterceptorRegistry registry) {
        registry.addInterceptor(jwtInterceptor).addPathPatterns("/users/**");  // JWT Interceptor ko register karo
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:} % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item \texttt{@Configuration}: Ye annotation batata hai ki yeh class ek configuration hai.
    \item \texttt{WebMvcConfigurer}: Ye interface provide karta hai methods jo web configuration ke liye use hote hain.
    \item \texttt{addInterceptors()}: Ye method interceptors ko register karta hai.
\end{itemize}

% Horizontal Line
\noindent\rule{\textwidth}{1pt}
\vspace{0.5cm}

% Step 9: Create Global Exception Handler Section
\textcolor{subheadingcolor}{\textbf{\Large Step 9: Create Global Exception Handler}} % Light blue for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

\textbf{File Name:} `GlobalExceptionHandler.java` \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\textbf{Location:} `src/main/java/com/example/demo/exception/` \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

% Code Snippet: GlobalExceptionHandler.java
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{GlobalExceptionHandler.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
package com.example.demo.exception;

import org.springframework.http.HttpStatus;
import org.springframework.http.ResponseEntity;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.ControllerAdvice;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.ExceptionHandler;

@ControllerAdvice  // Ye annotation batata hai ki yeh class global exception handling ke liye hai
public class GlobalExceptionHandler {

    @ExceptionHandler(RuntimeException.class)  // Ye method RuntimeException handle karega
    public ResponseEntity<String> handleRuntimeException(RuntimeException e) {
        return new ResponseEntity<>(e.getMessage(), HttpStatus.INTERNAL_SERVER_ERROR);  // Error message return karo
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:} % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item \texttt{@ControllerAdvice}: Ye annotation batata hai ki yeh class global exception handling ke liye hai.
    \item \texttt{@ExceptionHandler}: Ye annotation batata hai ki yeh method specific exception handle karega.
\end{itemize}

% Horizontal Line
\noindent\rule{\textwidth}{1pt}
\vspace{0.5cm}

% Step 10: Run the Application Section
\textcolor{subheadingcolor}{\textbf{\Large Step 10: Run the Application}} % Light blue for subheadings
\vspace{0.3cm}

\textbf{File Name:} `DemoApplication.java` \\ % \textbf{} for bold text
\textbf{Location:} `src/main/java/com/example/demo/` \\ % \textbf{} for bold text

% Code Snippet: DemoApplication.java
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=codeborder, title=\textbf{DemoApplication.java}, fonttitle=\bfseries]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
package com.example.demo;

import org.springframework.boot.SpringApplication;
import org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.SpringBootApplication;

@SpringBootApplication  // Ye batata hai ki yeh Spring Boot application hai
public class DemoApplication {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        SpringApplication.run(DemoApplication.class, args);  // Application start karo
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:} % \textbf{} for bold text
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]
    \item \texttt{@SpringBootApplication}: Ye annotation Spring Boot ko batata hai ki yeh application ka main class hai.
    \item \texttt{SpringApplication.run()}: Ye method Spring Boot application ko start karta hai.
\end{tcolorbox}

% Horizontal Line
\noindent\rule{\textwidth}{1pt}

% Client Section
\section*{\color{mainblue}\faCode~1️⃣ Feign client (Express.js me External API calls ka kaam)}
�� \textbf{Yeh folder doosre microservices se baat karne ke liye hota hai using \texttt{@FeignClient}} \\
�� \textbf{Express.js Comparison:} Jaise \texttt{axios} ka use hota hai doosre services ko call karne ke liye

\subsection*{Spring Boot Code (With Comments)}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
// Foreign Client ka use karke doosre service se baat karne ke liye interface banaya 
@FeignClient(name = "user-service", url = "http://localhost:8081")  
public interface UserClient {

    // Yeh endpoint `/users/{id}` ko call karega aur user ka data return karega  
    @GetMapping("/users/{id}")  
    UserResponse getUserById(@PathVariable Long id);
}
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{Express.js (Axios ke saath)}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=JavaScript]
const axios = require("axios");

// Function jo doosre service se data lega
async function getUserById(id) {
    const response = await axios.get(`http://localhost:8081/users/${id}`);
    return response.data;
}
\end{lstlisting}

% Title
\title{\color{headingblue}\textbf{Microservices vs Monolithic \& Feign Client vs Axios (Microservices Communication)}}

\begin{document}

\maketitle

% Part 1: Microservices vs Monolithic
\section*{\color{headingblue}Part 1: Microservices vs Monolithic (Comparison)}
\begin{tabular}{|p{4cm}|p{6cm}|p{6cm}|}
    \hline
    \textbf{Feature} & \textbf{Monolithic App} & \textbf{Microservices} \\
    \hline
    \textbf{Architecture} & Ek badi app hoti hai jisme saare modules ek saath hote hain. & Chhoti-chhoti independent services hoti hain jo ek doosre se API ke through baat karti hain. \\
    \hline
    \textbf{Scalability} & Slow, kyunki pura system ek saath scale karna padta hai. & Fast \& Easy, kyunki sirf jo service chahiye wahi scale hoti hai. \\
    \hline
    \textbf{Failure Impact} & Agar ek module fail ho jaye to pura system down ho sakta hai. & Agar ek service fail ho jaye to baaki services kaam karti rahengi. \\
    \hline
    \textbf{Technology Freedom} & Sirf ek hi technology use hoti hai. & Har service alag technology use kar sakti hai (Jaise ek service Node.js aur doosri Python me ho sakti hai). \\
    \hline
    \textbf{Development Speed} & Slow, kyunki ek hi codebase me sab kuch likhna padta hai. & Fast, kyunki alag-alag teams alag services develop kar sakti hain. \\
    \hline
\end{tabular}

\vspace{1em}
\textbf{Example:}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{Monolithic:} Ek single app jo `User`, `Order`, aur `Payment` system ko ek saath manage karti hai.
    \item \textbf{Microservices:} `User Service`, `Order Service`, aur `Payment Service` alag hote hain aur API ke through baat karte hain.
\end{itemize}

% Part 2: Feign Client vs Axios
\section*{\color{headingblue}Part 2: Feign Client vs Axios (Microservices Communication)}
Agar \textbf{Order Service} ko \textbf{User Service} se data lena ho to ye kaise hoga?

\subsection*{1. Feign Client in Spring Boot}
\textbf{Spring Boot me Feign Client use hota hai jo doosre Microservices se baat karta hai bina manually HTTP request likhe.}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
@FeignClient(name = "user-service", url = "http://localhost:8081")
public interface UserClient {
    @GetMapping("/users/{id}")
    UserResponse getUserById(@PathVariable Long id);
}
\end{lstlisting}

\begin{itemize}
    \item \texttt{@FeignClient(name = "user-service")} automatically request send karega.
    \item \texttt{getUserById()} method \texttt{User Service} se user ka data fetch karega.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{2. Axios in Express.js}
\textbf{Express.js me Feign Client nahi hota, isliye Axios ka use hota hai API call ke liye.}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=JavaScript]
const axios = require("axios");

async function getUserById(id) {
    try {
        const response = await axios.get(`http://localhost:8081/users/${id}`);
        return response.data;
    } catch (error) {
        console.error("Error fetching user data:", error);
        return null;
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\begin{itemize}
    \item \texttt{axios.get()} request bhejta hai aur data fetch karta hai.
    \item \texttt{try-catch} block error handle karne ke liye use hota hai.
\end{itemize}

% Comparison Table
\section*{\color{headingblue}Feign Client vs Axios (Comparison Table)}
\begin{tabular}{|p{5cm}|p{5cm}|p{5cm}|}
    \hline
    \textbf{Feature} & \textbf{Feign Client (Spring Boot)} & \textbf{Axios (Express.js)} \\
    \hline
    \textbf{Communication} & Microservices ko easy connect karta hai bina manually HTTP request likhe. & Manually HTTP request likhni padti hai. \\
    \hline
    \textbf{Code Simplicity} & Code simple aur clean hota hai. & Extra HTTP handling likhni padti hai. \\
    \hline
    \textbf{Error Handling} & Spring Boot automatically error handle karta hai. & Manually error handle karna padta hai. \\
    \hline
    \textbf{Performance} & Fast aur optimized. & Extra HTTP request handling overhead hota hai. \\
    \hline
    \textbf{Technology} & Spring Cloud Feign ka use karta hai. & Axios ek external library hai. \\
    \hline
\end{tabular}

% Conclusion
\section*{\color{headingblue}Conclusion}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{Monolithic Apps} simple hoti hain par scale karna mushkil hota hai.
    \item \textbf{Microservices Architecture} independent services banakar scalability aur reliability improve karta hai.
    \item \textbf{Feign Client} (Spring Boot) microservices communication ko easy banata hai bina manually API calls likhe.
    \item \textbf{Axios} (Express.js) manually API request send karta hai, par zyada control deta hai.
\end{itemize}

\section*{\color{headingblue}Real-Life Example}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{Amazon:} Order Service, Payment Service, aur User Service alag hote hain.
    \item \textbf{Netflix:} Movie Service, User Service, aur Recommendation Service alag hote hain.
    \item \textbf{Uber:} Ride Booking, User Management, aur Payment System alag-alag services hain.
\end{itemize}







% Config Section
\section*{\color{mainblue}\faCogs~2️⃣ config (Express.js me Middleware aur Configurations ka kaam)}
�� \textbf{Yeh folder Spring Boot me middleware, security, aur settings store karta hai} \\
�� \textbf{Express.js Comparison:} Jaise \texttt{server.js} me middleware aur configs likhte hain

\subsection*{Spring Boot Code (With Comments)}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
// Configuration class banayi jo Spring Boot ko bataegi ki CORS allow karna hai  
@Configuration
public class CorsConfig {

    @Bean // Bean register kar raha hai jo ek object return karega
    public WebMvcConfigurer corsConfigurer() {
        return new WebMvcConfigurer() {
            @Override
            public void addCorsMappings(CorsRegistry registry) {
                // Sare endpoints ke liye CORS allow karega
                registry.addMapping("/**").allowedOrigins("*");
            }
        };
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{Express.js (Middleware ke saath)}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=JavaScript]
const cors = require("cors");

// Middleware use kiya jo CORS enable karega
app.use(cors());
\end{lstlisting}

% Controller Section
\section*{\color{mainblue}\faRoute~3️⃣ controller (Express.js me Routes/Controllers ka kaam)}
�� \textbf{Yeh request handle karta hai aur REST APIs define karta hai} \\
�� \textbf{Express.js Comparison:} Jaise \texttt{routes/jobRoutes.js} me \texttt{app.get()} use karte hain

\subsection*{Spring Boot Code (With Comments)}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
// REST Controller banaya jo "/jobs" endpoint ko handle karega  
@RestController
@RequestMapping("/jobs")
public class JobController {

    // GET request ko handle karega jo "/jobs/{id}" par aayegi  
    @GetMapping("/{id}")
    public Job getJobById(@PathVariable Long id) {  
        // Service se job ka data leke return karega  
        return jobService.getJobById(id);
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{Express.js (Router)}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=JavaScript]
const express = require("express");
const router = express.Router();

// GET route jo "/jobs/:id" ko handle karega
router.get("/jobs/:id", (req, res) => {
    res.json({ id: req.params.id, title: "Software Engineer" });
});

module.exports = router;
\end{lstlisting}

\title{\textbf{\color{blue} Understanding and Using DTO (Data Transfer Object) in Spring Boot}}
\author{}
\date{}

\begin{document}

\maketitle

\section*{\color{blue} Why Use DTO (Data Transfer Object)?}

DTO ek special class hoti hai jo sirf data transfer ke liye use hoti hai. Iska main kaam hai ki hum sirf wahi data API response me bhejein jo zaroori hai, bina database ka pura object expose kiye.

\subsection*{\color{red} Bina DTO ke Problem}
Agar aap directly \texttt{UserSignupEntity} return karoge toh API response me password jaise sensitive data bhi chala jayega, jo ek bad practice hai.

\subsection*{\color{red} DTO ke Fayde}
\begin{itemize}
    \item Sirf zaroori fields bhejo (e.g., \texttt{success}, \texttt{message}).
    \item Sensitive data hide hota hai, security improve hoti hai.
    \item Code clean aur maintainable banta hai.
\end{itemize}

\section*{\color{blue} DTO Implementation in Spring Boot}

\subsection*{\color{blue} Project Folder Structure}
\begin{lstlisting}[basicstyle=\ttfamily,frame=none]
src/
│── main/java/com/example/demo/
│   ├── controller/    <-- API logic
│   ├── service/       <-- Business logic
│   ├── entity/        <-- Database Entity
│   ├── dto/           <-- DTO Classes
│   ├── repository/    <-- Database Queries
│   ├── DemoApplication.java
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{\color{blue} Step 1: DTO Class Creation}

\textbf{File: \texttt{src/main/java/com/example/demo/dto/ApiResponse.java}}
\begin{lstlisting}[style=javaStyle]
package com.example.demo.dto;

import lombok.AllArgsConstructor;
import lombok.Data;

@Data
@AllArgsConstructor
public class ApiResponse {
    private boolean success;
    private String message;
}
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{\color{blue} Step 2: Controller Update}

\textbf{File: \texttt{src/main/java/com/example/demo/controller/UserController.java}}
\begin{lstlisting}[style=javaStyle]
package com.example.demo.controller;

import com.example.demo.dto.ApiResponse;
import com.example.demo.entity.UserSignupEntity;
import com.example.demo.service.UserSignupService;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.*;

@RestController
@RequestMapping("/api/users")
public class UserController {

    private final UserSignupService userSignupService;

    public UserController(UserSignupService userSignupService) {
        this.userSignupService = userSignupService;
    }

    @PostMapping("/create")
    public ApiResponse createUser(@RequestBody UserSignupEntity user) {
        try {
            userSignupService.registerUser(user);
            return new ApiResponse(true, "User created successfully.");
        } catch (Exception e) {
            return new ApiResponse(false, "User creation failed: " + e.getMessage());
        }
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{\color{blue} Step 3: Service Class Update}

\textbf{File: \texttt{src/main/java/com/example/demo/service/UserSignupService.java}}
\begin{lstlisting}[style=javaStyle]
package com.example.demo.service;

import com.example.demo.entity.UserSignupEntity;
import com.example.demo.repository.UserSignupRepository;
import org.springframework.stereotype.Service;

@Service
public class UserSignupService {

    private final UserSignupRepository userSignupRepository;

    public UserSignupService(UserSignupRepository userSignupRepository) {
        this.userSignupRepository = userSignupRepository;
    }

    public UserSignupEntity registerUser(UserSignupEntity user) {
        return userSignupRepository.save(user);
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{\color{blue} Step 4: Repository Class}

\textbf{File: \texttt{src/main/java/com/example/demo/repository/UserSignupRepository.java}}
\begin{lstlisting}[style=javaStyle]
package com.example.demo.repository;

import com.example.demo.entity.UserSignupEntity;
import org.springframework.data.jpa.repository.JpaRepository;
import org.springframework.stereotype.Repository;

@Repository
public interface UserSignupRepository extends JpaRepository<UserSignupEntity, Long> {
}
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{\color{blue} Step 5: Entity Class Update}

\textbf{File: \texttt{src/main/java/com/example/demo/entity/UserSignupEntity.java}}
\begin{lstlisting}[style=javaStyle]
package com.example.demo.entity;

import jakarta.persistence.*;
import lombok.Getter;
import lombok.Setter;
import java.sql.Timestamp;
import java.time.Instant;

@Entity
@Table(name = "users")
@Getter
@Setter
public class UserSignupEntity {

    @Id
    @GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY)
    private Long id;

    @Column(unique = true, nullable = false, length = 100)
    private String email;

    @Column(nullable = false, length = 255)
    private String password;

    @Column(nullable = false, length = 20)
    private String role;

    @Column(name = "created_at", updatable = false)
    private Timestamp createdAt;

    @PrePersist
    protected void onCreate() {
        this.createdAt = Timestamp.from(Instant.now());
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\section*{\color{blue} API Testing}

\subsection*{\color{blue} Request: POST \texttt{/api/users/create}}
\begin{lstlisting}[style=javaStyle]
{
    "email": "test@gmail.com",
    "password": "123456",
    "role": "user"
}
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{\color{red} ✅ Success Response}
\begin{lstlisting}[style=javaStyle]
{
    "success": true,
    "message": "User created successfully."
}
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{\color{red} ❌ Failure Response}
\begin{lstlisting}[style=javaStyle]
{
    "success": false,
    "message": "User creation failed: Duplicate email found."
}
\end{lstlisting}

\section*{\color{blue} Conclusion}
\begin{itemize}
    \item DTO ka use karke API ka response clean aur secure banaya.
    \item Directly \texttt{UserSignupEntity} return karne se bach gaye.
    \item Service aur Repository classes alag rakhi jo code maintainable banayegi.
    \item Future me easily modify kar sakte hain (DTO structure badal ke).
\end{itemize}





% Entity Section
\section*{\color{mainblue}\faDatabase~5️⃣ entity (Express.js me Mongoose Models ya Sequelize ka kaam)}
�� \textbf{Entity wo class hoti hai jo database table ko represent karti hai} \\
�� \textbf{Express.js Comparison:} Jaise \texttt{Mongoose} models ya \texttt{Sequelize} models use karte hain

\subsection*{Spring Boot Code (With Comments)}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
@Entity // Is class ko DB table ke roop me define kar raha hai  
@Table(name = "jobs") // Table ka naam "jobs" rakha hai  
public class Job {
    @Id
    @GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY) // Auto Increment ID  
    private Long id;
    
    private String title; // Job ka title
}
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{Express.js (Mongoose Model)}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=JavaScript]
const mongoose = require("mongoose");

// Job model banaya jo MongoDB collection ko represent karega
const jobSchema = new mongoose.Schema({
    title: String,
});

const Job = mongoose.model("Job", jobSchema);
\end{lstlisting}

% Enums Section
\section*{\color{mainblue}\faList~6️⃣ enums (Constant values ko define karne ke liye)}
�� \textbf{Enums predefined values store karte hain (e.g., Status, Roles)} \\
�� \textbf{Express.js Comparison:} Jaise \texttt{constants.js} file me constants define karte hain

\subsection*{Spring Boot Code (With Comments)}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
public enum JobStatus {
    ACTIVE, // Job active hai
    CLOSED, // Job closed hai
    PENDING; // Job pending hai
}
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{Express.js (Constants File)}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=JavaScript]
const JOB_STATUS = {
    ACTIVE: "ACTIVE",
    CLOSED: "CLOSED",
    PENDING: "PENDING",
};
\end{lstlisting}

% Exception Section
\section*{\color{mainblue}\faExclamationTriangle~7️⃣ exception (Express.js me Error Handling ka kaam)}
�� \textbf{Custom exceptions aur error handling ke liye hota hai} \\
�� \textbf{Express.js Comparison:} Jaise \texttt{app.use((err, req, res, next) => \{ ... \})}

\subsection*{Spring Boot Code (With Comments)}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
@ResponseStatus(HttpStatus.NOT_FOUND) // 404 error return karega  
public class JobNotFoundException extends RuntimeException {
    public JobNotFoundException(String message) {
        super(message); // Error message set karega  
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{Express.js (Custom Error Middleware)}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=JavaScript]
app.use((err, req, res, next) => {
    res.status(500).json({ error: err.message });
});
\end{lstlisting}
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]
% Resources Section
\section*{\color{mainblue}\faFolder~resources (Static Files, .env, Configs)}
�� \textbf{Yeh folder static files, application properties aur templates store karta hai} \\
�� \textbf{Express.js Comparison:} Jaise \texttt{public/}, \texttt{.env}, \texttt{views/} Express.js me hota hai
\end{tcolorbox}
% Conclusion
\section*{\color{mainblue}\faCheckCircle~Conclusion}
✔ \textbf{Spring Boot me structure alag hai but kaam same hai jo Express.js me hota hai}

===============================

\begin{document}

% Title

\maketitle

% Mapper Section
\section*{\color{mainblue}\faExchange~8️⃣ mapper (Entity ko DTO me convert karna, Express.js me response format change karna)}
�� \textbf{Mapper ka kaam hota hai database entity ko DTO me convert karna aur wapas} \\
�� \textbf{Express.js Comparison:} Jaise manually response ka format change karna

\subsection*{Spring Boot Code (With Comments)}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
// Job entity ko DTO me convert karne ka helper class
public class JobMapper {
    
    // Static method jo Job entity ko JobResponseDTO me convert karega
    public static JobResponseDTO toDTO(Job job) {
        return new JobResponseDTO(job.getId(), job.getTitle());
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
�� \textbf{Yeh kaam har request me karne se bachne ke liye mapper banate hain}

\subsection*{Express.js (Manually Response Map karna)}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=JavaScript]
// Function jo job entity ko response DTO format me change karega
function jobToDTO(job) {
    return { id: job.id, title: job.title };
}

// API route me manually convert karna hoga
app.get("/jobs/:id", async (req, res) => {
    const job = await Job.findById(req.params.id);
    res.json(jobToDTO(job)); // Response format ko DTO banaya
});
\end{lstlisting}
�� \textbf{Express.js me yeh manually har route me karna padta hai, isliye Spring Boot mapper better hai}

% Repository Section
\section*{\color{mainblue}\faDatabase~9️⃣ repository (Database Queries, Express.js me Mongoose ya Sequelize ka kaam)}
�� \textbf{Repository layer DB queries execute karti hai} \\
�� \textbf{Express.js Comparison:} Jaise \texttt{Mongoose.find()} ya \texttt{Sequelize.findAll()} use karte hain

\subsection*{Spring Boot Code (With Comments)}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
// Repository ka kaam DB queries ko handle karna hai
@Repository
public interface JobRepository extends JpaRepository<Job, Long> {
    // JpaRepository CRUD operations provide karega
}
\end{lstlisting}
�� \textbf{Yeh `findById()`, `save()`, `delete()` jaise methods automatically provide karta hai}

\subsection*{Express.js (Mongoose Queries)}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=JavaScript]
// Express.js me Mongoose ka use karke DB se data fetch karna
const jobs = await Job.find();
\end{lstlisting}
�� \textbf{Spring Boot ka `JpaRepository` automatic methods provide karta hai, jabki Express.js me manually likhna padta hai}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]

% Scheduler Section
\section*{\color{mainblue}\faClock~�� scheduler (Background me Periodic Tasks, Express.js me Cron Jobs)}
�� \textbf{Scheduler background me automatically kuch operations run karta hai} \\
�� \textbf{Express.js Comparison:} Jaise \texttt{node-cron} ka use periodic tasks run karne ke liye

\end{tcolorbox}

\subsection*{Spring Boot Code (With Comments)}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
// Scheduler jo har raat 12 baje purane jobs delete karega
@Scheduled(cron = "0 0 * * * ?") // CRON job format (every day at midnight)
public void cleanOldJobs() {
    jobService.deleteOldJobs(); // Service call karke purane jobs delete karega
}
\end{lstlisting}
�� \textbf{Spring Boot me `@Scheduled` annotation se background task run kar sakte hain}

\subsection*{Express.js (Cron Job)}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=JavaScript]
const cron = require("node-cron");

// Har raat 12 baje kaam chalane ke liye cron job setup kiya
cron.schedule("0 0 * * *", () => {
    console.log("Running scheduled task: Deleting old jobs...");
});
\end{lstlisting}
�� \textbf{Express.js me `node-cron` package ka use hota hai}

% Resources Section
\section*{\color{mainblue}\faFolder~resources (Express.js me Views, Static Files, .env ka kaam)}
�� \textbf{Yeh folder static files, application properties aur templates store karta hai} \\
�� \textbf{Express.js Comparison:} Jaise \texttt{public/}, \texttt{.env}, \texttt{views/}

�� \textbf{Spring Boot aur Express.js dono me yeh alag folder me rakha jata hai for better organization}

\subsection*{Spring Boot (`resources/application.properties`)}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=properties]
server.port=8080
spring.datasource.url=jdbc:mysql://localhost:3306/mydb
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{Express.js (`.env` file)}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=env]
PORT=3000
DB_URL=mongodb://localhost:27017/mydb
\end{lstlisting}
�� \textbf{Dono ka kaam same hai, bas syntax alag hai}

% Conclusion
\section*{\color{mainblue}\faCheckCircle~Conclusion}
✔ \textbf{Spring Boot me `mapper`, `repository`, aur `scheduler` alag se define hote hain jo Express.js me manually likhna padta hai} \\
✔ \textbf{Agar aur koi doubt hai ya kisi topic ka aur deep explanation chahiye to batao!} ��

===============================

\begin{document}

% Title
\title{\color{mainblue}\textbf{\faFolderOpen~Spring Boot Annotations Explained}}


% FeignClient Section
\section*{\color{mainblue}\faCode~1. `@FeignClient`}
- \textbf{Spring Boot}: `@FeignClient` ek aisa annotation hai jo aapko dusre microservices ya REST APIs ko easily call karne mein help karta hai. Ye ek tarah ka client banata hai jo dusre service ke saath communicate karta hai.
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
@FeignClient(name = "user-service", url = "http://localhost:8081")
public interface UserServiceClient {
    @GetMapping("/users/{id}")
    User getUserById(@PathVariable Long id);
}
\end{lstlisting}
- `name = "user-service"`: Ye service ka naam hai, jisse aap identify kar sakte hain. \\
- `url = "http://localhost:8081"`: Ye uska base URL hai jahan par ye service available hai.

- \textbf{Express.js mein relate karein}: Express.js mein aap `axios` ya `fetch` use karte hain dusre APIs ko call karne ke liye. `@FeignClient` bhi wahi kaam karta hai, lekin Spring Boot mein ye ek declarative way hai, matlab aapko manually HTTP calls nahi likhne padte, Spring khud handle karta hai.

\documentclass{article}
\usepackage{tcolorbox}
\usepackage{xcolor} % For custom colors
\usepackage{fontawesome} % For icons like \faCode
\usepackage{listings} % For code listings

% Define colors
\definecolor{mainblue}{RGB}{0, 102, 204}

\begin{document}

% PathVariable Section
\section*{\color{mainblue}\faCode~2. `@PathVariable`}
    \item \begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]\textbf{Spring Boot}: `@PathVariable` ka use URL se variable values extract karne ke liye hota hai. Jaise agar aapke paas ek endpoint hai `/users/{id}`, toh `{id}` wala part extract karne ke liye `@PathVariable` use karte hain.
    \begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
@GetMapping("/users/{id}")
public User getUserById(@PathVariable Long id) {
    // id ka use karke user fetch karo
}
    \end{lstlisting}

    \item 
        \textbf{Express.js mein relate karein}: Express.js mein aap `req.params` use karte hain URL se variables extract karne ke liye. Jaise:
        \begin{lstlisting}[language=JavaScript]
app.get('/users/:id', (req, res) => {
    const id = req.params.id;
    // id ka use karke user fetch karo
});
        \end{lstlisting}
    \end{tcolorbox}
\end{itemize}



% GetMapping Section
\section*{\color{mainblue}\faCode~3. `@GetMapping`}
- 
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]
\textbf{Spring Boot}: `@GetMapping` ka use GET request ke liye endpoint define karne ke liye hota hai. Jaise:
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
@GetMapping("/users")
public List<User> getAllUsers() {
    // sab users return karo
}
\end{lstlisting}
- Agar aap `@GetMapping` mein kuch path specify nahi karte, toh ye default route ke liye use hota hai. Matlab agar aapka base URL hai `http://localhost:8080`, toh `@GetMapping` wala method `http://localhost:8080` par GET request handle karega.

- \textbf{Express.js mein relate karein}: Express.js mein aap `app.get()` use karte hain GET request handle karne ke liye. Jaise:
\begin{lstlisting}[language=JavaScript]
app.get('/users', (req, res) => {
    // sab users return karo
});

\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

% PostMapping Section
\section*{\color{mainblue}\faCode~4. `@PostMapping`}
- 
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]
\textbf{Spring Boot}: `@PostMapping` ka use POST request ke liye endpoint define karne ke liye hota hai. Jaise:
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
@PostMapping("/users")
public User createUser(@RequestBody User user) {
    // user ko create karo
}
\end{lstlisting}

- \textbf{Express.js mein relate karein}: Express.js mein aap `app.post()` use karte hain POST request handle karne ke liye. Jaise:
\begin{lstlisting}[language=JavaScript]
app.post('/users', (req, res) => {
    const user = req.body;
    // user ko create karo
});
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

% GetMapping without Path Section
\section*{\color{mainblue}\faCode~5. `@GetMapping` without path}
-
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]\textbf{Spring Boot}: Agar aap `@GetMapping` mein koi specific path specify nahi karte, toh ye default route ke liye use hota hai. Matlab agar aapka base URL hai `http://localhost:8080`, toh `@GetMapping` wala method `http://localhost:8080` par GET request handle karega.
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
@GetMapping
public String home() {
    return "Welcome to the home page!";
}
\end{lstlisting}


- \textbf{Express.js mein relate karein}: Express.js mein aap `app.get('/')` use karte hain root route ke liye. Jaise:
\begin{lstlisting}[language=JavaScript]
app.get('/', (req, res) => {
    res.send('Welcome to the home page!');
});
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

% PostMapping without Path Section
\section*{\color{mainblue}\faCode~6. `@PostMapping` without path}
- 
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]\textbf{Spring Boot}: Agar aap `@PostMapping` mein koi specific path specify nahi karte, toh ye default route ke liye use hota hai. Matlab agar aapka base URL hai `http://localhost:8080`, toh `@PostMapping` wala method `http://localhost:8080` par POST request handle karega.
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
@PostMapping
public String createSomething(@RequestBody SomeObject obj) {
    // kuch create karo
}
\end{lstlisting}

- \textbf{Express.js mein relate karein}: Express.js mein aap `app.post('/')` use karte hain root route ke liye POST request handle karne ke liye. Jaise:
\begin{lstlisting}[language=JavaScript]
app.post('/', (req, res) => {
    const obj = req.body;
    // kuch create karo
});
\end{lstlisting}

% Summary Section
\section*{\color{mainblue}\faCheckCircle~Summary}
- `@FeignClient` -> Express.js mein `axios` ya `fetch` ki tarah hai, lekin declarative way mein. \\
- `@PathVariable` -> Express.js mein `req.params` ki tarah hai. \\
- `@GetMapping` -> Express.js mein `app.get()` ki tarah hai. \\
- `@PostMapping` -> Express.js mein `app.post()` ki tarah hai. \\
- `@GetMapping` aur `@PostMapping` without path -> Express.js mein root route (`'/'`) ke liye use hota hai.
\end{tcolorbox}

===============================
\hrule



\title{\textbf{Spring Boot vs Express.js: Missing Topics in Real-life Projects}}
\author{}
\date{}

\begin{document}
\maketitle

\section*{\textcolor{blue}{\huge Missing Topics in Your Notes}}
\textbf{Real-life Spring Boot projects} me jo topics zaroori hain, unko Express.js se relate karke samjhaya gaya hai. Har line ka breakdown bhi diya gaya hai. 

\section*{\textcolor{blue}{\LARGE 1. Application Layer Architecture}}
Spring Boot me projects ek \textbf{specific architecture} follow karte hain:
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{MVC (Model-View-Controller)}
    \item \textbf{3-Tier Architecture (Controller → Service → Repository)}
    \item \textbf{Hexagonal Architecture (Port \\& Adapter Model)}
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{\textcolor{red}{Spring Boot - 3-Tier Architecture}}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java,frame=single,breaklines=true]
@RestController
@RequestMapping("/users")
public class UserController {
    @Autowired  
    private UserService userService;

    @GetMapping("/{id}")
    public User getUserById(@PathVariable Long id) {
        return userService.getUserById(id);
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{\textcolor{red}{Express.js - Same Structure}}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=JavaScript,frame=single,breaklines=true]
// Controller
app.get("/users/:id", async (req, res) => {
    const user = await userService.getUserById(req.params.id);
    res.json(user);
});
\end{lstlisting}

\section*{\textcolor{blue}{\LARGE 2. Security (Spring Security, JWT, OAuth2)}}
\textcolor{red}{\textbf{Authentication aur authorization real-world applications me mandatory hoti hai!}}

\subsection*{\textcolor{red}{Spring Boot - JWT Implementation}}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java,frame=single,breaklines=true]
@Service
public class JwtUtil {
    private static final String SECRET_KEY = "mySecretKey";

    public String generateToken(String username) {
        return Jwts.builder()
                .setSubject(username)
                .setIssuedAt(new Date())
                .setExpiration(new Date(System.currentTimeMillis() + 86400000))
                .signWith(SignatureAlgorithm.HS256, SECRET_KEY)
                .compact();
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{\textcolor{red}{Express.js - JWT Implementation}}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=JavaScript,frame=single,breaklines=true]
const jwt = require("jsonwebtoken");
function generateToken(username) {
    return jwt.sign({ username }, "mySecretKey", { expiresIn: "1d" });
}
\end{lstlisting}

\section*{\textcolor{blue}{\LARGE 3. Global Exception Handling}}
\textcolor{red}{\textbf{Production-level applications me centralized error handling zaroori hota hai!}}

\subsection*{\textcolor{red}{Spring Boot - Global Exception Handler}}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java,frame=single,breaklines=true]
@ControllerAdvice
public class GlobalExceptionHandler {
    @ExceptionHandler(RuntimeException.class)
    public ResponseEntity<String> handleRuntimeException(RuntimeException e) {
        return new ResponseEntity<>(e.getMessage(), HttpStatus.INTERNAL_SERVER_ERROR);
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{\textcolor{red}{Express.js - Error Middleware}}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=JavaScript,frame=single,breaklines=true]
app.use((err, req, res, next) => {
    res.status(500).json({ error: err.message });
});
\end{lstlisting}

\section*{\textcolor{blue}{\LARGE 4. Docker \& Deployment}}
\textcolor{red}{\textbf{Real-world applications ko containerized aur deploy karna ek must-have skill hai!}}

\subsection*{\textcolor{red}{Spring Boot - Dockerfile}}
\begin{lstlisting}[frame=single,breaklines=true]
FROM openjdk:17
WORKDIR /app
COPY target/myapp.jar myapp.jar
CMD ["java", "-jar", "myapp.jar"]
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{\textcolor{red}{Express.js - Dockerfile}}
\begin{lstlisting}[frame=single,breaklines=true]
FROM node:16
WORKDIR /app
COPY package.json ./
RUN npm install
COPY . .
CMD ["node", "server.js"]
\end{lstlisting}

\section*{\textcolor{blue}{\LARGE 5. Logging \& Monitoring}}
\textcolor{red}{\textbf{Logs aur monitoring real-time debugging ke liye crucial hote hain!}}

\subsection*{\textcolor{red}{Spring Boot - Logging}}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java,frame=single,breaklines=true]
import org.slf4j.Logger;
import org.slf4j.LoggerFactory;

@RestController
public class JobController {
    private static final Logger logger = LoggerFactory.getLogger(JobController.class);

    @GetMapping("/jobs/{id}")
    public Job getJobById(@PathVariable Long id) {
        logger.info("Fetching job with id: " + id);
        return jobService.getJobById(id);
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{\textcolor{red}{Express.js - Logging with Morgan}}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=JavaScript,frame=single,breaklines=true]
const morgan = require("morgan");
app.use(morgan("dev"));
\end{lstlisting}

\definecolor{bluecolor}{RGB}{0, 0, 139}
\definecolor{redcolor}{RGB}{255, 0, 0}
\definecolor{codebg}{RGB}{240, 240, 240}

\lstset{
    backgroundcolor=\color{codebg},
    basicstyle=\ttfamily\footnotesize,
    keywordstyle=\color{blue},
    commentstyle=\color{red},
    stringstyle=\color{red},
    breaklines=true,
    frame=single,
}

\begin{document}

\title{\textbf{\huge \textcolor{bluecolor}{Annotations in Spring Boot}}}
\date{}
\maketitle

\section{\textcolor{bluecolor}{1. @Configuration}}
\subsection*{Kya Hai Ye?}
\texttt{@Configuration} ek annotation hai jo Spring Boot ko batata hai ki ye class ek configuration file ki tarah kaam karegi jisme hum beans define kar sakte hain.

\subsection*{Agar Hum Na Dein Toh Kya Hoga?}
\textcolor{redcolor}{Agar @Configuration nahi diya toh Spring is class ko ek configuration file nahi samjhega aur @Bean methods execute nahi karega.}

\subsection*{Example:}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
@Configuration
public class AppConfig {
    @Bean
    public MyService myService() {
        return new MyService();
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\section{\textcolor{bluecolor}{2. @EnableFeignClients}}
\subsection*{Kya Hai Ye?}
Feign ek declarative REST client hai jo external APIs se connect hone ke liye use hota hai.

\subsection*{Agar Hum Na Dein Toh Kya Hoga?}
\textcolor{redcolor}{Agar ye annotation na ho toh Feign clients kaam nahi karenge aur API calls fail ho jayengi.}

\subsection*{Example:}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
@EnableFeignClients(basePackages = "com.aidiph.api.central.client")
public class MyApplication {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        SpringApplication.run(MyApplication.class, args);
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\section{\textcolor{bluecolor}{3. @EnableWebSecurity aur @EnableMethodSecurity}}
\subsection*{Kya Hai Ye?}
\texttt{@EnableWebSecurity} authentication aur authorization handle karta hai.
\texttt{@EnableMethodSecurity} method-level security enable karta hai.

\subsection*{Agar Hum Na Dein Toh Kya Hoga?}
\textcolor{redcolor}{Agar ye annotations nahi diye toh security disable ho jayegi aur endpoints unprotected rahenge.}

\subsection*{Example:}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
@EnableWebSecurity
@EnableMethodSecurity
public class SecurityConfig extends WebSecurityConfigurerAdapter {
    @Override
    protected void configure(HttpSecurity http) throws Exception {
        http.authorizeRequests().anyRequest().authenticated();
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\section{\textcolor{bluecolor}{4. @SecurityRequirement}}
\subsection*{Kya Hai Ye?}
Swagger documentation me batata hai ki API ko authorization ki zaroorat hai.

\subsection*{Agar Hum Na Dein Toh Kya Hoga?}
\textcolor{redcolor}{Swagger me API ke liye authorization ka option nahi dikhega.}

\subsection*{Example:}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
@SecurityRequirement(name = "Authorization")
public class MyController {
    // API methods
}
\end{lstlisting}

\section{\textcolor{bluecolor}{5. @RequestMapping}}
\subsection*{Kya Hai Ye?}
Isse hum ek class ya method ke liye URL define kar sakte hain jo HTTP request handle karega.

\subsection*{Agar Hum Na Dein Toh Kya Hoga?}
\textcolor{redcolor}{Agar @RequestMapping nahi diya toh Spring Boot request ko is controller se match nahi karega aur error milega 404 Not Found.}

\subsection*{Example:}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
@RestController
@RequestMapping(value = "central/permissions")
public class PermissionController {
    @GetMapping
    public List<Permission> getPermissions() {
        return List.of(new Permission("READ"), new Permission("WRITE"));
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}





\definecolor{blue}{RGB}{0, 0, 255}
\definecolor{red}{RGB}{0, 150, 0}
\definecolor{red}{RGB}{200, 0, 0}
\definecolor{lightgray}{RGB}{240, 240, 240}

\newtcolorbox{mybox}{colback=lightgray,colframe=black,arc=5pt}

\lstset{
  basicstyle=\ttfamily\small,
  backgroundcolor=\color{lightgray},
  keywordstyle=\color{blue}\bfseries,
  commentstyle=\color{red},
  stringstyle=\color{red},
  frame=single,
  breaklines=true,
  showstringspaces=false
}

\title{\textbf{Miscellaneous Annotations in Spring Boot}}
\author{}
\date{}

\begin{document}
\maketitle

\section{\textcolor{blue}{Miscellaneous Annotations}}

\subsection{\textbf{@Slf4j}}
\textcolor{red}{\textbf{✅ Kya Hai Ye?}} 
\\ \texttt{@Slf4j} ek Lombok annotation hai jo \textbf{automatic logging setup} karta hai. Isse \texttt{log.info()} aur \texttt{log.error()} jaise logging methods bina manually \texttt{Logger} banaye use ho sakte hain.

\textcolor{red}{\textbf{�� Agar Na Dein Toh Kya Hoga?}}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \texttt{log.info("Message")} ya \texttt{log.error("Error")} likhne par \textbf{error aayega} kyunki logger define nahi hoga.
    \item Har class me \textbf{manually logger setup} karna padega jo \textbf{time-consuming} hoga.
\end{itemize}

\textcolor{red}{\textbf{✅ Example:}}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
@Slf4j
public class MyClass {
    public void test() {
        log.info("This is a log message.");
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\textcolor{red}{\textbf{�� Agar @Slf4j Na Ho:}}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
public class MyClass {
    private static final Logger log = LoggerFactory.getLogger(MyClass.class);
    
    public void test() {
        log.info("This is a log message.");
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

---
\subsection{\textbf{@Validated}}
\textcolor{red}{\textbf{✅ Kya Hai Ye?}}
\\ 
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]
\texttt{@Validated} annotation \textbf{Spring Boot ke validation framework} ko enable karta hai. Isse hum input data ko validate kar sakte hain bina manually \texttt{if-else} check likhe.

\textcolor{red}{\textbf{�� Agar Na Dein Toh Kya Hoga?}}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \texttt{@Valid} ya \texttt{@NotNull} jaise annotations \textbf{kaam nahi karenge}.
    \item Invalid data ko manually check karna padega using \texttt{if-else}.
\end{itemize}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textcolor{red}{\textbf{✅ Example:}}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
@Validated
public class UserController {
    public ResponseEntity<?> createUser(@Valid @RequestBody UserRequest request) {
        // Handle request
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

---
\subsection{\textbf{@RestController}}
\textcolor{red}{\textbf{✅ Kya Hai Ye?}} 
\\ \texttt{@RestController} \textbf{Spring Boot me API endpoints create karne} ke liye use hota hai.

\textcolor{red}{\textbf{�� Agar Na Dein Toh Kya Hoga?}}
\begin{itemize}
    \item Agar sirf \texttt{@Controller} likha aur \texttt{@ResponseBody} nahi diya toh \textbf{method ka return HTML page render karne ki koshish karega}.
    \item API request ke response me \textbf{JSON return nahi hoga}.
\end{itemize}

\textcolor{red}{\textbf{✅ Example:}}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
@RestController
@RequestMapping("/users")
public class UserController {
    @GetMapping
    public String getUser() {
        return "Hello User";
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

---
\subsection{\textbf{@RequiredArgsConstructor}}
\textcolor{red}{\textbf{✅ Kya Hai Ye?}} 
\\ Lombok annotation hai jo \texttt{final} fields ke liye \textbf{automatic constructor generate} karta hai.

\textcolor{red}{\textbf{�� Agar Na Dein Toh Kya Hoga?}}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{Hume manually constructor likhna padega} jisme \texttt{final} fields ka initialization karein.
    \item Agar \textbf{class me multiple dependencies ho}, toh manually constructor likhna \textbf{tedious ho sakta hai}.
\end{itemize}

\textcolor{red}{\textbf{✅ Example:}}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
@RequiredArgsConstructor
public class UserService {
    private final UserRepository userRepository;
}
\end{lstlisting}

---
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]
\subsection{\textbf{@CrossOrigin}}
\textcolor{red}{\textbf{✅ Kya Hai Ye?}}
\\ \texttt{@CrossOrigin} \textbf{CORS (Cross-Origin Resource Sharing)} enable karta hai. 

\textcolor{red}{\textbf{�� Agar Na Dein Toh Kya Hoga?}}
\begin{itemize}
    \item Frontend agar alag server pe chal raha hai toh \textbf{CORS error aayega}.
    \item Browser request ko \textbf{block} kar dega.
\end{itemize}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textcolor{red}{\textbf{✅ Example:}}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
@CrossOrigin(origins = "*", allowedHeaders = "*")
@RestController
public class MyController {
    @GetMapping("/data")
    public String getData() {
        return "Hello";
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\section{\textcolor{blue}{�� Conclusion}}
Yeh miscellaneous annotations \textbf{Spring Boot applications ko maintainable aur efficient banati hain}.

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]

\textbf{�� Agar hum inhe na dein toh:}
\begin{itemize}
    \item Logging \textbf{manually setup} karna padega \texttt{@Slf4j} na hone par.
    \item Input validation \textbf{manually handle} karni padegi \texttt{@Validated} na hone par.
    \item JSON response \textbf{properly return nahi hoga} \texttt{@RestController} na hone par.
    \item \textbf{Constructor manually likhna padega} \texttt{@RequiredArgsConstructor} na hone par.
    \item \textbf{CORS error aayega} \texttt{@CrossOrigin} na hone par.
\end{itemize}
\end{tcolorbox}



\title{\textbf{\huge Spring Boot vs Express.js Annotations}}
\author{}
\date{}

\begin{document}

\maketitle

\section*{\textcolor{blue}{7. @Operation, @ApiResponses, @ApiResponse}}

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Spring Boot Explanation:}}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{@Operation}: Ye annotation Swagger/OpenAPI documentation ke liye hoti hai. Isse aap API endpoint ko describe kar sakte ho, jaise ki summary aur description dena.
    \item \textbf{@ApiResponses}: Ye annotation ek list hoti hai jo aapke API ke possible responses ko specify karti hai.
    \item \textbf{@ApiResponse}: Ye annotation ek specific response ko define karti hai, jaise response code aur description.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Express.js Comparison:}} Express.js mein, jab aap API banate ho, tab aap comments ya Swagger jaise tools ka use karte ho API documentation ke liye.

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Code Example:}}
\begin{verbatim}
@Operation(summary = "Add User Career Profile", description = "Creates a new user career profile.")
@ApiResponses(value = {
    @ApiResponse(responseCode = "201", description = "User career profile created successfully."),
    @ApiResponse(responseCode = "400", description = "Invalid request body."),
    @ApiResponse(responseCode = "401", description = "Unauthorized access."),
    @ApiResponse(responseCode = "403", description = "Access forbidden.")
})
@PostMapping
public ResponseEntity<?> createCareerProfile(@RequestBody UserCareerProfileRequest request) {
    // Career profile create karna ka logic yahan likhenge
}
\end{verbatim}

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Without these annotations:}} Agar ye annotations nahi diye to Swagger ya OpenAPI documentation me aapka API describe nahi hoga. Yeh annotations documentation generate karne mein madad karte hain, taaki frontend developer ko samajh aaye ki API kaise use karna hai aur expected responses kya hain.

\section*{\textcolor{blue}{8. @RequestBody}}

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Spring Boot Explanation:}}
\begin{itemize}
    \item Ye annotation HTTP request body ko Java object ke sath bind karne ke liye use hota hai. Jab aap POST request bhejte ho aur body me data send karte ho, tab Spring us data ko object me convert karta hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Express.js Comparison:}} Express.js mein aap \texttt{req.body} ka use karte ho, jo ki body data ko fetch karta hai.

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Code Example:}}
\begin{verbatim}
@PostMapping
public ResponseEntity<?> createCareerProfile(@RequestBody UserCareerProfileRequest request) {
    // Career profile create karna ka logic
}
\end{verbatim}

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Without this annotation:}} Agar \texttt{@RequestBody} annotation nahi use karoge, to Spring Boot request ke body ko object me convert nahi karega, aur aapko manually parsing karna padega, jo kaafi complex ho sakta hai.

\section*{\textcolor{blue}{9. @Getter, @Setter, @NoArgsConstructor, @AllArgsConstructor}}

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Spring Boot Explanation:}}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{@Getter}: Ye Lombok annotation automatically class ke fields ke liye getter methods generate karta hai.
    \item \textbf{@Setter}: Ye Lombok annotation automatically setter methods generate karta hai.
    \item \textbf{@NoArgsConstructor}: Ye constructor bina kisi argument ke generate karta hai.
    \item \textbf{@AllArgsConstructor}: Ye saare fields ke liye constructor generate karta hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Express.js Comparison:}} Express.js mein aapko manually getters, setters, aur constructors define karne padte hain.

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Code Example:}}
\begin{verbatim}
@Getter
@Setter
@NoArgsConstructor
@AllArgsConstructor
public class UserCareerProfileRequest {
    private String userId;
    private String careerDetails;
}
\end{verbatim}

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Without these annotations:}} Agar aap ye annotations use nahi karte, to aapko manually getters, setters, aur constructors likhne padenge. Yeh code ko bohot verbose bana deta hai.

\section*{\textcolor{blue}{10. @Schema(description = "Current page number")}}

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Spring Boot Explanation:}}
\begin{itemize}
    \item Ye annotation Swagger/OpenAPI documentation me field ke description ko add karta hai. Isse aap model ki fields ko achhe se document kar sakte ho.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Express.js Comparison:}} Express.js mein aap comments ya Swagger annotations ka use karte ho field description dene ke liye.

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Code Example:}}
\begin{verbatim}
public class PaginationRequest {
    @Schema(description = "Current page number")
    private int page;
}
\end{verbatim}

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Without this annotation:}} Agar aap ye annotation nahi denge, to Swagger/OpenAPI documentation me us field ka description nahi dikhayi dega, jo ki documentation ko samajhne mein problem create kar sakta hai.

\section*{\textcolor{blue}{11. @EntityListeners(AuditingEntityListener.class), @CreatedDate, @CreatedBy, @LastModifiedBy, @LastModifiedDate}}

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Spring Boot Explanation:}}
\begin{itemize}
    \item Ye annotations auditing ke liye hoti hain, jo ki entity ke creation aur modification time ko automatically track karti hain. Jaise hi koi entity create ya update hoti hai, yeh fields automatically populate ho jaati hain.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Express.js Comparison:}} Express.js mein aapko manually yeh fields set karne padte hain jab record create ya update hota hai.

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Code Example:}}
\begin{verbatim}
@EntityListeners(AuditingEntityListener.class)
public class User {
    @CreatedDate
    private LocalDateTime createdDate;

    @CreatedBy
    private String createdBy;

    @LastModifiedBy
    private String lastModifiedBy;

    @LastModifiedDate
    private LocalDateTime lastModifiedDate;
}
\end{verbatim}

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Without these annotations:}} Agar aap ye annotations nahi use karte, to aapko manually created date, modified date, created by, aur modified by ko set karna padega har time jab entity create ya update hoti hai.

\section*{\textcolor{blue}{12. @ControllerAdvice, @ExceptionHandler(ConstraintViolationException.class)}}

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Spring Boot Explanation:}}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{@ControllerAdvice}: Ye global exception handling ke liye use hota hai. Aap isme ek centralized error handling mechanism define kar sakte ho.
    \item \textbf{@ExceptionHandler}: Ye specific exception ko handle karne ke liye use hota hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Express.js Comparison:}} Express.js mein aap middleware ka use karte ho error handling ke liye.

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Code Example:}}
\begin{verbatim}
@ControllerAdvice
public class GlobalExceptionHandler {
    @ExceptionHandler(ConstraintViolationException.class)
    public ResponseEntity<?> handleConstraintViolation(ConstraintViolationException ex) {
        return ResponseEntity.badRequest().body(ex.getMessage());
    }
}
\end{verbatim}

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Without these annotations:}} Agar yeh annotations nahi use karoge, to aapko har controller mein exception handling manually likhni padegi, jo code ko repetitive aur error-prone bana sakta hai.

\section*{\textcolor{blue}{13. @Serial}}

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Spring Boot Explanation:}}
\begin{itemize}
    \item Ye annotation Java serialization ke liye hota hai, jo ki object ko byte stream me convert karta hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Express.js Comparison:}} Express.js mein aap JSON.stringify aur JSON.parse ka use karte ho serialization ke liye.

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Code Example:}}
\begin{verbatim}
public class MyClass implements Serializable {
    @Serial
    private static final long serialVersionUID = 1L;
}
\end{verbatim}

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Without this annotation:}} Agar aap yeh annotation use nahi karte, to serialization ke liye aapko manual configuration karni padegi.

\section*{\textcolor{blue}{14. @Component}}

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Spring Boot Explanation:}}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{@Component}: Is annotation ka use kisi bhi class ko Spring container ke under ek bean banane ke liye hota hai, jisse Spring automatically detect aur register kar leta hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Express.js Comparison:}} Express.js mein aap manually modules ko \texttt{require} karte ho.

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Code Example:}}
\begin{verbatim}
@Component
public class MyService {
    // Business logic yahan
}
\end{verbatim}

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Without this annotation:}} Agar yeh annotation nahi hota, to Spring ko ye class automatically detect nahi hoti, aur aapko manually isse register karna padega.

\section*{\textcolor{blue}{15. @ImportAutoConfiguration}}

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Spring Boot Explanation:}}
\begin{itemize}
    \item Ye annotation Spring Boot ko automatically configuration classes ko import karne ka permission deta hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Express.js Comparison:}} Express.js mein aapko manually middleware aur plugins configure karne padte hain.

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Code Example:}}
\begin{verbatim}
@ImportAutoConfiguration({MyConfiguration.class})
public class MyApplication {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        SpringApplication.run(MyApplication.class, args);
    }
}
\end{verbatim}

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Without this annotation:}} Agar aap yeh annotation nahi use karte, to aapko manually configuration ko handle karna padega, jo development process ko slow kar sakta hai.

===============================
\hrule

\definecolor{examplered}{RGB}{0, 153, 76}
\definecolor{warningred}{RGB}{204, 0, 0}
\definecolor{codebg}{RGB}{173, 216, 230}
\definecolor{tablered}{RGB}{144, 238, 144}

\lstset{
    backgroundcolor=\color{codebg},
    basicstyle=\ttfamily\small,
    breaklines=true,
    frame=single,
    language=Java,
    keywordstyle=\color{blue},
    commentstyle=\color{red},
    stringstyle=\color{red},
    showstringspaces=false,
    tabsize=4
}

\newtcolorbox{examplebox}[1]{
