% Title Page
\title{\textbf{\color{headingblue}Spring Boot JPA Relationships Explained in Hinglish}}


\begin{document}

\maketitle

% Introduction
\section*{\color{headingblue}Introduction}
Spring Boot mein \texttt{@ManyToOne}, \texttt{@OneToMany}, \texttt{@OneToOne}, aur \texttt{@ManyToMany} annotations ka use \textbf{entity relationships} define karne ke liye hota hai. Agar tum naye ho toh main har ek cheez step by step samjhata hoon.

\subsection*{Hinglish Explanation}
Spring Boot mein \texttt{JPA} aur \texttt{Hibernate} ka use karke hum tables (entities) ko relational database mein connect kar sakte hain. Is document mein hum 4 types ke relationships ko samjhenge.

% Spring Boot JPA Relationships Basics
\section*{\color{headingblue}Spring Boot JPA Relationships Basics}
Spring Boot mein agar humein \textbf{do tables (entities) ko relational database mein connect} karna ho, toh hum \textbf{JPA (Java Persistence API) aur Hibernate} ka use karte hain.

JPA relationships ke 4 types hote hain:

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]

\begin{enumerate}
    \item \textbf{\color{headingblue}@OneToOne} → Ek table ka ek row doosri table ke ek row se connected hota hai.
    \item \textbf{\color{headingblue}@OneToMany} → Ek table ka ek row doosri table ke \textbf{multiple rows} se connected hota hai.
    \item \textbf{\color{headingblue}@ManyToOne} → Multiple rows ek hi table ke ek row se connected hote hain.
    \item \textbf{\color{headingblue}@ManyToMany} → Dono tables ke multiple rows ek doosre se connected hote hain.
\end{enumerate}


\subsection*{Hinglish Explanation}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \texttt{@OneToOne}: Ek student ka sirf ek address ho sakta hai.
    \item \texttt{@OneToMany}: Ek school ke bahut saare students ho sakte hain.
    \item \texttt{@ManyToOne}: Bahut saare students ek hi school mein ho sakte hain.
    \item \texttt{@ManyToMany}: Ek student multiple courses le sakta hai aur ek course multiple students ke liye ho sakta hai.
\end{itemize}
\end{tcolorbox}

% Understanding @ManyToOne
\section*{\color{headingblue}1. Understanding `@ManyToOne` (Many-to-One Relationship)}
`@ManyToOne` ka matlab hai \textbf{bahut saare students ek hi school ke under aayenge.}

\subsection*{Example: School aur Student Relationship}
\begin{examplebox}{Java Code: School Entity}
\begin{lstlisting}
import jakarta.persistence.*;

@Entity
public class School {
    @Id
    @GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY)  // Auto increment ID
    private Long id;
    private String name;
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

\begin{examplebox}{Java Code: Student Entity}
\begin{lstlisting}
import jakarta.persistence.*;

@Entity
public class Student {
    @Id
    @GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY)  // Auto increment ID
    private Long id;
    private String name;

    @ManyToOne
    @JoinColumn(name = "school_id")  // Foreign key column in Student table
    private School school;
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

\subsection*{Generated Database Tables}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=SQL, basicstyle=\ttfamily\small, keywordstyle=\color{blue}]
CREATE TABLE school (
    id BIGINT AUTO_INCREMENT PRIMARY KEY,
    name VARCHAR(255)
);

CREATE TABLE student (
    id BIGINT AUTO_INCREMENT PRIMARY KEY,
    name VARCHAR(255),
    school_id BIGINT,
    FOREIGN KEY (school_id) REFERENCES school(id)
);
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{Hinglish Explanation}
Yahan \texttt{@ManyToOne} ka matlab hai ki ek student ek school se belong karta hai. \texttt{school\_id} foreign key banega \texttt{student} table mein.

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]

\subsection*{Q: Agar `@ManyToOne` na likhein toh kya hoga?}
Agar `@ManyToOne` \textbf{nahi likha}, toh `school` field sirf ek normal variable ban jayega, aur \textbf{database mein foreign key nahi banegi.}

\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{examplebox}{Java Code: Without @ManyToOne}
\begin{lstlisting}
@Entity
public class Student {
    @Id
    @GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY)
    private Long id;
    private String name;

    private School school;  // ❌ Foreign key nahi banegi
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

\subsection*{Hinglish Explanation}
Is case mein **Hibernate `school\_id` column create nahi karega**, aur relation ka data manually manage karna padega.

% Understanding @OneToMany
\section*{\color{headingblue}2. Understanding `@OneToMany` (One-to-Many Relationship)}
`@OneToMany` ka matlab hai \textbf{ek school ke multiple students honge.}

\begin{examplebox}{Java Code: School Entity with @OneToMany}
\begin{lstlisting}
import java.util.List;
import jakarta.persistence.*;

@Entity
public class School {
    @Id
    @GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY)
    private Long id;
    private String name;

    @OneToMany(mappedBy = "school")  // Connect with Student entity
    private List<Student> students;
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]

\subsection*{Hinglish Explanation}
\texttt{mappedBy = "school"} ka matlab hai yeh field \texttt{Student} table ke \texttt{school} field se connected hai. Iska direct foreign key column nahi banta, kyunki ye ek reverse mapping hai.

\end{tcolorbox}

% Understanding @OneToOne
\section*{\color{headingblue}3. Understanding `@OneToOne` (One-to-One Relationship)}
Ek student ka sirf ek address ho sakta hai.

\begin{examplebox}{Java Code: Address Entity}
\begin{lstlisting}
@Entity
public class Address {
    @Id
    @GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY)
    private Long id;
    private String city;
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

\begin{examplebox}{Java Code: Student Entity with @OneToOne}
\begin{lstlisting}
@Entity
public class Student {
    @Id
    @GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY)
    private Long id;
    private String name;

    @OneToOne
    @JoinColumn(name = "address_id")  // Foreign key
    private Address address;
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]

\subsection*{Hinglish Explanation}
\texttt{address\_id} foreign key banega \texttt{student} table mein.

\end{tcolorbox}

% Understanding @ManyToMany
\section*{\color{headingblue}4. Understanding `@ManyToMany` (Many-to-Many Relationship)}
Ek student multiple courses le sakta hai aur ek course multiple students ke liye ho sakta hai.

\begin{examplebox}{Java Code: Student Entity with @ManyToMany}
\begin{lstlisting}
import java.util.List;
import jakarta.persistence.*;

@Entity
public class Student {
    @Id
    @GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY)
    private Long id;
    private String name;

    @ManyToMany
    @JoinTable(
        name = "student_course",
        joinColumns = @JoinColumn(name = "student_id"),
        inverseJoinColumns = @JoinColumn(name = "course_id")
    )
    private List<Course> courses;
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

\begin{examplebox}{Java Code: Course Entity}
\begin{lstlisting}
@Entity
public class Course {
    @Id
    @GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY)
    private Long id;
    private String courseName;

    @ManyToMany(mappedBy = "courses")
    private List<Student> students;
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

\subsection*{Generated SQL Table}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=SQL, basicstyle=\ttfamily\small, keywordstyle=\color{blue}]
CREATE TABLE student_course (
    student_id BIGINT,
    course_id BIGINT,
    FOREIGN KEY (student_id) REFERENCES student(id),
    FOREIGN KEY (course_id) REFERENCES course(id)
);
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{Hinglish Explanation}
\texttt{student\_course} naam ka ek extra table banega, jo \texttt{student\_id} aur \texttt{course\_id} ko connect karega.

% Conclusion
\section*{\color{headingblue}Conclusion (Summary)}
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{|>{\columncolor{headingblue!20}}p{4cm}|>{\columncolor{examplered!20}}p{4cm}|>{\columncolor{yellow!20}}p{4cm}|}
    \hline
    \rowcolor{headingblue!30}
    \textbf{Annotation} & \textbf{Description} & \textbf{Foreign Key Generated?} \\
    \hline
    \texttt{@OneToOne} & Ek row doosri table ke ek row se connected & \textcolor{examplered}{Yes} \\
    \hline
    \texttt{@OneToMany} & Ek row doosri table ke multiple rows se connected & \textcolor{warningred}{No} \\
    \hline
    \texttt{@ManyToOne} & Multiple rows ek row se connected & \textcolor{examplered}{Yes} \\
    \hline
    \texttt{@ManyToMany} & Multiple rows ek doosre se connected & \textcolor{examplered}{Yes} \\
    \hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\subsection*{Hinglish Explanation}
Yeh table batata hai ki konse relationship mein foreign key banegi aur konse mein nahi.

% Additional Explanation for Beginners

\section*{\color{headingblue}Additional Explanation for Beginners}
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]
    \item \textbf{\color{headingblue}@JoinColumn(name = "school\_id")}: Yeh annotation batata hai ki \texttt{student} table mein ek column banega jiska naam \texttt{school\_id} hoga aur yeh \texttt{school} table ke \texttt{id} column se connect hoga.
    \item \textbf{\color{headingblue}@GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY)}: Yeh annotation batata hai ki \texttt{id} column auto-increment hogi.
    \item \textbf{\color{headingblue}@Entity}: Yeh annotation batata hai ki yeh class ek database table ko represent karti hai.
    \item \textbf{\color{headingblue}@Id}: Yeh annotation batata hai ki yeh field table ka primary key hai.
    \item \textbf{\color{headingblue}@OneToMany(mappedBy = "school")}: Yeh annotation batata hai ki \texttt{students} list \texttt{Student} entity ke \texttt{school} field se connected hai.


% Real-Life Example
\section*{\color{headingblue}Real-Life Example}
Imagine you are building a school management system:
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{School} aur \textbf{Student} ka \texttt{@ManyToOne} relationship hoga.
    \item \textbf{Student} aur \textbf{Address} ka \texttt{@OneToOne} relationship hoga.
    \item \textbf{Student} aur \textbf{Course} ka \texttt{@ManyToMany} relationship hoga.
\end{itemize}
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsection*{Hinglish Explanation}
Is tarah se, hum complex relationships ko easily manage kar sakte hain.

% Final Note
\section*{\color{headingblue}Final Note}
�� \textbf{Ab Spring Boot ka JPA relationship ka basic concept clear ho gaya? Koi aur doubt hai toh batao!} 

===============================
\hrule

% Custom Colors
\definecolor{headingblue}{RGB}{0, 102, 204}
\definecolor{examplered}{RGB}{0, 153, 76}
\definecolor{codebg}{RGB}{173, 216, 230}
\definecolor{tablered}{RGB}{144, 238, 144}

% Title
\title{\textbf{\color{headingblue}Understanding @JoinTable and @JoinColumn in Hinglish}}


\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]

\maketitle

% Section: @JoinTable Explanation
\section*{\color{headingblue}@JoinTable Ka Matlab}
\texttt{@JoinTable} annotation ka use \texttt{@ManyToMany} relationship mein kiya jata hai. Iska matlab hai ki ek extra table banega jo dono tables ke IDs ko connect karega.

\subsection*{Example: @JoinTable Ka Code}
\begin{examplebox}{Java Code: @JoinTable Example}
\begin{lstlisting}
@ManyToMany
@JoinTable(
    name = "student_course",
    joinColumns = @JoinColumn(name = "student_id"),
    inverseJoinColumns = @JoinColumn(name = "course_id")
)
private List<Course> courses;
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

\subsection*{Hinglish Explanation}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \texttt{name = "student\_course"}: Yeh batata hai ki extra table ka naam \texttt{student\_course} hoga.
    \item \texttt{joinColumns = @JoinColumn(name = "student\_id")}: Yeh batata hai ki \texttt{student\_id} column \texttt{student} table se connect hoga.
    \item \texttt{inverseJoinColumns = @JoinColumn(name = "course\_id")}: Yeh batata hai ki \texttt{course\_id} column \texttt{course} table se connect hoga.
\end{itemize}
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsection*{Generated SQL Table}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=SQL, basicstyle=\ttfamily\small, keywordstyle=\color{blue}]
CREATE TABLE student_course (
    student_id BIGINT,
    course_id BIGINT,
    FOREIGN KEY (student_id) REFERENCES student(id),
    FOREIGN KEY (course_id) REFERENCES course(id)
);
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{Table Representation}
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{|>{\columncolor{headingblue!20}}p{4cm}|>{\columncolor{examplered!20}}p{4cm}|}
    \hline
    
    \textbf{Column Name} & \textbf{Description} \\
    \hline
    \texttt{student\_id} & \texttt{student} table ke \texttt{id} se connected hai. \\
    \hline
    
    \texttt{course\_id} & \texttt{course} table ke \texttt{id} se connected hai. \\
    \hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\subsection*{Hinglish Explanation}
Yeh extra table (\texttt{student\_course}) banega jo \texttt{student\_id} aur \texttt{course\_id} ko connect karega.

% Section: @JoinColumn Default Behavior
\section*{\color{headingblue}@JoinColumn Mein Default Behavior}
Agar hum \texttt{@JoinColumn} mein \texttt{name} specify nahi karte, toh Hibernate automatically ek default column name generate karta hai.

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]

\subsection*{Example: @JoinColumn Without Name}
\begin{examplebox}{Java Code: @JoinColumn Without Name}
\begin{lstlisting}
@OneToOne
@JoinColumn // name specify nahi kiya gaya
private Address address;
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

\subsection*{Hinglish Explanation}
\begin{itemize}
    \item Agar \texttt{name} specify nahi kiya gaya, toh Hibernate default column name use karega.
    \item Default column name \texttt{address\_id} hoga, kyunki field ka naam \texttt{address} hai aur \texttt{\_id} append ho jayega.
    \item Matlab, agar field ka naam \texttt{address} hai, toh default column name \texttt{address\_id} hoga.
\end{itemize}
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsection*{Generated SQL Column}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=SQL, basicstyle=\ttfamily\small, keywordstyle=\color{blue}]
CREATE TABLE student (
    id BIGINT AUTO_INCREMENT PRIMARY KEY,
    name VARCHAR(255),
    address_id BIGINT,  // Default column name
    FOREIGN KEY (address_id) REFERENCES address(id)
);
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{Table Representation}
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{|>{\columncolor{headingblue!20}}p{4cm}|>{\columncolor{examplered!20}}p{4cm}|}
    \hline
    
    \textbf{Column Name} & \textbf{Description} \\
    \hline
    \texttt{id} & Primary key of the \texttt{student} table. \\
    \hline
    
    \texttt{name} & Name of the student. \\
    \hline
    \texttt{address\_id} & Foreign key connecting to the \texttt{address} table. \\
    \hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\subsection*{Hinglish Explanation}
Agar hum \texttt{name = "address\_id"} specify nahi karte, toh Hibernate automatically \texttt{address\_id} column banayega.

% Section: Summary
\section*{\color{headingblue}Summary}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \texttt{@JoinTable} ka use \texttt{@ManyToMany} relationship mein extra table banane ke liye hota hai.
    \item \texttt{@JoinColumn} mein agar \texttt{name} specify nahi kiya gaya, toh Hibernate default column name generate karega.
    \item Default column name field ke naam ke saath \texttt{\_id} append karke banaya jata hai (e.g., \texttt{address\_id}).
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{Hinglish Explanation}
Is tarah se, hum \texttt{@JoinTable} aur \texttt{@JoinColumn} ka use karke complex relationships ko easily manage kar sakte hain. Agar default behavior samajhna hai, toh \texttt{name} specify nahi karna padega.


===============================

\title{\textbf{Spring Boot Annotations - Detailed Explanation}}
\author{Your Name}
\date{}
\maketitle

\section{Spring Boot Annotations}

\subsection{@SpringBootApplication}
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=blue!10,colframe=blue!80,title=Overview]
\texttt{@SpringBootApplication} Spring Boot application ka entry point hota hai. Isme teen annotations combine hote hain: 
\texttt{@Configuration}, \texttt{@EnableAutoConfiguration}, aur \texttt{@ComponentScan}.
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Real-Life Example:}  
Maano aap ek restaurant management system bana rahe hain. \texttt{@SpringBootApplication} wali class aapki restaurant ki main gate ki tarah hai, jahan se sab kuch start hota hai.

\begin{lstlisting}[style=javaStyle]
@SpringBootApplication
public class RestaurantApplication {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        SpringApplication.run(RestaurantApplication.class, args);
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{Explanation:}  
\texttt{SpringApplication.run()} se aapki restaurant (application) start ho jati hai. ��

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]

\subsection{@RestController vs @Controller}
Dono annotations controllers ke liye use hote hain, lekin inka use case alag hai.

\textbf{Real-Life Example:}  

\begin{itemize}
    \item \texttt{@Controller}: Maano aap ek website bana rahe hain jahan par aap users ko HTML pages dikhana chahte hain. Jaise ki restaurant ka menu page.
\end{itemize}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{lstlisting}[style=javaStyle]
@Controller
public class MenuController {
    @GetMapping("/menu")
    public String showMenu() {
        return "menu"; // "menu.html" template render karega
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]

\begin{itemize}
    \item \texttt{@RestController}: Maano aap ek mobile app ke liye API bana rahe hain jo JSON data return karega. Jaise ki restaurant ka menu data JSON format mein.
\end{itemize}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{lstlisting}[style=javaStyle]
@RestController
public class MenuApiController {
    @GetMapping("/api/menu")
    public List<MenuItem> getMenu() {
        return menuService.getMenuItems(); // JSON response dega
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]
Agar aap web pages return kar rahe hain toh \texttt{@Controller} use karo, aur agar API bana rahe hain toh \texttt{@RestController} use karo.
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsection{@Service, @Repository, @Component}
Ye annotations Spring Boot ke components ko identify karne ke liye use hote hain.

\textbf{Real-Life Example:}

\begin{itemize}
    \item \texttt{@Service}: Maano aap restaurant mein waiter ka kaam karne wali service class bana rahe hain.
\end{itemize}

\begin{lstlisting}[style=javaStyle]
@Service
public class WaiterService {
    public String takeOrder(String order) {
        return "Order taken: " + order;
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\begin{itemize}
    \item \texttt{@Repository}: Maano aap restaurant ka database handle kar rahe hain, jaise ki orders ko store karna.
\end{itemize}

\begin{lstlisting}[style=javaStyle]
@Repository
public interface OrderRepository extends JpaRepository<Order, Long> {
    // Database queries yaha likhte hain
}
\end{lstlisting}

\begin{itemize}
    \item \texttt{@Component}: Maano aap ek utility class bana rahe hain jo general kaam karegi, jaise ki bill generate karna.
\end{itemize}

\begin{lstlisting}[style=javaStyle]
@Component
public class BillGenerator {
    public String generateBill() {
        return "Bill generated";
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!10,colframe=green!80,title=Tip]
Ye annotations Spring Boot ke "IoC Container" me automatically register ho jate hain.
\end{tcolorbox}

  language=Java,
  basicstyle=\ttfamily\footnotesize,
  keywordstyle=\color{blue},
  commentstyle=\color{gray},
  stringstyle=\color{red},
  showstringspaces=false,
  breaklines=true,
  frame=single

\begin{document}

\section{Dependency Injection (DI) aur Inversion of Control (IoC)}

\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Spring Boot me DI kaise kaam karta hai?}}\\
Dependency Injection (DI) ka matlab hai ki objects ka creation Spring Boot handle karega, aur hume manually \texttt{new} keyword se object banane ki zarurat nahi hoti.

\subsection*{Real-Life Example:}
Maano aap restaurant mein waiter aur chef ko manage kar rahe hain. Waiter ko chef ki zarurat hai order complete karne ke liye. Spring Boot automatically chef ka object waiter ko provide karega.

\begin{lstlisting}
@Service
public class ChefService {
    public String cookFood(String order) {
        return "Cooking: " + order;
    }
}

@RestController
public class WaiterController {
    private final ChefService chefService;

    // Dependency Injection (Constructor-based)
    @Autowired
    public WaiterController(ChefService chefService) {
        this.chefService = chefService;
    }

    @GetMapping("/order")
    public String placeOrder(@RequestParam String order) {
        return chefService.cookFood(order);
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{\textcolor{red}{✅ Spring Boot automatically ChefService ka object inject karega!}}

\subsection*{@Autowired ka deeper explanation}
Agar tum \texttt{@Autowired} use karte ho toh Spring Boot automatically object inject kar deta hai.

\begin{lstlisting}
@Component
public class ManagerService {
    @Autowired
    private WaiterService waiterService;

    @Autowired
    private ChefService chefService;

    public String manageRestaurant() {
        return waiterService.takeOrder("Pizza") + " " + chefService.cookFood("Pizza");
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{\textcolor{red}{�� Best Practice: Constructor Injection use karo instead of Field Injection.}}

\subsection*{Manual DI kaise kar sakte hain (@Bean, @ComponentScan)?}
Agar tum manually object create karna chahte ho toh \texttt{@Bean} use kar sakte ho.

\begin{lstlisting}
@Configuration
public class RestaurantConfig {
    @Bean
    public SpecialChef specialChef() {
        return new SpecialChef();
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{\textcolor{red}{✅ Spring Boot automatically RestaurantConfig me defined beans ko use karega.}}

\section{Spring Boot Security (Basic Authentication \\& JWT)}

\subsection*{Basic Authentication Setup}
Spring Security ka default configuration username \texttt{"user"} aur randomly generated password deta hai.

\begin{lstlisting}
<dependency>
    <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
    <artifactId>spring-boot-starter-security</artifactId>
</dependency>
\end{lstlisting}

\begin{lstlisting}
@Configuration
@EnableWebSecurity
public class SecurityConfig {
    @Bean
    public SecurityFilterChain securityFilterChain(HttpSecurity http) throws Exception {
        http.authorizeHttpRequests(auth -> auth
                .anyRequest().authenticated())
            .formLogin();
        return http.build();
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{\textcolor{red}{�� Isse Spring Boot me default login form enable ho jayega.}}

\subsection*{JWT Authentication Example}
JWT (JSON Web Token) authentication kaafi secure aur stateless hota hai.

\begin{lstlisting}
public String generateToken(String username) {
    return Jwts.builder()
        .setSubject(username)
        .setIssuedAt(new Date())
        .setExpiration(new Date(System.currentTimeMillis() + 1000 * 60 * 60)) // 1 Hour
        .signWith(SignatureAlgorithm.HS256, "secret")
        .compact();
}
\end{lstlisting}

\begin{lstlisting}
public Claims validateToken(String token) {
    return Jwts.parser()
        .setSigningKey("secret")
        .parseClaimsJws(token)
        .getBody();
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{\textcolor{red}{✅ JWT authentication me token request headers me send hota hai.}}

\section{Spring Boot Exception Handling}

\subsection*{@ControllerAdvice ka use}
\begin{lstlisting}
@ControllerAdvice
public class GlobalExceptionHandler {
    @ExceptionHandler(OrderNotFoundException.class)
    public ResponseEntity<String> handleOrderNotFoundException(OrderNotFoundException e) {
        return new ResponseEntity<>(e.getMessage(), HttpStatus.NOT_FOUND);
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{\textcolor{red}{�� Yeh har ek exception ko globally handle karega.}}

\section{Spring Boot Logging}

\begin{lstlisting}
@Slf4j
@Service
public class OrderService {
    public void placeOrder(String order) {
        log.info("Order placed: " + order);
        log.error("Error placing order: " + order);
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{\textcolor{red}{✅ Yeh logs console pe print honge aur application debugging me help karenge.}}

\section{Deployment of Spring Boot Application}

\subsection*{Jar file Generate karna}
\begin{lstlisting}
mvn clean package
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{Docker Pe Deploy Karna}
\begin{lstlisting}
FROM openjdk:17
COPY target/app.jar app.jar
CMD ["java", "-jar", "app.jar"]
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{\textcolor{red}{Ab isko Kubernetes ya AWS pe deploy kar sakte ho!}}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]

\section{Validation in Spring Boot}
Spring Boot mein validation ke liye \textbf{\textcolor{red}{@Valid, @NotNull, @Size, @Email}} annotations ka use kiya jata hai. Ye annotations ensure karte hain ki input data correct format mein ho.

\end{tcolorbox}

\subsection{Real-Life Example}
Maano aap ek restaurant ka user registration form bana rahe hain, jisme har user ka data validate karna hai.

\begin{lstlisting}[style=javaStyle, caption={User DTO with Validation}]
public class UserDTO {
    @NotNull
    private String name;

    @Email
    private String email;
}
\end{lstlisting}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]

\noindent
\textbf{\textcolor{red}{@NotNull}}: Ensure karta hai ki field \textbf{name} null na ho. \\
\textbf{\textcolor{red}{@Email}}: Ensure karta hai ki \textbf{email} valid email format mein ho.

\subsection{Additional Validations}
Agar aap aur validation lagana chahte hain to \textbf{\textcolor{red}{@Size}} ka use kar sakte hain:

\begin{lstlisting}[style=javaStyle, caption={User DTO with More Validations}]
public class UserDTO {
    @NotNull
    @Size(min = 3, max = 50)
    private String name;

    @Email
    @NotNull
    private String email;
}
\end{lstlisting}

\noindent
\textbf{\textcolor{red}{@Size(min = 3, max = 50)}}: Ensure karega ki name kam se kam 3 aur maximum 50 characters ka ho.

\subsection{Using @Valid in Controller}
Agar aap Spring Boot Controller mein request validation karna chahte hain, to \textbf{\textcolor{red}{@Valid}} ka use kar sakte hain:

\begin{lstlisting}[style=javaStyle, caption={Using @Valid in a Controller}]
@RestController
public class UserController {
    @PostMapping("/register")
    public ResponseEntity<String> registerUser(@Valid @RequestBody UserDTO user) {
        return ResponseEntity.ok("User registered successfully!");
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\noindent
\textbf{\textcolor{red}{@Valid}}: Ensure karta hai ki incoming request ka data valid ho.
\end{tcolorbox}

\title{\textbf{\color{headings} One-to-Many Relation in Spring Boot \\ 
Foreign Key Issue – Simple Explanation}}
\author{}
\date{}

\begin{document}

\maketitle

\section{\textbf{\color{headings} Introduction}}
This document explains the One-to-Many relationship in Spring Boot and why foreign keys exist in the child table rather than the parent table. 

\section{\textbf{\color{headings} Understanding One-to-Many Relationship}}
A \textbf{School} has multiple \textbf{Students}:
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{One School $\rightarrow$ Many Students}
    \item Each student belongs to one school, but a school has many students.
\end{itemize}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colframe=examples, colback=white, title=Example]
ABC School has students: Rahul, Priya, Aman.
\end{tcolorbox}

\section{\textbf{\color{headings} Foreign Key Placement Issue}}
Foreign keys are stored in the \textbf{child table} (Student), not the \textbf{parent table} (School). 

\begin{lstlisting}[language=SQL]
Student Table:
+----+--------+----------+
| id | name   | schoolId |
+----+--------+----------+
| 1  | Rahul  | 101      |
| 2  | Priya  | 101      |
| 3  | Aman   | 102      |
+----+--------+----------+
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{Why not store students directly in the school table?}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \color{warnings}{Relational databases cannot store lists in a single column.}
    \item \textbf{Foreign keys are always in the child table.}
\end{itemize}

\section{\textbf{\color{headings} Correct Approach in Spring Boot}}
Spring Boot handles this using \textbf{@OneToMany} and \textbf{@ManyToOne} annotations:

\begin{lstlisting}
@Entity
public class School {
    @Id
    @GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY)
    private Long id;

    private String name;

    @OneToMany(mappedBy = "school", cascade = CascadeType.ALL)
    private List<Student> students;
}
\end{lstlisting}

\begin{lstlisting}
@Entity
public class Student {
    @Id
    @GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY)
    private Long id;

    private String name;

    @ManyToOne
    @JoinColumn(name = "school_id")
    private School school;
}
\end{lstlisting}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]
\begin{itemize}
    \item \texttt{@OneToMany(mappedBy = "school")} means \textbf{School has a list of students but does not store a foreign key}. 
    \item \texttt{@ManyToOne @JoinColumn(name = "school_id")} means \textbf{Student table stores the foreign key}. 
\end{itemize}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]

\section{\textbf{\color{headings} CascadeType.ALL Explanation}}
If \textbf{CascadeType.ALL} is used:
\begin{itemize}
    \item Deleting a \textbf{School} deletes its \textbf{Students}.
    \item Updating a \textbf{School} updates its \textbf{Students}.
\end{itemize}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colframe=examples, colback=white, title=Example]
Deleting School ID 101 will delete all students linked to it.
\end{tcolorbox}

\section{\textbf{\color{headings} Summary}}
\begin{enumerate}
    \item \textbf{Foreign key is always in the child table (Student), not the parent table (School).}
    \item \textbf{Spring Boot uses @OneToMany and @ManyToOne to map relationships.}
    \item \textbf{CascadeType.ALL helps manage related records automatically.}
\end{enumerate}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]

\title{\textbf{\color{headingcolor}{\huge Most Important Point Below all points are very very important and made from my mistakes so please go through each line by line....}}

\end{tcolorbox}

\maketitle

\section*{Mistake: Spring Boot Controller Not Found Issue}

\subsection*{\textbf{\textcolor{warningcolor}{\xmark\ Galti Jo Hui Thi:}}}
\begin{enumerate}
    \item \textbf{Package Structure Galat Tha:}
    \begin{itemize}
        \item Maine `controller` aur `service` folders **`java` folder ke andar** bana diye the.
        \item Lekin **Spring Boot sirf `@SpringBootApplication` wale class ke parent package me scan karta hai**.
        \item Mera `DemoApplication.java` **`com.example.demo`** package me tha, par `Controller.java` **`com.example.demo.Controller`** package me likha tha, jo Spring Boot ke scan range ke bahar tha.
    \end{itemize}
    \item \textbf{Class Name `Controller` Rakha Tha:}
    \begin{itemize}
        \item `Controller` naam dena **galat tha** kyunki Spring ke `@Controller` annotation ke saath **naming conflict ho raha tha**.
        \item Is wajah se Spring Boot ne `Controller.java` ko properly detect nahi kiya.
    \end{itemize}
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{\textbf{\textcolor{examplecolor}{\checkmark\ Correct Solution Jo Follow Karna Hai:}}}
\begin{enumerate}
    \item \textbf{Package Structure Sahi Karna:}
    \begin{itemize}
        \item **Controller aur Service folders** `DemoApplication` ke **bagal me hone chahiye**.
        \item \textbf{Sahi Structure:}
    \end{itemize}
    \begin{tcolorbox}[colback=examplecolor!10, colframe=examplecolor, title=Correct Folder Structure]
    \begin{lstlisting}
    src/main/java/com/example/demo/
    ├── DemoApplication.java  <-- Spring Boot ka main class
    ├── controller/           <-- Yahan controllers rakhna hai
    │   ├── ApiController.java  (Rename from Controller.java)
    ├── service/              <-- Yahan services rakhni hai
    │   ├── ServiceClass.java
    \end{lstlisting}
    \end{tcolorbox}
    \item Ab `DemoApplication.java` **automatically `controller` aur `service` folder scan karega**.
    \item \textbf{Class Name Meaningful Rakhna:}
    \begin{itemize}
        \item `Controller.java` ka naam **rename karke** `ApiController.java` rakho taaki **naming conflict na ho**.
    \end{itemize}
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{\textbf{\textcolor{headingcolor}{\star\ Key Takeaways:}}}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{\textcolor{warningcolor}{Spring Boot sirf `@SpringBootApplication` ke parent package me controllers aur services ko detect karega.}}
    \item \textbf{\textcolor{warningcolor}{Controller class ka naam generic (`Controller.java`) mat rakho, use something like `ApiController.java`.}}
    \item \textbf{\textcolor{warningcolor}{Packages aur folders ka structure sahi hona chahiye nahi toh Spring Boot usko detect nahi karega.}}
\end{itemize}

\begin{document}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]

\section{Getter and Setter Methods in Java (Hinglish Explanation)}

\end{tcolorbox}

Getter aur Setter methods ka use \textbf{Encapsulation} ke concept ko implement karne ke liye hota hai. Yeh methods \textbf{private variables} ko access karne aur modify karne ka safe tareeka provide karte hain.

\section{Getter and Setter Methods Kya Hote Hain?}

\textbf{Getter Methods} → Private variables ki value \textbf{read} karne ke liye.  
\textbf{Setter Methods} → Private variables ki value \textbf{update} karne ke liye.  

\subsection{Example (Java)}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java, caption=Getter and Setter Methods in Java]
public class User {
    private String email; // Private variable

    // Getter Method
    public String getEmail() {
        return email;
    }

    // Setter Method
    public void setEmail(String email) {
        this.email = email;
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\begin{examplebox}{Getter vs Setter}
\textbf{Getter se sirf value read hoti hai aur Setter se value update hoti hai.}
\end{examplebox}

\section{Agar Getter and Setter Use Nahi Karenge to Kya Hoga?}

Agar \textbf{getter aur setter} methods \textbf{nahi use} karoge to:

\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{Private variables ko access nahi kar paoge}  
    - Kyunki \textbf{private} variables \textbf{directly access nahi kiye ja sakte} kisi aur class se.  
    \item \textbf{Encapsulation break ho jayegi}  
    - Private data ko \textbf{directly modify} karna \textbf{unsafe hota hai}.  
    \item \textbf{Data Validation nahi kar sakte}  
    - \textbf{Setter method me validation dal sakte hain}, lekin direct access se validation nahi hoga.
\end{itemize}

\subsection{Example Without Getter/Setter}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java, caption=Without Getter/Setter Methods]
public class User {
    private String email; // Private variable

    public void showEmail() {
        System.out.println(email); // Direct access not possible from another class
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

Yahan \texttt{email} variable \textbf{private} hai, to isse \textbf{direct access nahi kar sakte}. Agar \textbf{getter method nahi hoga}, to iski value \textbf{bahar se read nahi kar paoge}.

\section{Getter/Setter ka Express.js ke saath Comparison}

Agar tum \textbf{Express.js} jaante ho, to isse \textbf{Mongoose Model ke concept} se relate kar sakte ho.

\subsection{Express.js Mongoose Model (Getter/Setter jaisa)}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=JavaScript, caption=Getter and Setter in Express.js Mongoose Model]
const mongoose = require('mongoose');

const userSchema = new mongoose.Schema({
    email: { type: String, required: true }
});

// Getter function jaisa
userSchema.methods.getEmail = function() {
    return this.email;
};

// Setter function jaisa
userSchema.methods.setEmail = function(newEmail) {
    this.email = newEmail;
};

const User = mongoose.model('User', userSchema);

let user = new User({ email: "test@example.com" });

console.log(user.getEmail()); // Getter ka use
user.setEmail("newemail@example.com"); // Setter ka use
console.log(user.getEmail());
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection{Express.js vs Java Getter/Setter}

\begin{longtable}{|c|c|c|}
\hline
\rowcolor{headingblue} \textbf{Feature} & \textbf{Express.js (Mongoose)} & \textbf{Java (Spring Boot)} \\
\hline
\rowcolor{tablerow} \textbf{Encapsulation} & Schema me define hota hai & Private variables aur methods ka use hota hai \\
\hline
\textbf{Getter Method} & \texttt{user.getEmail()} & \texttt{user.getEmail()} \\
\hline
\rowcolor{tablerow} \textbf{Setter Method} & \texttt{user.setEmail("newemail")} & \texttt{user.setEmail("newemail")} \\
\hline
\textbf{Validation} & Schema validation (\texttt{required: true}) & Setter me validation likh sakte ho \\
\hline
\end{longtable}

\section{Conclusion (Hinglish Me)}

\begin{itemize}
    \item Getter aur Setter \textbf{Encapsulation implement karne} ke liye use hote hain.
    \item \textbf{Getter value ko read karne} ke liye hota hai.
    \item \textbf{Setter value update karne} aur \textbf{validation apply karne} ke liye hota hai.
    \item \textbf{Agar getter aur setter nahi likhoge to private variables ko access nahi kar paoge.}
    \item \textbf{Express.js me yeh concept Mongoose ke methods aur schema validation ke through implement hota hai.}
\end{itemize}

Ab tum Getter aur Setter ko \textbf{Mongoose Model ke instance methods} se relate kar sakte ho!

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]

\title{\textbf{\textcolor{purple}{\huge User Authentication in Spring Boot }}}
\end{tcolorbox}

\section*{Overview}
In this section, we will implement user authentication using email and password in Spring Boot. We will create methods to:
\begin{itemize}
    \item \checkmark\ Find a user by email
    \item \checkmark\ Check if the password matches
    \item \checkmark\ Return true if authentication is successful, otherwise false
\end{itemize}

\section*{\textcolor{blue}{1. Service Layer - UserSignupService.java}}
This layer handles business logic, including finding users and verifying passwords.

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=gray!10, colframe=blue!50, title=\textbf{Java Code}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java, style=JavaStyle]
// �� src/main/java/com/example/demo/Service/UserSignupService.java
package com.example.demo.Service;

import com.example.demo.Entity.UserSignupEntity;
import com.example.demo.Repository.UserSignupRepository;
import org.springframework.beans.factory.annotation.Autowired;
import org.springframework.stereotype.Service;
import java.util.Optional;

@Service // ✅ Service Layer Annotation
public class UserSignupService {

    @Autowired // ✅ Spring Boot will inject the repository automatically
    private UserSignupRepository userSignupRepository;

    /**
     * ✅ Method to authenticate user based on email & password
     * @param email - User's email ID
     * @param password - User's entered password
     * @return true if user exists and password matches, false otherwise
     */
    public boolean authenticateUser(String email, String password) {
        // �� Step 1: Find user by email in the database
        Optional<UserSignupEntity> userOptional = userSignupRepository.findByEmail(email);

        // �� Step 2: Check if user exists
        if (userOptional.isPresent()) { // ✅ If user found in DB
            UserSignupEntity user = userOptional.get(); // �� Extract user object

            // �� Step 3: Compare passwords (⚠️ Plain-text comparison, not recommended for production)
            return user.getPassword().equals(password); // ✅ Return true if password matches
        }

        // �� Step 4: Return false if user does not exist
        return false;
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\definecolor{alertbox}{rgb}{1.0, 0.8, 0.8}   % Light red

\begin{document}

\title{\textbf{Repository Layer - UserSignupRepository.java}}
\author{}
\date{}
\maketitle

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=infobox,colframe=blue!50,title=\textbf{This interface interacts with the database to find users by email.}]
\end{tcolorbox}

\vspace{0.5cm}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=notebox,colframe=black,title=\textbf{Java Code}]
\begin{lstlisting}[style=mystyle]
// src/main/java/com/example/demo/Repository/UserSignupRepository.java
package com.example.demo.Repository;

import com.example.demo.Entity.UserSignupEntity;
import org.springframework.data.jpa.repository.JpaRepository;
import org.springframework.stereotype.Repository;
import java.util.Optional;

@Repository // Marks this interface as a Repository
public interface UserSignupRepository extends JpaRepository<UserSignupEntity, Long> {

    /**
     * Custom query method to find a user by email
     * @param email - User's email ID
     * @return Optional containing UserSignupEntity if found, otherwise empty
     */
    Optional<UserSignupEntity> findByEmail(String email); 
    // Spring Data JPA will automatically generate SQL: SELECT * FROM users WHERE email = ?
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\vspace{0.5cm}

\section*{Code Explanation in Detail}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=notebox,colframe=black,title=\textbf{Service Layer (UserSignupService.java)}]
This handles authentication logic.
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=infobox,colframe=black,title=\textbf{public boolean authenticateUser(String email, String password)}]
This method takes email and password as input and returns true if authentication is successful, otherwise false.
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=notebox,colframe=black,title=\textbf{Optional<UserSignupEntity> userOptional = userSignupRepository.findByEmail(email);} ]
findByEmail(email) - Database se email ke basis par user dhoondhta hai. \\
Optional<UserSignupEntity> - NullPointerException avoid karne ke liye Optional use hota hai. \\
Agar email exist nahi karta toh Optional.empty() return hoga.
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=infobox,colframe=black,title=\textbf{if (userOptional.isPresent())}]
Check kar raha hai ki user database me mila ya nahi. \\
Agar mila toh true hoga aur andar ka code execute hoga.
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=notebox,colframe=black,title=\textbf{UserSignupEntity user = userOptional.get();}]
userOptional.get() se actual user object retrieve ho raha hai.
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=infobox,colframe=black,title=\textbf{return user.getPassword().equals(password);} ]
User ka password match karta hai ya nahi check kar raha hai.
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=alertbox,colframe=black,title=\textbf{Security Alert}]
Plain-text password check safe nahi hota. \\
Production me password hashing (BCrypt) use karna chahiye.
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=notebox,colframe=black,title=\textbf{return false;}]
Agar email exist nahi karta toh false return karega.
\end{tcolorbox}

\vspace{0.5cm}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=notebox,colframe=black,title=\textbf{Repository Layer (UserSignupRepository.java)}]
JpaRepository<UserSignupEntity, Long> \\
UserSignupEntity - Database table ke corresponding entity class. \\
Long - Primary key type.
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=infobox,colframe=black,title=\textbf{Optional<UserSignupEntity> findByEmail(String email);} ]
Spring Data JPA automatically SQL query generate kar dega:
\end{tcolorbox}

\vspace{0.3cm}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=notebox,colframe=black,title=\textbf{Generated SQL Query}]
\begin{lstlisting}[style=mystyle]
SELECT * FROM users WHERE email = ?;
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=infobox,colframe=black,title=\textbf{Additional Notes}]
Optional keyword use NullPointerException avoid karne ke liye hota hai. \\
Agar email match karega toh Optional<UserSignupEntity> return hoga, warna Optional.empty().
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{document}

\title{\textbf{Final Summary}}
\date{}
\maketitle

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=infobox,colframe=blue!50,title=\textbf{Step-by-Step Authentication Process}]
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{Step 1:} User enters email \& password. \\
          \textit{User input aata hai authentication ke liye.}
    \item \textbf{Step 2:} Database me \texttt{findByEmail(email)} se check hota hai. \\
          \textit{Repository email match karke user return karta hai.}
    \item \textbf{Step 3:} Agar user exist karta hai toh password match hota hai. \\
          \textit{Plain-text password compare hota hai (⚠ Secure nahi hai).}
    \item \textbf{Step 4:} Agar password sahi hai toh \texttt{true} return hota hai. \\
          \textit{Authentication successful.}
    \item \textbf{Step 5:} Agar user nahi mila ya password galat hai toh \texttt{false} return hota hai. \\
          \textit{Authentication fail ho jata hai.}
\end{itemize}
\end{tcolorbox}

\vspace{0.5cm}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=alertbox,colframe=red!50,title=\textbf{�� Security Improvements (Best Practices) ��}]
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{�� Warning:} Abhi hum password ko \textbf{plain-text} me check kar rahe hain, jo \textbf{secure nahi hai}.
    \item \textbf{Password Hashing ka Use Karo:}
          \begin{itemize}
              \item \textbf{BCrypt} ya \textbf{Argon2} hashing algorithms use karo.
          \end{itemize}
\end{itemize}
\end{tcolorbox}

\vspace{0.3cm}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=notebox,colframe=black,title=\textbf{�� Example Code (Java)}]
\begin{lstlisting}[style=mystyle]
BCryptPasswordEncoder encoder = new BCryptPasswordEncoder();
if (encoder.matches(password, user.getPassword())) { ... }
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\vspace{0.3cm}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=infobox,colframe=black,title=\textbf{Additional Security Measures}]
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{Database me encrypted password store karo.}
    \item \textbf{Login attempt count limit set karo} (Brute-force attack se bachne ke liye).
\end{itemize}
\end{tcolorbox}

\vspace{0.5cm}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=notebox,colframe=black,title=\textbf{�� Conclusion (Hinglish Me)}]
✔ \textbf{Spring Boot} me authentication ke liye \texttt{findByEmail()} use hota hai. \\
✔ Agar \textbf{email exist} karta hai aur \textbf{password match} hota hai toh authentication successful hota hai. \\
✔ \textbf{Optional} class ka use \textbf{NullPointerException} handle karne ke liye kiya jata hai. \\
✔ \textbf{Security ke liye password hashing implement karna zaroori hai.}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]

% Title Page
\title{\textbf{\textcolor{violet}{\huge Spring Boot mai Bean Concepts Explained}}}

\date{\today}

\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{document}

% Title Page
\maketitle

% Section 1: Spring me Bean kya hota hai?
\section{Spring me Bean kya hota hai?}
\textbf{Bean} ek object hota hai jo \textbf{Spring IoC (Inversion of Control) container} ke dwara manage kiya jata hai. Jab hum `@Bean` annotation ka use karte hain, to Spring ko batate hain ki us object ko create aur manage karna hai.

% Section 2: BCryptPasswordEncoder kya hai aur kyun zaroori hai?
\section{BCryptPasswordEncoder kya hai aur kyun zaroori hai?}
\textbf{BCryptPasswordEncoder} ek hashing algorithm hai jo passwords ko securely store karne ke liye use hota hai. Ye passwords ko encrypt karta hai taaki agar koi database hack ho jaye to bhi passwords secure rahe.

% Section 3: BCryptPasswordEncoder ko Bean kyun banana padta hai?
\section{BCryptPasswordEncoder ko Bean kyun banana padta hai?}
\subsection{Dependency Injection (DI) ke liye}
Agar hum har jagah `new BCryptPasswordEncoder()` likhenge, to har baar naya object banega. Isse memory aur performance issues ho sakte hain. \textbf{Bean} banane se Spring ek hi object ko manage karta hai aur usko jahan bhi zaroorat ho, wahan inject kar deta hai.

\subsection{Memory Management}
Agar hum har baar `new BCryptPasswordEncoder()` likhenge, to har baar naya object banega. Isse memory zyada use hogi. \textbf{Bean} banane se ek hi object reuse hota hai, jisse memory bachti hai.

\subsection{Loose Coupling aur Testability}
\textbf{Loose Coupling} ka matlab hai ki hum directly object create nahi karte, balki Spring se usko inject karwate hain. Isse code flexible aur testable ban jata hai. \textbf{Unit Testing} mein hum mock objects use kar sakte hain, jo ki easy hota hai jab hum `@Autowired` ka use karte hain.

% Section 4: Bean kaise kaam karta hai?
\section{Bean kaise kaam karta hai?}
\subsection{Bean ke bina (Galat Tarika)}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
public class UserService {
    private BCryptPasswordEncoder encoder = new BCryptPasswordEncoder(); // Galat Tarika
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{Problem:} Har baar `UserService` create hone par naya `BCryptPasswordEncoder` object banega. \textbf{Solution:} Isko Bean bana ke use karo!

\subsection{Bean ke saath (Sahi Tarika)}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
@Configuration
public class SecurityConfig {

    @Bean
    public PasswordEncoder passwordEncoder() {
        return new BCryptPasswordEncoder(); //  Ek hi object Spring manage karega
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
Ab `UserService.java` mein isko \textbf{autowire} karenge:
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
@Service
public class UserService {

    @Autowired
    private PasswordEncoder passwordEncoder; // Spring Bean inject karega

    public void registerUser(User user) {
        String hashedPassword = passwordEncoder.encode(user.getPassword());
        user.setPassword(hashedPassword);
        userRepository.save(user);
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{Benefit:} Spring khud hi `BCryptPasswordEncoder` ko inject kar dega jab bhi zaroorat hogi.

% Section 5: Summary (Hinglish Mein)
\section{Summary (Hinglish Mein)}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{Spring mein "Bean" ka matlab hai ki Spring khud us object ko manage karega.}
    \item \textbf{Agar har jagah `new BCryptPasswordEncoder()` likhoge, to har baar naya object banega, jo memory waste karega.}
    \item \textbf{Agar `@Bean` use karoge, to ek hi object Spring manage karega, aur hum bas `@Autowired` se use kar sakte hain.}
    \item \textbf{Loose coupling aur dependency injection se code maintainable aur testable ban jata hai.}
\end{itemize}

% Section 6: Agar hum Bean nahi banayenge to kya hoga?
\section{Agar hum Bean nahi banayenge to kya hoga?}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{Memory Waste:} Har baar naya object banega, jisse memory zyada use hogi.
    \item \textbf{Code Duplication:} Har jagah `new BCryptPasswordEncoder()` likhna padega, jo code ko messy banayega.
    \item \textbf{Testing Difficulties:} Unit testing mein mock objects use karna mushkil ho jayega.
\end{itemize}

% Section 7: Kuch aur doubts clear karne ke liye
\section{Kuch aur doubts clear karne ke liye}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{Agar hum `@Bean` na use karein to kya hoga?} Agar hum `@Bean` na use karein, to humein har jagah manually `new BCryptPasswordEncoder()` likhna padega. Isse code maintain karna mushkil ho jayega aur memory bhi zyada use hogi.
    \item \textbf{Kya hum `BCryptPasswordEncoder` ko directly class mein use kar sakte hain?} Ha, kar sakte hain, lekin ye best practice nahi hai. Isse code tightly coupled ho jayega aur testing mein dikkat aayegi.
    \item \textbf{Kya hum ek se zyada `BCryptPasswordEncoder` Bean bana sakte hain?} Ha, bana sakte hain, lekin Spring ko batana padega ki konsa Bean use karna hai. Iske liye `@Qualifier` annotation ka use hota hai.
    \item \textbf{Kya `BCryptPasswordEncoder` ke alawa aur koi PasswordEncoder use kar sakte hain?} Ha, Spring Security mein aur bhi PasswordEncoder hote hain jaise `NoOpPasswordEncoder`, `Pbkdf2PasswordEncoder`, etc. Lekin `BCryptPasswordEncoder` sabse secure mana jata hai.
\end{itemize}

% Section 8: Final Thought
\section{Final Thought}
\begin{itemize}
    \item `BCryptPasswordEncoder` ko `@Bean` banana ek best practice hai. Isse memory efficient, maintainable, aur testable code milta hai.
    \item Agar aur koi doubt ho to pooch sakte hain. 
\end{itemize}

% Section 9: Recommended Location for SecurityConfig.java
\section{Recommended Location for `SecurityConfig.java`}
\subsection{Best Practice (Create a Config Package)}
Place it inside a \textbf{dedicated configuration package}:
\begin{lstlisting}[language=bash]
src/main/java/com/example/demo/
│── Controller/
│── Entity/
│── Repository/
│── Service/
│── Config/    Create this package for configurations
│    ├── SecurityConfig.java   Place this file here
│
└── DemoApplication.java  (Main Spring Boot Application)
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection{Why Create a `Config/` Package?}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{Organized Structure:} Keeps configuration files separate from business logic.
    \item \textbf{Scalability:} You can add more configuration files later (like JWT, CORS, etc.).
    \item \textbf{Easy to Maintain:} If you have multiple security-related configurations, they stay in one place.
\end{itemize}

\subsection{What If You Don't Create a `Config/` Package?}
If you don’t want to create a `Config/` package, you can place `SecurityConfig.java` in the same package as your `DemoApplication.java` (main class), because Spring Boot automatically scans the \textbf{same package and its sub-packages}.

\subsection{Alternative Location}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=bash]
src/main/java/com/example/demo/
│── Controller/
│── Entity/
│── Repository/
│── Service/
│── SecurityConfig.java   Place here if no config package
│
└── DemoApplication.java   (Main Spring Boot Application)
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{This works fine}, but a separate `Config/` package is recommended for better structure.

\subsection{Final Answer (Best Practice)}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{Create `Config/` package}
    \item \textbf{Place `SecurityConfig.java` inside it}
    \item This keeps your \textbf{Spring Boot project clean, modular, and scalable.} 
\end{itemize}

===============================
\hrule

% Title Page

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]

\title{\textbf{\textcolor{violet}{\huge Step-by-Step Guide to Fix Missing Dependency Issues}}}

\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{document}

\maketitle

% Introduction
\section*{\color{headingblue}Introduction}
This document provides a step-by-step guide to resolve missing dependency issues in Maven or Gradle projects using IntelliJ IDEA. It includes detailed instructions, examples, and Hinglish explanations for better understanding.

\section*{\color{headingblue}Step-by-Step Guide}
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textbf{Step \arabic*:}]
    \item \textbf{Open `pom.xml` or `build.gradle` File}
    \begin{itemize}
        \item \textbf{Maven (`pom.xml`):} Open the `pom.xml` file and add the missing dependency in the `<dependencies>` section.
        \item \textbf{Gradle (`build.gradle`):} Open the `build.gradle` file and add the missing dependency in the `dependencies` block.
        \item \textbf{Hinglish Explanation:} `pom.xml` ya `build.gradle` file ko open karo aur missing dependency ko add karo.
    \end{itemize}

    \begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]

    \item \textbf{Reload Maven/Gradle Project}
    \begin{itemize}
        \item \textbf{Maven:} Right-click on `pom.xml` and select \texttt{Maven > Reload Project}.
        \item \textbf{Gradle:} Right-click on `build.gradle` and select \texttt{Reload Gradle Project}.
        \item \textbf{Hinglish Explanation:} Project ko reload karo taaki changes apply ho sakein.
    \end{itemize}

    \end{tcolorbox}

    \item \textbf{Force Update Dependencies}
    \begin{itemize}
        \item \textbf{Maven:} Run the following command in the terminal:
        \begin{commandbox}
            \texttt{mvn clean install}
        \end{commandbox}
        \item \textbf{Gradle:} Run the following command in the terminal:
        \begin{commandbox}
            \texttt{./gradlew build --refresh-dependencies}
        \end{commandbox}
        \item \textbf{Hinglish Explanation:} Dependencies ko force update karo taaki sab kuch download ho jaye.
    \end{itemize}

    \item \textbf{Invalidate Cache and Restart IntelliJ}
    \begin{itemize}
        \item Go to \texttt{File > Invalidate Caches / Restart}.
        \item \textbf{Hinglish Explanation:} IntelliJ ka cache clear karo aur restart karo.
    \end{itemize}

    \item \textbf{Verify Imports}
    \begin{itemize}
        \item Manually import the missing class in your Java file.
        \item \textbf{Hinglish Explanation:} Java file mein missing class ko manually import karo.
    \end{itemize}

    \item \textbf{Restart Application}
    \begin{itemize}
        \item Restart your Spring Boot application.
        \item \textbf{Hinglish Explanation:} Application ko restart karo aur check karo ki sab sahi se kaam kar raha hai.
    \end{itemize}
\end{enumerate}

% Example Section
\section*{\color{headingblue}Examples}
\begin{examplebox}{Example: Adding Spring Security Dependency}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=xml]
<!-- Maven Dependency for Spring Security -->
<dependency>
    <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
    <artifactId>spring-boot-starter-security</artifactId>
</dependency>
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

% Table Section
\section*{\color{headingblue}Tables}
\begin{table}[h!]
    \centering
    \begin{tabular}{|>{\columncolor{headingblue!30}}p{4cm}|>{\columncolor{examplered!30}}p{4cm}|>{\columncolor{yellow!30}}p{4cm}|}
        \hline
        \textbf{Step} & \textbf{Action} & \textbf{Hinglish Explanation} \\
        \hline
        Step 1 & Open `pom.xml` or `build.gradle` & File ko open karo aur dependency add karo \\
        \hline
        Step 2 & Reload Project & Project ko reload karo \\
        \hline
        Step 3 & Force Update Dependencies & Dependencies ko force update karo \\
        \hline
        Step 4 & Invalidate Cache & Cache clear karo aur IntelliJ restart karo \\
        \hline
        Step 5 & Verify Imports & Missing class ko manually import karo \\
        \hline
        Step 6 & Restart Application & Application restart karo \\
        \hline
    \end{tabular}
    \caption{Step-by-Step Summary}
\end{table}

% Summary Section
\section*{\color{headingblue}Summary}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \color{warningred} \textbf{Check `pom.xml` or `build.gradle` for missing dependencies.}
    \item \color{warningred} \textbf{Reload the project to apply changes.}
    \item \color{warningred} \textbf{Force update dependencies if necessary.}
    \item \color{warningred} \textbf{Invalidate cache and restart IntelliJ.}
    \item \color{warningred} \textbf{Verify imports and restart the application.}
\end{itemize}

% Title
\begin{center}

 \begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]
  \title{\textbf{\textcolor{violet}{\huge Java mein \texttt{import} kaise kaam karta hai? 
  (Hinglish Guide)}}}

\end{tcolorbox}
  
\end{center}

% Introduction
\section{Introduction}
Agar aap Java ya Spring Boot seekh rahe ho, toh aapko \texttt{import} ka concept samajhna zaroori hai. Ye guide step-by-step aapko \texttt{import}, \texttt{package}, aur \texttt{class} ka basic samjhane wali hai.

---

% Step 1: Package kya hota hai?
\section{Step 1: \texttt{package} kya hota hai?}

\documentclass{article}
\usepackage{xcolor}
\usepackage{listings}

% Define colors
\definecolor{foldercolor}{rgb}{0.2, 0.6, 1.0}  % Blue folder
\definecolor{filecolor}{rgb}{0.0, 0.5, 0.0}    % red files

\begin{document}

\section*{Package ke andar multiple classes ka structure}
Suppose you have a package named \texttt{com.example.demo}. Inside this package, you can have multiple classes, such as:

\begin{lstlisting}[basicstyle=\ttfamily, language=]
com/example/demo/
    ├── Main.java
    ├── User.java
    ├── Product.java
    └── Utils.java
\end{lstlisting}

Here:

\begin{itemize}
    \item \texttt{Main.java}, \texttt{User.java}, \texttt{Product.java}, and \texttt{Utils.java} are all part of the \texttt{com.example.demo} package.
    \item Each file represents a separate class.
\end{itemize}




\begin{itemize}
  \item \textbf{\texttt{package} ek folder jaisa hota hai}, jo aapki Java classes ko organize karne ke liye use hota hai.
  \item Ye \textbf{namespace} provide karta hai jisse same naam wali classes ek doosre se alag rah sakein.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Example:}  
Agar aapka project ka structure kuch aisa hai:

\begin{lstlisting}
com/example/demo/Security/JWTUtils.java
\end{lstlisting}

Toh \texttt{JWTUtils.java} \textbf{\texttt{com.example.demo.Security} package} ke andar hai.

\subsection{Package define karna}
Jab aap koi Java file (\texttt{.java}) likhte ho, toh sabse pehle \texttt{package} define karna hota hai:

\begin{examplebox}{Package Definition}
\begin{lstlisting}
package com.example.demo.Security; // Batata hai ki ye class kis package mein hai

public class JWTUtils {
    // Methods yaha honge
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

---

% Step 2: Import kya hota hai?
\section{Step 2: \texttt{import} kya hota hai?}
\begin{itemize}
  \item \textbf{Jab aap ek class ko doosri class mein use karna chahte ho}, toh usko import karna padta hai.
  \item Import batata hai ki Java ko kahaan se class ya method uthani hai.
\end{itemize}

---

% Step 3: Aapka import statement galat kyun hai?
\section{Step 3: Aapka \texttt{import} statement galat kyun hai?}
Aap likh rahe ho:
\begin{lstlisting}
import com.example.demo.Security.JWTUtils.*;
\end{lstlisting}
Lekin ye \textbf{incorrect} hai kyunki:
\begin{itemize}
  \item \textbf{\texttt{JWTUtils} ek class hai, package nahi} – Isliye \texttt{.*} lagana galat hai.
  \item \textbf{\texttt{import com.example.demo.Security.JWTUtils;}} likhna chahiye. ✅
\end{itemize}

---

% Step 4: Sahi Tarika: Import ek puri class
\section{Step 4: Sahi Tarika: Import ek puri class}
Agar \texttt{JWTUtils.java} aapke \texttt{com.example.demo.Security} folder ke andar hai, toh sahi import hoga:

\begin{examplebox}{Correct Import Statement}
\begin{lstlisting}
import com.example.demo.Security.JWTUtils;
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

Ab aap \texttt{JWTUtils} class ke methods ko is tarah se use kar sakte ho:

\begin{lstlisting}
String token = JWTUtils.generateToken("user@example.com");
\end{lstlisting}

---

% Step 5: Static Import (Direct Method Use)
\section{Step 5: Static Import (Direct Method Use)}
Agar aapko \textbf{class ka naam likhne se bachna hai}, toh aap \textbf{static import} ka use kar sakte ho.

\subsection{Example: Static Import}
\begin{examplebox}{Static Import Example}
\begin{lstlisting}
import static com.example.demo.Security.JWTUtils.generateToken;
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

Ab aap \textbf{directly method use kar sakte ho} bina \texttt{JWTUtils.} likhe:

\begin{lstlisting}
String token = generateToken("user@example.com"); // Ab JWTUtils likhne ki zaroorat nahi
\end{lstlisting}

---

% Step 6: Final Steps (Check & Fix)
\section{Step 6: Final Steps (Check & Fix)}
Agar still error aa raha hai, toh \textbf{ye cheezein check karo:}
\begin{itemize}
  \item \textbf{Check karo ki \texttt{JWTUtils.java} sahi package (\texttt{com.example.demo.Security}) mein hai ya nahi.}
  \item \textbf{Galat import ko hatao aur sahi wala likho:}  
    \begin{lstlisting}
    import com.example.demo.Security.JWTUtils;
    \end{lstlisting}
  \item \textbf{Agar method ko direct use karna hai toh \texttt{static import} ka use karo.}
\end{itemize}

---
===============================

% Document begins
\begin{document}

% Title
\begin{center}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]
  {\bfseries\Huge\color{headingblue} Complete Explanation of SecurityConfig in Spring Boot \par}

\end{tcolorbox}
  
\end{center}

% Introduction
\section{Introduction}
Spring Boot me **Spring Security** ka use **authentication aur authorization** handle karne ke liye hota hai.  
\textcolor{examplered}{Ye `SecurityConfig` file ek middleware ki tarah kaam karti hai jo requests ko filter karti hai.}  
\textcolor{examplered}{Yeh `Interceptor` se different hai kyunki yeh request ko unauthorized hone pe reject bhi kar sakta hai.}

Agar tum Express.js se relate karna chahte ho, to:
- \textbf{Interceptor} ≈ `app.use(middleware)`
- \textbf{Spring Security Middleware} ≈ `app.use(authMiddleware)`

---

% Step 1: SecurityConfig File Ka Role
\section{SecurityConfig File Ka Role}
\subsection{Spring Boot me Security Middleware (Interceptor se Different)}
\begin{center}
  \begin{tabular}{|>{\columncolor{headingblue!30}}p{4cm}|>{\columncolor{examplered!30}}p{4cm}|>{\columncolor{yellow!30}}p{4cm}|}
    \hline
    \textbf{Feature} & \textbf{Spring Security (`SecurityConfig`)} & \textbf{Interceptor (`LoggingInterceptor`)} \\
    \hline
    Purpose & Authentication \& Authorization & Logging, Custom Rules \\
    \hline
    Request Control & Unauthorized request ko reject karta hai & Request ko log ya modify karta hai \\
    \hline
    Registration & `SecurityFilterChain` in `SecurityConfig` & `InterceptorRegistry` in `WebConfig` \\
    \hline
  \end{tabular}
\end{center}

---

% Step 2: SecurityConfig.java Code Explanation
\section{SecurityConfig.java Code Explanation}
\textbf{src/main/java/com/example/demo/Config/SecurityConfig.java}

\begin{examplebox}{SecurityConfig.java}
\begin{lstlisting}
package com.example.demo.Config;

import org.springframework.context.annotation.Bean;
import org.springframework.context.annotation.Configuration;
import org.springframework.security.config.annotation.web.builders.HttpSecurity;
import org.springframework.security.crypto.bcrypt.BCryptPasswordEncoder;
import org.springframework.security.crypto.password.PasswordEncoder;
import org.springframework.security.web.SecurityFilterChain;

import static org.springframework.security.config.Customizer.withDefaults;

@Configuration  // Batata hai ki yeh ek configuration class hai
public class SecurityConfig {

    // Step 1: Password Encoding (For Storing Hashed Passwords)
    @Bean
    public PasswordEncoder passwordEncoder() {
        return new BCryptPasswordEncoder(); // Passwords ko hash karne ke liye BCrypt use kar rahe hain
    }

    // Step 2: Security Filter Chain (Authentication & Authorization)
    @Bean
    public SecurityFilterChain securityFilterChain(HttpSecurity http) throws Exception {
        http
                .csrf(csrf -> csrf.disable())  // CSRF protection disable (sirf testing ke liye)
                .authorizeHttpRequests(auth -> auth
                        .requestMatchers("/users/login", "/users/signup", "/users/test").permitAll()  // Public APIs
                        .anyRequest().authenticated() // Baki sab requests secure hongi
                )
                .httpBasic(withDefaults())  // Basic Authentication enable
                .formLogin(form -> form.disable()); // Default Spring Boot Login Form ko disable kar rahe hain

        return http.build();
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

---

% Step 3: SecurityConfig Ka Step-by-Step Breakdown
\section{SecurityConfig Ka Step-by-Step Breakdown}
\subsection{Step 1: `@Configuration` (Spring Boot ko batana ki yeh ek config file hai)}
\begin{lstlisting}
@Configuration
public class SecurityConfig {
\end{lstlisting}
\textcolor{examplered}{Isse Spring Boot automatically is class ko load karega.}

---

\subsection{Step 2: Password Encoder (`BCryptPasswordEncoder`)}
\begin{lstlisting}
@Bean
public PasswordEncoder passwordEncoder() {
    return new BCryptPasswordEncoder();
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textcolor{examplered}{Yeh `passwordEncoder()` function passwords ko hash karne ke liye use hota hai.}  
\textcolor{examplered}{Agar tum user password database me store kar rahe ho, to yeh plain text ke bajaye encrypted format me store karega.}

---

\subsection{Step 3: Security Rules (Middleware for Authentication)}
\begin{lstlisting}
@Bean
public SecurityFilterChain securityFilterChain(HttpSecurity http) throws Exception {
\end{lstlisting}
\textcolor{examplered}{Yeh function `SecurityFilterChain` ko return karta hai, jo ek middleware jaisa kaam karta hai.}  
\textcolor{examplered}{Yeh har request ko check karega ki yeh public hai ya authentication required hai.}

---

\subsection{Step 4: CSRF Protection Disable (Testing Mode)}
\begin{lstlisting}
.csrf(csrf -> csrf.disable())  
\end{lstlisting}
\textcolor{examplered}{CSRF (Cross-Site Request Forgery) security ko disable kar rahe hain.}  
\textcolor{examplered}{Production me isko enable rakhna zaroori hai.}

---

\subsection{Step 5: Public Routes (Permit Some APIs)}
\begin{lstlisting}
.authorizeHttpRequests(auth -> auth
        .requestMatchers("/users/login", "/users/signup", "/users/test").permitAll()  
\end{lstlisting}
\textcolor{examplered}{Yeh batata hai ki `/users/login`, `/users/signup`, aur `/users/test` routes sabko access mil sakta hai.}  
\textcolor{examplered}{Iska matlab yeh APIs bina login ke bhi accessible hongi.}

---

\subsection{Step 6: Secure Other Routes}
\begin{lstlisting}
.anyRequest().authenticated()
\end{lstlisting}
\textcolor{examplered}{Iska matlab hai ki jo routes explicitly allow nahi kiye gaye, wo sabhi authentication ke bina access nahi kiye ja sakte.}  
\textcolor{examplered}{Agar koi unauthenticated user `/users/profile` API call karega, to `401 Unauthorized` error milega.}

---

\subsection{Step 7: Enable Basic Authentication}
\begin{lstlisting}
.httpBasic(withDefaults())
\end{lstlisting}
\textcolor{examplered}{Yeh Basic Authentication enable karta hai.}  
\textcolor{examplered}{Agar tum JWT ya OAuth use kar rahe ho, to isko disable karke custom authentication use kar sakte ho.}

---

\subsection{Step 8: Disable Default Spring Security Login Form}
\begin{lstlisting}
.formLogin(form -> form.disable());
\end{lstlisting}
\textcolor{examplered}{By default, Spring Security ek login form dikhata hai.}  
\textcolor{examplered}{Isko disable kar diya gaya hai kyunki hum sirf API authentication chahte hain.}

---

% Step 4: SecurityConfig Ko Register Kaise Kiya Gaya Hai?
\section{SecurityConfig Ko Register Kaise Kiya Gaya Hai?}
\textcolor{examplered}{Spring Boot me `@Configuration` aur `@Bean` use karke automatic registration hoti hai.}  
\textcolor{examplered}{Agar tum Spring Boot me `SecurityConfig` likh dete ho, to Spring Boot khud isko middleware jaisa treat karega.}  
\textcolor{examplered}{Alag se `WebConfig` me register karne ki zaroorat nahi hai.}

---

% Step 5: SecurityConfig Test Karne Ke Liye Postman Requests
\section{SecurityConfig Test Karne Ke Liye Postman Requests}
\subsection{Public APIs (Allowed Without Login)}
\begin{lstlisting}
GET http://localhost:8080/users/test
\end{lstlisting}
\textcolor{examplered}{Response:}
\begin{lstlisting}
{
  "message": "This is a public API"
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textcolor{examplered}{Ye request bina authentication ke allow hogi.}

---

\subsection{Secure API (Unauthorized Without Login)}
\begin{lstlisting}
GET http://localhost:8080/users/profile
\end{lstlisting}
\textcolor{examplered}{Response:}  
\begin{lstlisting}
{
  "error": "Unauthorized"
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textcolor{examplered}{Ye request `401 Unauthorized` dega, kyunki authentication required hai.}

---

\subsection{Secure API (With Authentication)}
\begin{lstlisting}
GET http://localhost:8080/users/profile
Authorization: Basic <base64-encoded-username:password>
\end{lstlisting}
\textcolor{examplered}{Agar tum username/password sahi bhejoge to request authorized ho jayegi.}  

\textcolor{examplered}{Agar tum JWT use karna chahte ho, to `httpBasic(withDefaults())` hata ke JWT middleware use kar sakte ho.}

---

% Final Summary
\section{Final Summary}
\begin{center}
  \begin{tabular}{|>{\columncolor{headingblue!30}}p{4cm}|>{\columncolor{examplered!30}}p{4cm}|>{\columncolor{yellow!30}}p{4cm}|}
    \hline
    \textbf{Feature} & \textbf{Function} & \textbf{Role} \\
    \hline
    `@Configuration` & SecurityConfig class ko Spring Boot me register karta hai & Middleware define karta hai \\
    \hline
    `PasswordEncoder` & `BCryptPasswordEncoder` & Passwords ko hash karne ke liye \\
    \hline
    `SecurityFilterChain` & `http.authorizeHttpRequests()` & Security rules define karta hai \\
    \hline
    `csrf.disable()` & CSRF protection disable karta hai & Sirf testing ke liye \\
    \hline
    `.permitAll()` & Public APIs allow karta hai & `/users/login`, `/users/signup` ko authentication ke bina allow karta hai \\
    \hline
    `.anyRequest().authenticated()` & Baki sabhi routes secure karta hai & Agar login nahi kiya to `401 Unauthorized` dega \\
    \hline
    `.httpBasic(withDefaults())` & Basic Authentication enable karta hai & Default username/password se login karne ke liye \\
    \hline
    `.formLogin().disable()` & Default login form disable karta hai & Sirf API authentication allow karta hai \\
    \hline
  \end{tabular}
\end{center}

---

% Conclusion
\section{Conclusion}
\textcolor{examplered}{Spring Boot me `SecurityConfig` ek middleware ki tarah kaam karta hai jo requests ko authenticate karta hai.}  
\textcolor{examplered}{Agar kisi request ko authentication ki zaroorat hai aur user login nahi hai, to `401 Unauthorized` error aayega.}  
\textcolor{examplered}{Agar tum JWT use karna chahte ho to `httpBasic()` hata kar JWT middleware use kar sakte ho.}  

\textcolor{examplered}{Ab tum `SecurityConfig` ko easily implement kar sakte ho aur APIs ko secure kar sakte ho!}

---

===============================
\hrule



% Define colors
\definecolor{blue}{RGB}{0,102,204}
\definecolor{red}{RGB}{0,153,76}
\definecolor{red}{RGB}{204,0,0}
\definecolor{lightblue}{RGB}{173,216,230}
\definecolor{lightred}{RGB}{144,238,144}

% Define code block style
\lstdefinestyle{javaStyle}{
    backgroundcolor=\color{lightblue},
    basicstyle=\ttfamily\footnotesize,
    keywordstyle=\color{blue}\bfseries,
    stringstyle=\color{red},
    commentstyle=\color{red},
    breaklines=true,
    frame=single,
    morekeywords={public, class, package, import, static, void, new, extends}
}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]

\title{\textbf{\textcolor{violet}{\huge Rules for Class Names and Filenames in Java (Spring Boot}}}

\end{tcolorbox}


\begin{document}

\maketitle

\section*{\color{blue} Importance of Matching Class Name and Filename}
Spring Boot (aur Java me generally) me \textbf{class ka naam filename se match hona chahiye}. Agar aisa nahi hota, to aapko \textbf{compilation error} milega.

\section*{\color{blue} ✅ Rules for Class Names and Filenames}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]

\subsection*{1. \textbf{Class Name = File Name}}
Agar aapki class ka naam \texttt{UserSignupEntity} hai, to file ka naam bhi \textbf{UserSignupEntity.java} hona chahiye.

\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Example:}
\begin{lstlisting}[style=javaStyle]
public class UserSignupEntity {
    // class content
}
\end{lstlisting}
✅ \textbf{Filename:} \texttt{UserSignupEntity.java}

\subsection*{2. \textbf{Case-Sensitive}}
Java \textbf{case-sensitive} hota hai, to \texttt{UserSignupEntity.java} aur \texttt{usersignupentity.java} alag files maani jayengi.

\subsection*{3. \textbf{Public Classes Must Match File Name}}
Agar class \texttt{public} hai, to filename aur class name exactly match karna chahiye.

\textbf{❌ Wrong Example:}
\begin{itemize}
    \item File: \texttt{User.java}
    \item Class inside:
\end{itemize}
\begin{lstlisting}[style=javaStyle]
public class UserSignupEntity { }  // ❌ Will cause compilation error
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{4. \textbf{Package Naming}}
Agar class kisi package me hai \texttt{package com.example.demo.entity;}, to:
\begin{itemize}
    \item ✅ \textbf{File Path:} \texttt{src/main/java/com/example/demo/entity/UserSignupEntity.java}
\end{itemize}

\section*{\color{red} �� What Happens if Class Name and File Name Don't Match?}
Aapko \textbf{compilation error} milega:
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=lightblue, colframe=red]
\texttt{Error: The public type UserSignupEntity must be defined in its own file}
\end{tcolorbox}

===============================
