\begin{document}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]

\title{\textbf{\textcolor{violet}{\huge Spring Boot: Understanding \texttt{findByEmail()} and Objects in Simple Terms}}}}

\end{tcolorbox}

\author{}
\date{}
\maketitle

\section*{\textcolor{headingcolor}{1. What is an Object? (Simple Explanation)}}

\subsection*{\textcolor{headingcolor}{Definition:}}  
An \textbf{object} is a \textbf{real-world instance of a class}.  
A \textbf{class} is like a \textbf{blueprint}, and an \textbf{object} is an \textbf{actual usable item} made from it.  

\subsection*{\textcolor{headingcolor}{Example: \texttt{UserSignupEntity} Class (Blueprint)}}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
public class UserSignupEntity {
    private Long id;
    private String email;
    private String password;
    private String role;

    // Constructor
    public UserSignupEntity(Long id, String email, String password, String role) {
        this.id = id;
        this.email = email;
        this.password = password;
        this.role = role;
    }

    // Getter Method
    public String getEmail() {
        return email;
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textcolor{important}{☝️ This class defines a user, but it's just a structure (blueprint).}  

\subsection*{\textcolor{headingcolor}{Example: Creating Objects from Class}}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
UserSignupEntity user1 = new UserSignupEntity(1L, "satyam@gmail.com", "password123", "USER");
UserSignupEntity user2 = new UserSignupEntity(2L, "john@gmail.com", "johnpass", "ADMIN");
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{�� Think of a class as a Car Blueprint, and objects as real Honda City, BMW, etc. ��}  

\section*{\textcolor{headingcolor}{2. Understanding \texttt{Optional<UserSignupEntity> findByEmail(String email);}}}

\subsection*{\textcolor{headingcolor}{What is This?}}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
Optional<UserSignupEntity> findByEmail(String email);
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{This method helps fetch a user from the database using their email.}

\subsection*{\textcolor{headingcolor}{Breaking It Down}}
\begin{tabular}{|c|l|}
\hline
\textbf{Keyword} & \textbf{Meaning} \\
\hline
\texttt{Optional<>} & \textbf{Wrapper that may or may not contain a value} \\
\hline
\texttt{UserSignupEntity} & \textbf{Type of object inside Optional} (user details) \\
\hline
\texttt{findByEmail(String email)} & \textbf{Method name (Spring Boot converts it into SQL query)} \\
\hline
\texttt{String email} & \textbf{Input parameter (email we are searching for)} \\
\hline
\end{tabular}

\subsection*{\textcolor{headingcolor}{Example Query That Spring Generates}}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=SQL]
SELECT * FROM users WHERE email = 'satyam@gmail.com' LIMIT 1;
\end{lstlisting}
\textcolor{important}{✅ No need to write SQL manually, Spring JPA does it for us!}

\section*{\textcolor{headingcolor}{3. Where to Define \texttt{findByEmail()}?}}

\subsection*{\textcolor{headingcolor}{Correct Repository Code}}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
public interface UserSignupRepository extends JpaRepository<UserSignupEntity, Long> {
    Optional<UserSignupEntity> findByEmail(String email); // ✅ Auto-generates SQL query
}
\end{lstlisting}

\section*{\textcolor{headingcolor}{4. How to Use \texttt{findByEmail()} in a Service Class?}}

\subsection*{\textcolor{headingcolor}{Correct Usage in Service Class}}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
public UserSignupEntity findByEmail(String email) {
    Optional<UserSignupEntity> userOptional = userSignupRepository.findByEmail(email);
    return userOptional.orElse(null); // If user is not found, return null
}
\end{lstlisting}

\textcolor{important}{�� Better Approach: Throw Exception Instead of Returning Null}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
public UserSignupEntity findByEmail(String email) {
    return userSignupRepository.findByEmail(email)
           .orElseThrow(() -> new RuntimeException("User not found with email: " + email));
}
\end{lstlisting}

\section*{\textcolor{headingcolor}{5. Why Do We Define \texttt{findByEmail()} in Repository?}}

\begin{tabular}{|c|l|}
\hline
\textbf{Reason} & \textbf{Explanation} \\
\hline
�� \textbf{Auto Query Generation} & Spring JPA \textbf{automatically creates SQL}. \\
\hline
✅ \textbf{Less Code Needed} & No need to write complex SQL queries. \\
\hline
�� \textbf{Direct Database Access} & \texttt{findByEmail()} directly calls the DB. \\
\hline
�� \textbf{Prevents Errors} & Using \texttt{Optional} avoids \texttt{NullPointerException}. \\
\hline
\end{tabular}

\section*{\textcolor{headingcolor}{�� Final Summary}}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{An object} is a real-world instance of a class.
    \item \texttt{findByEmail(String email)} is a method that automatically generates an SQL query.
    \item We define it inside \texttt{UserSignupRepository} to let Spring Boot handle JPA queries.
\end{itemize}

\textcolor{important}{✅ Now you fully understand Objects, Repositories, and Optional! ��}

===============================
\hrule

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]


\title{\textbf{\textcolor{violet}{\huge Spring Boot: Understanding `findByEmail()` \& Other Repository Methods}}}

\end{tcolorbox}


\begin{document}

% Title Page
\maketitle

% Introduction
\section{Introduction}
Ye guide \textbf{Objects, Optional, Repository, aur Query Methods} ko Spring Boot me samjhane me madad karegi. Chaliye step-by-step samjhte hain.

---

% Section 1: Pre-Built Methods from JpaRepository
\section{Pre-Built Methods from `JpaRepository` (No Need to Define)}
Spring Boot me `JpaRepository` \textbf{kuch important CRUD methods automatically provide karta hai}, jinhe hume manually likhne ki zaroorat nahi hoti. Agar hum `UserSignupRepository` ko `JpaRepository` se extend karte hain, to ye methods automatically available ho jate hain:

\begin{examplebox}{Pre-Built Methods}
\begin{lstlisting}
userSignupRepository.findById(1L);  // ✅ Find by ID
userSignupRepository.findAll();     // ✅ Get all users
userSignupRepository.save(user);    // ✅ Save a new user
userSignupRepository.deleteById(1L); // ✅ Delete user by ID
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

\textcolor{warningred}{\textbf{�� In methods ko likhne ki koi zaroorat nahi hoti, ye built-in hote hain!}}

---

% Section 2: Custom Query Methods (Auto-Generated by Spring Boot)
\section{Custom Query Methods (Auto-Generated by Spring Boot)}
`findByEmail()` ke alawa, aap aur bhi \textbf{custom query methods} define kar sakte ho \textbf{Spring JPA ke naming conventions} ka use karke. Spring Boot \textbf{automatically SQL query generate karega}.

\subsection{Custom Methods Ka Example}
\begin{examplebox}{Custom Query Methods}
\begin{lstlisting}
public interface UserSignupRepository extends JpaRepository<UserSignupEntity, Long> {
    
    // ✅ Find user by email
    Optional<UserSignupEntity> findByEmail(String email);

    // ✅ Find users by role
    List<UserSignupEntity> findByRole(String role);  

    // ✅ Find users who signed up after a certain date
    List<UserSignupEntity> findByCreatedAtAfter(Timestamp timestamp);

    // ✅ Find active users
    List<UserSignupEntity> findByIsActiveTrue();

    // ✅ Find users whose email contains a specific string (like search)
    List<UserSignupEntity> findByEmailContaining(String keyword);
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

\textcolor{warningred}{\textbf{�� Isme hume SQL likhne ki koi zaroorat nahi hai, Spring Boot khud query generate karega!}}

---





% Section 3: Custom Queries with @Query
\section{Custom Queries with `@Query` (Jab Naming Convention Kaafi Nahi Hota)}
Kabhi kabhi complex queries likhni hoti hain jo \textbf{naming convention se possible nahi hoti}. Aise cases me hum `@Query` annotation ka use kar sakte hain.

\subsection{Example: Get Users with Role = "ADMIN"}
\begin{examplebox}{Custom Query Example}
\begin{lstlisting}
@Query("SELECT u FROM UserSignupEntity u WHERE u.role = 'ADMIN'")
List<UserSignupEntity> findAdmins();
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

\subsubsection{�� When Will This Query Execute?}
Jab bhi `findAdmins()` function ko call kiya jayega, Spring Boot **automatically is query ko execute karega**. Ye function database se **sabhi users jinka role 'ADMIN' hai unko fetch karega**. Iska use tab hoga jab hume sirf administrators ki list chahiye.






\subsubsection{�� Dynamic Role Fetching (Passing Variable Instead of 'ADMIN')}
Agar hume hardcoded 'ADMIN' ke jagah kisi bhi role ka data fetch karna hai, toh hum `@Query` me variable pass kar sakte hain:

\begin{examplebox}{Dynamic Role Query}
\begin{lstlisting}
@Query("SELECT u FROM UserSignupEntity u WHERE u.role = :role")
List<UserSignupEntity> findUsersByRole(@Param("role") String role);
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

\textbf{�� Explanation:}  
- `:role` → Yeh **named parameter** hai jo query ke andar **dynamically replace** hoga.  
- `@Param("role")` → Iska kaam hai method ke argument `role` ko SQL query ke `:role` placeholder se link karna.  

\textbf{�� How This Query Gets Executed?}  
Jab bhi `findUsersByRole("ADMIN")` call hoga, Spring Boot **automatically executes** the following SQL query:

\begin{lstlisting}
SELECT * FROM users WHERE role = 'ADMIN';
\end{lstlisting}

Agar hum `findUsersByRole("USER")` call karte hain, to SQL query kuch aise banegi:

\begin{lstlisting}
SELECT * FROM users WHERE role = 'USER';
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{�� Usage in Service Layer:}  
Repository method `findUsersByRole()` ko service class me aise call kiya jata hai:

\begin{examplebox}{Calling the Method in Service Class}
\begin{lstlisting}
List<UserSignupEntity> admins = userSignupRepository.findUsersByRole("ADMIN"); // Fetch Admins
List<UserSignupEntity> users = userSignupRepository.findUsersByRole("USER");  // Fetch Normal Users
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

\textbf{�� Key Takeaways:}  
- `@Query` ka use tab hota hai jab built-in naming conventions kaafi nahi hote.  
- `@Param` annotation se hum dynamic values SQL query me inject kar sakte hain.  
- `findUsersByRole("ADMIN")` call hone par `ADMIN` role ke users fetch honge.  
- `findUsersByRole("USER")` call hone par `USER` role ke users fetch honge.  

�� Ab aap kisi bhi role ka data dynamically fetch kar sakte hain! ��






\textcolor{warningred}{\textbf{✅ Ye queries database me directly SQL run karne ke liye kaam aati hain.}}

---

% Section 4: Using @Modifying for Update & Delete Queries
\section{Using `@Modifying` for Update \& Delete Queries}
Agar aap \textbf{koi record update ya delete karna chahte ho bina entity ko pehle fetch kiye}, to `@Modifying` use kar sakte ho.

\subsection{Example: Soft Delete a User (Mark as Inactive)}
\begin{examplebox}{@Modifying Example}
\begin{lstlisting}
@Modifying
@Query("UPDATE UserSignupEntity u SET u.isActive = false WHERE u.email = :email")
void deactivateUser(@Param("email") String email);
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

\textcolor{warningred}{\textbf{✅ Iska fayda ye hai ki poori entity ko fetch kiye bina hi `isActive` field update ho jayegi, jo performance ke liye accha hai.}}

---

% Section 5: Summary
\section{Summary: Repository Me Kya Kya Methods Use Kar Sakte Hain?}
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{|p{5cm}|p{6cm}|p{4cm}|}
    \hline
    \textbf{Method Type} & \textbf{Example} & \textbf{Kya Manually Likhnana Zaroori Hai?} \\
    \hline
    \textbf{Basic CRUD Methods} & `findById(Long id)`, `findAll()` & \textcolor{warningred}{❌ No (Built-in)} \\
    \hline
    \textbf{Find by Field Name} & `findByEmail(String email)`, `findByRole(String role)` & \textcolor{warningred}{✅ Yes (Spring generates query)} \\
    \hline
    \textbf{Comparison Queries} & `findByCreatedAtAfter(Timestamp t)` & \textcolor{warningred}{✅ Yes} \\
    \hline
    \textbf{Boolean Queries} & `findByIsActiveTrue()` & \textcolor{warningred}{✅ Yes} \\
    \hline
    \textbf{Search Queries} & `findByEmailContaining(String keyword)` & \textcolor{warningred}{✅ Yes} \\
    \hline
    \textbf{Custom SQL Queries} & `@Query("SELECT u FROM UserSignupEntity u WHERE u.role = 'ADMIN'")` & \textcolor{warningred}{✅ Yes} \\
    \hline
    \textbf{Update Queries} & `@Modifying @Query("UPDATE UserSignupEntity u SET u.isActive = false WHERE u.email = :email")` & \textcolor{warningred}{✅ Yes} \\
    \hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

---

% Section 6: Final Answer
\section{Final Answer: Kya Sirf `findByEmail()` Use Kar Sakte Hain?}
\textcolor{warningred}{\textbf{✔ Nahi! Aap bohot saare custom methods use kar sakte ho repository me.}}  
\textcolor{warningred}{\textbf{✔ Spring Boot method naming conventions ka use karke queries automatically generate kar sakta hai.}}  
\textcolor{warningred}{\textbf{✔ Agar complex query likhni ho to `@Query` ka use karo.}}  
\textcolor{warningred}{\textbf{✔ Agar kisi record ko update/delete karna ho bina fetch kiye, to `@Modifying` ka use karo.}}  

\textcolor{warningred}{\textbf{�� Ab aap apni repository me aur bhi powerful queries likh sakte ho!}} Agar aur doubts hain to batao! ��  

---

% Section 7: Notes for You
\section{Notes for You}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{Objects:} Java me objects real-world entities ko represent karte hain. Example: `UserSignupEntity` ek object hai jo database ke table ko represent karta hai.  
    \item \textbf{Optional:} Ye ek container object hai jo null values ko handle karta hai. Example: `Optional<UserSignupEntity>` ka matlab hai ki result null ho sakta hai.  
    \item \textbf{Repository:} Ye ek interface hai jo database operations ko handle karta hai. Example: `UserSignupRepository`.  
    \item \textbf{Query Methods:} Ye methods database se data fetch karne ke liye use hote hain. Example: `findByEmail()`, `findByRole()`.  
\end{itemize}

---

% Section 8: Tips for Better Understanding
\section{Tips for Better Understanding}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{Practice Karo:} Khud se custom methods likhkar dekho aur unhe test karo.  
    \item \textbf{Debugging:} Agar query sahi se kaam nahi kar rahi hai, to logs check karo aur SQL query ko database me manually run karke dekho.  
    \item \textbf{Documentation Padho:} Spring Data JPA ki official documentation padhne se aur samjh aayegi.  
\end{itemize}

---

% Section 9: Frequently Asked Questions (FAQs)
\section{Frequently Asked Questions (FAQs)}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{Q: Kya hum ek se zyada fields ke basis par query likh sakte hain?}  
    \textbf{A:} Haan! Example: `findByEmailAndRole(String email, String role)`.  

    \item \textbf{Q: Agar hume koi custom SQL query likhni hai to kya karein?}  
    \textbf{A:} `@Query` annotation ka use karo aur query likh do. Example:  
    \begin{lstlisting}
    @Query("SELECT u FROM UserSignupEntity u WHERE u.email = :email AND u.role = :role")
    Optional<UserSignupEntity> findByEmailAndRole(@Param("email") String email, @Param("role") String role);
    \end{lstlisting}

    \item \textbf{Q: `@Modifying` ka use kyu karte hain?}  
    \textbf{A:} `@Modifying` ka use tab karte hain jab hum database me koi update ya delete operation karna chahte hain bina entity ko fetch kiye.  
\end{itemize}

---

% Section 10: Conclusion
\section{Conclusion}
Spring Boot me `findByEmail()` jaise methods ka use karke aap easily database se data fetch kar sakte hain. Iske alawa, aap custom methods aur complex queries bhi likh sakte hain. Bas thoda practice karo aur concepts ko samjho, aap khud hi expert ban jaoge! ��  

Agar aur kuch samajhna hai ya koi doubt hai to pooch sakte ho!

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]

\title{\textbf{\textcolor{violet}{\huge Spring Boot: Understanding \texttt{@ManyToOne}, and Foreign key}}}

\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{document}

\maketitle




\section*{\color{purple} 1️⃣ Understanding \texttt{@ManyToOne} and \texttt{@JoinColumn} in \texttt{Todo} Entity}

In \texttt{Todo} entity, we want to store the user who created the To-Do. Since \textbf{one user can have multiple To-Dos}, we define a \textbf{Many-To-One relationship} where multiple To-Dos belong to a single user. 

\subsection*{\color{darkblue} �� Code: \texttt{@ManyToOne} Relationship in \texttt{Todo} Entity}
\begin{lstlisting}[style=mystyle, language=Java]
@ManyToOne // ✅ Relationship: Many Todos belong to one User
@JoinColumn(name = "user_id", nullable = false) // Foreign Key (Links to User table)
private UserSignupEntity user;
\end{lstlisting}

\section*{\color{darkblue} �� Line-by-Line Explanation (Hinglish Style) ��}

\subsection*{\color{darkblue} 1️⃣ \texttt{@ManyToOne} - Ek User Ke Multiple To-Dos Ho Sakte Hain}
\begin{lstlisting}[style=mystyle, language=Java]
@ManyToOne // ✅ Relationship: Many Todos belong to one User
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{�� Iska Matlab:}  
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{Ek user ke multiple To-Dos ho sakte hain.}  
    \item \textbf{Ek To-Do sirf ek user ka hoga.}  
    \item \textbf{Database me, \texttt{user\_id} foreign key hoga jo \texttt{users} table se link karega.}  
\end{itemize}

\textbf{�� Example Data in Tables:}  

\begin{longtable}{|c|c|}
\hline
\textbf{User Table (\texttt{users})} & \textbf{Todo Table (\texttt{todo})} \\
\hline
id: 1 (satyam@gmail.com) & id: 101, user\_id: 1, title: "Learn Spring Boot" \\
id: 1 (satyam@gmail.com) & id: 102, user\_id: 1, title: "Build JWT Auth" \\
id: 2 (john@gmail.com) & id: 103, user\_id: 2, title: "Complete Project" \\
\hline
\end{longtable}

\textbf{☝️ Dekh sakte ho, ek user (id: 1) ke multiple To-Dos ho sakte hain!}

\subsection*{\color{darkblue} 2️⃣ \texttt{@JoinColumn(name = "user\_id")} - Foreign Key Define Karta Hai}
\begin{lstlisting}[style=mystyle, language=Java]
@JoinColumn(name = "user_id", nullable = false) // Foreign Key (Links to User table)
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{�� Iska Matlab:}  
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{\texttt{user\_id} ek foreign key hoga} jo \texttt{users} table ke \texttt{id} column se linked rahega.  
    \item \textbf{\texttt{nullable = false}} ka matlab hai ki \textbf{har To-Do kisi ek user ke under aana zaroori hai}.  
\end{itemize}

\textbf{�� Database Table Structure (\texttt{todo} Table in SQL):}  
\begin{lstlisting}[style=mystyle, language=SQL]
CREATE TABLE todo (
    id BIGINT AUTO_INCREMENT PRIMARY KEY,
    user_id BIGINT NOT NULL, -- Foreign Key
    title VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL,
    description TEXT,
    completed BOOLEAN DEFAULT FALSE,
    created_at TIMESTAMP DEFAULT CURRENT_TIMESTAMP,
    FOREIGN KEY (user_id) REFERENCES users(id) -- ✅ Linking to Users table
);
\end{lstlisting}

✅ \textbf{Dekh sakte ho ki \texttt{user\_id} \texttt{users} table ke \texttt{id} se connected hai!}

\subsection*{\color{darkblue} 3️⃣ \texttt{UserSignupEntity} Kya Hai?}
\texttt{UserSignupEntity} ek \textbf{model (entity)} hai jo \texttt{users} table ko represent karta hai. Is entity ke andar \textbf{id, email, password, role, aur createdAt fields hoti hain.}  

\textbf{�� \texttt{UserSignupEntity} Example:}  
\begin{lstlisting}[style=mystyle, language=Java]
@Entity
@Table(name = "users")
public class UserSignupEntity {

    @Id
    @GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY)
    private Long id;

    @Column(unique = true, nullable = false)
    private String email;

    @Column(nullable = false)
    private String password;

    @Column(nullable = false)
    private String role;

    @Column(name = "created_at", updatable = false)
    private Timestamp createdAt;
}
\end{lstlisting}

�� \textbf{Is entity ka \texttt{id} field \texttt{user\_id} ke saath \texttt{todo} table me foreign key ke roop me use hoga.}

\section*{\color{darkblue} �� Summary (Hinglish Me)}
\begin{longtable}{|c|p{10cm}|}
\hline
\textbf{Concept} & \textbf{Explanation} \\
\hline
\texttt{@ManyToOne} & Ek User ke multiple To-Dos ho sakte hain, lekin ek To-Do sirf ek user ka hoga. \\
\hline
\texttt{@JoinColumn(name = "user\_id")} & \texttt{user\_id} field \texttt{users} table ke \texttt{id} column se link karega (Foreign Key). \\
\hline
\texttt{UserSignupEntity} & Ye \texttt{users} table ka model hai jo \texttt{id, email, password, role, createdAt} fields ko represent karta hai. \\
\hline
\end{longtable}

% Begin document
\begin{document}

% Title

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]

\title{\textbf{\textcolor{violet}{\huge Understanding `@RequestAttribute` in Spring}}}

\end{tcolorbox}

\section{Introduction}
`@RequestAttribute` is a Spring annotation that allows you to access data added as an attribute to the \texttt{HttpServletRequest}. This is typically used when an interceptor or middleware adds attributes to the request, and you need to retrieve them in a controller.

\section{Hinglish Notes on `@RequestAttribute`}
\subsection{`@RequestAttribute` Kya Hai?}
\textcolor{highlightblue}{`@RequestAttribute`} ek Spring annotation hai jo \textbf{HTTP request attributes} ko controller me access karne ke liye use hota hai. Yeh un data ko fetch karne ke liye kaam aata hai jo middleware (jaise ki Interceptor) ne request me add kiye hain.

\begin{itemize}
  \item \textbf{Source:} \textcolor{highlightred}{Interceptor, middleware}, ya kisi aur layer ne request me attribute add kiya hoga.
  \item \textbf{Purpose:} \textcolor{importantred}{Request ke andar ke attributes ko controller tak leke jaana.}
\end{itemize}

\section{Example in Hinglish}
\subsection{Interceptor Me Attribute Add Karna}
Interceptor ke \texttt{preHandle()} method me request attribute set karte hain:

\begin{tcolorbox}[note, title=Java Code Example: Interceptor]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java, basicstyle=\ttfamily\small, backgroundcolor=\color{lightblue}, frame=single]
@Component
public class LoggingInterceptor implements HandlerInterceptor {

    @Override
    public boolean preHandle(HttpServletRequest request, HttpServletResponse response, Object handler) {
        // User ID attribute add karte hain
        request.setAttribute("userId", 101); 
        return true; // Proceed with the request
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsection{Controller Me Attribute Access Karna}
Controller me \textcolor{highlightblue}{`@RequestAttribute`} annotation ke through yeh attribute access karte hain:

\begin{tcolorbox}[note, title=Java Code Example: Controller]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java, basicstyle=\ttfamily\small, backgroundcolor=\color{lightblue}, frame=single]
@RestController
@RequestMapping("/todo")
public class TodoController {

    @GetMapping("/test")
    public String testAttribute(@RequestAttribute("userId") Integer userId) {
        return "Logged-in User ID: " + userId;
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\section{Flow}
\begin{enumerate}
    \item \textbf{Interceptor:} \textcolor{highlightblue}{`userId`} ko \texttt{request.setAttribute("userId", value)} ke through request me set karta hai.
    \item \textbf{Controller:} \textcolor{highlightred}{`@RequestAttribute("userId")`} ke zariye us value ko fetch karta hai.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Output}
Agar request \texttt{/todo/test} API par jati hai, to response me ye milega:

\begin{tcolorbox}[note, title=Output]
\begin{lstlisting}[backgroundcolor=\color{lightblue}, frame=single]
Logged-in User ID: 101
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\section{Key Points}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{`@RequestAttribute`} un attributes ko fetch karta hai jo middleware ya interceptor me set hote hain.
    \item Yeh \textbf{request-scoped} hota hai (sirf current request ke liye valid).
    \item \textcolor{highlightred}{Common use cases:} \textcolor{importantred}{JWT token validation}, user roles, ya custom headers process karna.
\end{itemize}

Aise explain karo to ye samajhne aur likhne ke liye easy hoga. \textcolor{highlightblue}{�� Let me know if you'd like further help!}

% Colors
\definecolor{myblue}{RGB}{70,130,180}
\definecolor{mygreen}{RGB}{34,139,34}
\definecolor{myred}{RGB}{220,20,60}
\definecolor{mypurple}{RGB}{128,0,128}
\definecolor{codegray}{gray}{0.9}

% Java code style
\lstset{
    language=Java,
    basicstyle=\ttfamily\footnotesize,
    backgroundcolor=\color{codegray},
    keywordstyle=\color{myblue}\bfseries,
    commentstyle=\color{mygreen}\itshape,
    stringstyle=\color{mypurple},
    showstringspaces=false,
    frame=single,
    breaklines=true
}

\begin{document}


\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]

\title{\textbf{\textcolor{violet}{\huge {Hinglish Notes:} \texttt{ResponseEntity<?>} Simplified with Full Explanation}}}

\end{tcolorbox}

\subsection*{\textcolor{mypurple}{Problem Without \texttt{ResponseEntity<?>}}}

Pehle yeh samjho ki \textbf{\texttt{ResponseEntity<?>}} kyun zaroori hai. Agar hum \texttt{ResponseEntity<?>} ka use nahi karte, to:

\begin{enumerate}
    \item \textbf{\textcolor{myred}{Default Status Code Problem:}}
    \begin{itemize}
        \item Controller directly object ya string return karega, to Spring hamesha \texttt{200 OK} status code bhejta hai.
        \item Chahe data na mile ya koi error ho, response ka status \texttt{200 OK} hi hoga, jo galat indication deta hai.
    \end{itemize}

    \item \textbf{\textcolor{myred}{Error Handling Mushkil Hota Hai:}}
    \begin{itemize}
        \item Agar koi error aayi, to hum proper status code (\texttt{404}, \texttt{500}) aur error message bhej nahi sakte.
    \end{itemize}

    \item \textbf{\textcolor{myred}{No Control Over Response:}}
    \begin{itemize}
        \item Hum response me headers (e.g., metadata) add nahi kar sakte, aur body ko customize karna mushkil hota hai.
    \end{itemize}
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{\textcolor{mypurple}{Example Without \texttt{ResponseEntity<?>}}}

\begin{lstlisting}
@GetMapping("/todo/{id}")
public TodoEntity getTodoById(@PathVariable Long id) {
    TodoEntity todo = todoService.findById(id);

    if (todo == null) {
        return null; // Default response
    }

    return todo; // Default success response
}
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{\textcolor{myred}{Problems:}}
\begin{itemize}
    \item Agar \texttt{todo} na mile, to \texttt{null} return hoga, aur status code \texttt{200 OK} hi rahega.
    \item Client ko pata hi nahi chalega ki data kyun nahi mila ya kya problem hai.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{\textcolor{mypurple}{Solution: Using \texttt{ResponseEntity<?>}}}

\texttt{ResponseEntity<?>} ka use karke hum response ko \textbf{fully customize} kar sakte hain:
\begin{enumerate}
    \item \textbf{Custom Status Codes:} Success ke liye \texttt{200 OK}, data na mile to \texttt{404 Not Found}, aur error ke liye \texttt{500 Internal Server Error}.
    \item \textbf{Error Message:} Hum ek meaningful error message bhej sakte hain jo client ko help kare.
    \item \textbf{Control Over Headers and Body:} Response headers aur body ko modify karna possible hota hai.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{\textcolor{mypurple}{What Does \texttt{<?>} in \texttt{ResponseEntity<?>} Mean?}}

\begin{enumerate}
    \item \textbf{\texttt{<?>} Kya Hai?}
    \begin{itemize}
        \item Yeh ek \textbf{wildcard generic} hai, jo batata hai ki \texttt{ResponseEntity} ka response body kisi bhi type ka ho sakta hai.
    \end{itemize}

    \item \textbf{Flexibility Ka Example:}
    \begin{itemize}
        \item Response body \texttt{String}, \texttt{Object}, ya \texttt{List} kuch bhi ho sakti hai.
        \item Example:
        \begin{itemize}
            \item \texttt{ResponseEntity<String>}: Sirf ek string bhejni ho.
            \item \texttt{ResponseEntity<TodoEntity>}: Ek single \texttt{TodoEntity} object bhejna ho.
            \item \texttt{ResponseEntity<List<TodoEntity>>}: Todo objects ki list bhejni ho.
        \end{itemize}
    \end{itemize}

    \item \textbf{Agar \texttt{<?>} Use Karein:}
    \begin{lstlisting}
ResponseEntity<?> response;
response = ResponseEntity.ok("Hello World"); // String type
response = ResponseEntity.ok(todo); // Object type
    \end{lstlisting}
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{\textcolor{mypurple}{Example With \texttt{ResponseEntity<?>}}}

\begin{lstlisting}
@GetMapping("/todo/{id}")
public ResponseEntity<?> getTodoById(@PathVariable Long id) {
    TodoEntity todo = todoService.findById(id);

    if (todo == null) {
        // Todo nahi mila, 404 error ke saath response bhejo
        return ResponseEntity.status(404).body("Todo not found.");
    }

    // Success case: Todo mil gaya, 200 OK response bhejo
    return ResponseEntity.ok(todo);
}
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{\textcolor{mypurple}{Flow:}}

\begin{enumerate}
    \item \textbf{Agar Todo ID Valid Hai:}
    \begin{itemize}
        \item \texttt{todo} milta hai, aur \texttt{ResponseEntity.ok(todo)} ke saath \texttt{200 OK} response bheja jata hai.
    \end{itemize}

    \item \textbf{Agar Todo ID Invalid Hai:}
    \begin{itemize}
        \item \texttt{todo} nahi milta, to \texttt{ResponseEntity.status(404).body("Todo not found.")} ke saath error response bhejte hain.
    \end{itemize}
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{\textcolor{mypurple}{Responses:}}
\textbf{Todo Found:}
\begin{lstlisting}
{
    "id": 1,
    "title": "Complete Homework",
    "description": "Finish math homework",
    "completed": false
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{Status Code:} \texttt{200 OK}

\textbf{Todo Not Found:}
\begin{lstlisting}
{
    "message": "Todo not found."
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{Status Code:} \texttt{404 Not Found}

\subsection*{\textcolor{mypurple}{Why Beginners Should Use \texttt{ResponseEntity<?>}}}

\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{\textcolor{myred}{Problem Without \texttt{ResponseEntity<?>}:}}
    \begin{itemize}
        \item \textbf{Status Code Always \texttt{200 OK}:}
        \begin{itemize}
            \item Data na mile ya error ho, tab bhi \texttt{200 OK} milta hai (misleading response).
        \end{itemize}
    \end{itemize}

    \item \textbf{\textcolor{mygreen}{Solution With \texttt{ResponseEntity<?>}:}}
    \begin{enumerate}
        \item \textbf{Custom Status Codes:}
        \begin{itemize}
            \item Success: \texttt{200 OK}
            \item Data Not Found: \texttt{404 Not Found}
            \item System Error: \texttt{500 Internal Server Error}
        \end{itemize}

        \item \textbf{Custom Body:}
        \begin{itemize}
            \item Hum meaningful messages aur data bhej sakte hain.
        \end{itemize}

        \item \textbf{Dynamic Responses:}
        \begin{itemize}
            \item Response ki type dynamically decide hoti hai.
        \end{itemize}
    \end{enumerate}
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{\textcolor{mypurple}{Full Beginner-Friendly Code Example}}

\begin{lstlisting}
@GetMapping("/todo/{id}")
public ResponseEntity<?> getTodoById(@PathVariable Long id) {
    TodoEntity todo = todoService.findById(id);

    if (todo == null) {
        // 404 Not Found response
        return ResponseEntity.status(404).body("Todo not found.");
    }

    // 200 OK response
    return ResponseEntity.ok(todo);
}
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{\textcolor{mypurple}{Summary:}}

\begin{enumerate}
    \item \texttt{ResponseEntity<?>} ka use error handling aur dynamic responses ke liye hota hai.
    \item \texttt{<?>} batata hai ki response body kisi bhi type ki ho sakti hai (e.g., \texttt{String}, \texttt{Object}, \texttt{List}).
    \item Agar hum \texttt{ResponseEntity<?>} use nahi karte, to default response \texttt{200 OK} hota hai, jo galat indication de sakta hai.
\end{enumerate}

    captionpos=b

% Document Title

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]

\title{\textbf{\textcolor{violet}{\huge Hinglish Notes: Handling Password Exposure in API Responses with @JsonIgnore}}}

\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{document}

\maketitle

\section*{\textcolor{important}{Problem: Password Field Is Sent in API Response with \texttt{@JsonIgnore}}}
Agar aapka Spring Boot application me \texttt{UserSignupEntity} object API response me serialize ho raha hai, to \textbf{\textcolor{important}{password field}} bhi JSON me send ho jata hai. Yeh security ke liye risky hai kyunki hashed password ko bhi API ke through expose karna achha practice nahi hai.

\subsection*{\textcolor{important}{Example Problem}}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=json, caption=Example JSON Response with Password Field]
{
    "id": 6,
    "email": "satyam@gmail.com",
    "password": "$2a$10$q5AF/zqMrheOpu5YGnfP7eNR2dwhZR.k.P64t02rcHEiH6QtGzO/6",
    "role": "user",
    "createdAt": "2025-02-09T16:20:34.792+00:00"
}
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{\textcolor{important}{Issue:}}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{\textcolor{important}{Password field API response me visible hai, jo security breach ka reason ban sakta hai.}}
\end{itemize}

\section*{\textcolor{important}{Solution 1: Use \texttt{@JsonIgnore} on the Password Field}}
Agar aapko password field ko API response me se \textbf{\textcolor{important}{exclude}} karna hai, to \texttt{UserSignupEntity} class me password field par \texttt{@JsonIgnore} annotation lagao.

\subsection*{\textcolor{important}{Updated \texttt{UserSignupEntity} Class}}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=java, caption=Updated UserSignupEntity Class]
import com.fasterxml.jackson.annotation.JsonIgnore;

@Entity
public class UserSignupEntity {
    @Id
    @GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY)
    private Long id;

    @Column(nullable = false, unique = true)
    private String email;

    @JsonIgnore // Yeh password field ko JSON me serialize hone se rokega
    private String password;

    private String role;

    private LocalDateTime createdAt;

    // Getters and setters
}
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{\textcolor{important}{How It Solves the Problem}}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{\textcolor{important}{\texttt{@JsonIgnore} Kya Karta Hai?}}  
    Jackson library ko batata hai ki \textbf{\textcolor{important}{password field ko JSON response me include mat karo.}}
    \item Yeh backend me password ko available rakhta hai (e.g., authentication ke liye), lekin frontend ko expose nahi karta.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{\textcolor{important}{Response After Fix}}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=json, caption=Fixed JSON Response Without Password Field]
{
    "id": 6,
    "email": "satyam@gmail.com",
    "role": "user",
    "createdAt": "2025-02-09T16:20:34.792+00:00"
}
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{\textcolor{important}{Password field ab JSON me visible nahi hai.}}

\section*{\textcolor{important}{Why Use \texttt{@JsonIgnore}?}}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{\textcolor{important}{Easy to Use:}}  
    Sirf ek line ka annotation lagane se field exclude ho jata hai.
    \item \textbf{\textcolor{important}{Secures Sensitive Data:}}  
    API response me sensitive fields (jaise password) ko expose hone se rokta hai.
    \item \textbf{\textcolor{important}{No Impact on Backend Logic:}}  
    Password backend me authentication ke liye available rahta hai.
\end{itemize}

\section*{\textcolor{important}{Limitation of \texttt{@JsonIgnore}}}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{\textcolor{important}{Static Solution:}}  
    Agar kisi field ko dynamically hide karna ho (e.g., kisi specific endpoint ke liye), to \texttt{@JsonIgnore} kaam nahi karega. Iske liye DTO ya \texttt{@JsonView} use karna better hai.
\end{itemize}

===============================

\begin{document}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]

% Title
\begin{center}
  {\bfseries\Huge\color{headingblue} Relationships (`@ManyToOne`) API Responses Mein Nested Objects Automatically Kyu Include Hote Hain \par}
\end{center}

\end{tcolorbox}

---

### **Nested Objects Kya Hote Hain? (Simple Explanation with Example)**

\subsection{Nested Object Kya Hota Hai?}
Ek **nested object** woh object hota hai jo kisi aur object ke andar hota hai. Programming mein, yeh tab hota hai jab ek object ka dusre object ke saath relationship hota hai. For example:
- Ek `Todo` object ka `User` object ke saath relationship ho sakta hai (jo user ne todo create kiya hai).
- Jab aap `Todo` object fetch karte hain, toh `User` object automatically response mein include ho jata hai kyuki dono ke beech mein relationship hai.

\subsection{Nested Objects Ka Example}
Maano aapke paas do entities hain:
1. **`Todo` Entity**: Ek task ko represent karti hai.
2. **`User` Entity**: Us user ko represent karti hai jisne task create kiya hai.

`Todo` entity ka `User` entity ke saath `@ManyToOne` relationship hai. Jab aap `Todo` fetch karte hain, toh `User` object automatically response mein include ho jata hai.

\begin{examplebox}{Todo.java}
\begin{lstlisting}
@Entity
public class Todo {
    @Id
    private Long id;

    private String title;

    @ManyToOne
    @JoinColumn(name = "user_id")
    private User user; // User ke saath relationship
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

Jab aap `Todo` fetch karte hain, toh API response kuch aisa dikhega:
\begin{examplebox}{API Response}
\begin{lstlisting}
{
    "id": 1,
    "title": "Complete Spring Boot",
    "user": {
        "id": 6,
        "email": "user@example.com",
        "password": "hashed_password",  // Sensitive data expose ho raha hai
        "role": "admin"
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

---

### **Yeh Kyu Hota Hai?**

\subsection{Jackson Library}
Spring Boot **Jackson library** ka use karta hai JSON serialization ke liye. Jackson automatically sabhi fields ko include karta hai, including nested relationships, API response mein.

\subsection{Nested Objects Mein Problem}
1. **Sensitive Data Leak**: Fields jaise `password` response mein expose ho jate hain.
2. **Unwanted Data**: Response mein unnecessary data include ho jata hai, jisse uska size badh jata hai.

---

### **Nested Object Serialization Ko Kaise Rokhein?**

\subsection{Solution 1: `@JsonIgnore` Ka Use Karein}
Specific fields ko serialization se exclude karne ke liye `@JsonIgnore` ka use karein.

\begin{examplebox}{User.java}
\begin{lstlisting}
@Entity
public class User {
    @Id
    private Long id;

    private String email;

    @JsonIgnore // Password ko serialization se exclude karein
    private String password;

    private String role;
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

\subsection{Solution 2: `@JsonIgnoreProperties` Ka Use Karein}
Nested relationships mein specific fields ko exclude karne ke liye `@JsonIgnoreProperties` ka use karein.

\begin{examplebox}{Todo.java}
\begin{lstlisting}
@Entity
public class Todo {
    @Id
    private Long id;

    private String title;

    @ManyToOne
    @JoinColumn(name = "user_id")
    @JsonIgnoreProperties({"password"}) // User se password ko exclude karein
    private User user;
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

\subsection{Solution 3: DTOs (Data Transfer Objects) Ka Use Karein}
DTOs aapko full control dete hain ki API response mein kya data include karna hai.

\begin{examplebox}{DTOs}
\begin{lstlisting}
public class TodoDTO {
    private Long id;
    private String title;
    private UserDTO user; // Sirf required fields include karein
}

public class UserDTO {
    private Long id;
    private String email;
    private String role; // Password ko exclude karein
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

---

### **Key Points for Notes**

1. **Problem**:
   - Relationships jaise `@ManyToOne` ki wajah se nested objects automatically API responses mein include ho jate hain.

2. **Yeh Kyu Hota Hai**:
   - Jackson, jo Spring Boot ka default JSON serializer hai, sabhi fields ko include karta hai, including nested relationships.

3. **Solutions**:
   - Specific fields ko exclude karne ke liye `@JsonIgnore` ka use karein.
   - Nested relationships mein fields ko exclude karne ke liye `@JsonIgnoreProperties` ka use karein.
   - Response structure par full control pane ke liye DTOs ka use karein.

4. **Best Practice**:
   - Jab bhi aapko API response par full control chahiye, DTOs ka use karein.

---

### **Final Takeaway**
"Spring Boot mein relationships jaise `@ManyToOne` ki wajah se nested objects automatically API responses mein include ho jate hain. Sensitive data expose hone se bachne ke liye `@JsonIgnore`, `@JsonIgnoreProperties`, ya DTOs ka use karein."

---

% End of Document

% Define custom colors

\definecolor{greenexample}{RGB}{0, 153, 76}
\definecolor{redwarning}{RGB}{204, 0, 0}
\definecolor{lightbluecode}{RGB}{173, 216, 230}



% Code block settings
\lstset{
    backgroundcolor=\color{lightbluecode},
    basicstyle=\ttfamily\footnotesize,
    frame=single,
    keywordstyle=\color{blueheading}\bfseries,
    commentstyle=\color{greenexample},
    stringstyle=\color{redwarning},
    showstringspaces=false
}

\begin{document}


\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]

\title{\textbf{\textcolor{violet}{\huge {Understanding \texttt{==} vs \texttt{.equals()} in Java}}
\textcolor{blueheading}{In Java (and Spring Boot), when comparing \textbf{strings}, it’s important to understand the difference between \texttt{==} and \texttt{.equals()}.}}}


\end{tcolorbox}

---

\section{\texttt{==} kya karta hai?}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \texttt{==} compares \textbf{memory reference} (\textit{yani, dono objects ka address memory mein same hai ya nahi}).
    \item Agar do strings ka \textbf{reference} same hai toh hi \texttt{==} \texttt{true} return karega, \textbf{\textcolor{redwarning}{chahe unka content same ho ya na ho}}.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{Example:}
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=lightbluecode, colframe=blueheading, title=Java Code Example]
\begin{lstlisting}
String s1 = "admin";
String s2 = "admin";

if (s1 == s2) {
    System.out.println("Matched!"); // Ye chalega, kyunki dono ka reference same hai (interned string).
}

String s3 = new String("admin");

if (s1 == s3) {
    System.out.println("Matched!"); // Ye nahi chalega, kyunki reference alag hai, even though content same hai.
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

---

\section{\texttt{.equals()} kya karta hai?}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \texttt{.equals()} compares the \textbf{content} of the objects (\textit{yani strings ke andar ka actual data compare karega}).
    \item Isse koi farak nahi padta ki unka reference same hai ya alag.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{Example:}
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=lightbluecode, colframe=blueheading, title=Java Code Example]
\begin{lstlisting}
String s1 = "admin";
String s3 = new String("admin");

if (s1.equals(s3)) {
    System.out.println("Matched!"); // Ye chalega, kyunki content (value) same hai.
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

---

\section{Problem with \texttt{==} in Strings}
\begin{itemize}
    \item Jab aap Spring Boot mein strings like \texttt{role} ya \texttt{email} ko compare karte ho (\texttt{role == "admin"}), toh yeh dangerous ho sakta hai.
    \item Kyunki kabhi kabhi string alag memory mein store hoti hai (e.g., database se aaye data, HTTP request body), toh \texttt{==} fail karega even if the content is the same.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{Example:}
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=lightbluecode, colframe=blueheading, title=Java Code Example]
\begin{lstlisting}
String role = request.getAttribute("role"); // Database ya HTTP request se aaye.
if (role == "admin") {
    System.out.println("Role matched!"); // Ye fail karega, kyunki memory references alag hain.
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

---

\section{\texttt{.equals()} Reliable Hai}
\begin{itemize}
    \item Jab aap \texttt{.equals()} use karte ho, toh sirf \textbf{content match} hona zaruri hai.
    \item Isliye Spring Boot ya kisi bhi Java application mein string comparison ke liye \textbf{\textcolor{redwarning}{hamesha \texttt{.equals()} use karna chahiye.}}
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{Example (Correct Way):}
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=lightbluecode, colframe=blueheading, title=Java Code Example]
\begin{lstlisting}
String role = (String) request.getAttribute("role");
if ("admin".equals(role)) { // Always put "constant" first to avoid NullPointerException
    System.out.println("Role matched!"); // Ye hamesha sahi kaam karega.
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

---

\section{Why Use \texttt{"admin".equals(role)} Instead of \texttt{role.equals("admin")}?}
\begin{itemize}
    \item Jab aap \texttt{"admin".equals(role)} likhte ho, toh agar \texttt{role} null hai, tab bhi code crash nahi karega.
    \item Par agar \texttt{role.equals("admin")} likha aur \texttt{role} null nikla, toh \textbf{\textcolor{redwarning}{NullPointerException}} aayegi.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{Example:}
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=lightbluecode, colframe=blueheading, title=Java Code Example]
\begin{lstlisting}
String role = null;

if ("admin".equals(role)) {
    System.out.println("Matched!"); // Safe hai, null par bhi chalega.
}

if (role.equals("admin")) {
    System.out.println("Matched!"); // NullPointerException throw karega.
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

---

\section{Conclusion (Samajhne Layak Baat)}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{\texttt{==}}: Use tab karo jab tumhe \textbf{\textcolor{redwarning}{reference (address)}} check karna hai (bohot rare scenarios mein).
    \item \textbf{\texttt{.equals()}}: Strings ka \textbf{\textcolor{redwarning}{actual content compare}} karne ke liye hamesha use karo.
    \item \textbf{Safe pattern}: \texttt{"value".equals(variable)} likho, taaki null pointer ka risk na ho.
\end{itemize}

===============================
\hrule

\begin{document}



% Title
\begin{center}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]
  {\bfseries\Huge\color{headingblue} Understanding @OneToMany and @ManyToOne with Cascade and OrphanRemoval \par}


\end{tcolorbox}
  
\end{center}



% Introduction
\section{Introduction}
Agar aap Spring Boot aur Hibernate me relationships samajhna chahte hain, toh ye guide aapke liye hai. Ye guide aapko **@OneToMany** aur **@ManyToOne** annotations ke saath **Cascade** aur **OrphanRemoval** ka concept samjhayega.

---

% Section 1: Relationship Basics
\section{1. Relationship Basics: Parent and Child}

\subsection{Parent and Child Concept:}
\begin{itemize}
  \item \textbf{Parent Entity}: The entity that owns the lifecycle of the related entities (e.g., `UserSignupEntity` is the parent of `TodoEntity`).
  \item \textbf{Child Entity}: The entity that is dependent on the parent entity (e.g., `TodoEntity` is the child in the relationship).
\end{itemize}

\subsection{Defining Parent Entity: `UserSignupEntity`}
\begin{examplebox}{UserSignupEntity.java}
\begin{lstlisting}
@Entity
public class UserSignupEntity {
    @Id
    @GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY)
    private Long id;

    private String email;

    @OneToMany(mappedBy = "user", cascade = CascadeType.ALL, orphanRemoval = true)
    private List<TodoEntity> todos = new ArrayList<>();
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}



\subsection{Explanation of `private List<TodoEntity> todos = new ArrayList<>();`}
\begin{itemize}
  \item \textbf{1. List<TodoEntity>:}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item Ye ek list hai jo `UserSignupEntity` ke saath associated sabhi `TodoEntity` objects ko store karegi.
      \item Matlab, ek user ke paas multiple todos ho sakte hain, aur ye list un todos ko hold karegi.
    \end{itemize}

  \item \textbf{2. `new ArrayList<>()`:}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item Ye list ko initialize karta hai aur ek empty `ArrayList` banata hai.
      \item \textbf{Kyun zaroori hai?}
        \begin{itemize}
          \item Agar list initialize nahi ki jaye (yani `new ArrayList<>()` na likha jaye), to ye list `null` rahegi.
          \item `Null` list par koi bhi operation (jaise add ya remove) karne se error aayega (`NullPointerException`).
          \item Isliye, `new ArrayList<>()` likhna zaroori hai taaki list ready ho objects ko store karne ke liye.
        \end{itemize}
    \end{itemize}

  \item \textbf{3. Purpose (Maqsad):}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item Ye list `UserSignupEntity` aur `TodoEntity` ke beech ka relationship represent karti hai.
      \item Ek user (`UserSignupEntity`) ke paas multiple todos (`TodoEntity`) ho sakte hain, aur ye list un todos ko store karti hai.
    \end{itemize}
\end{itemize}




---

% Section 2: Child Entity: `TodoEntity`
\section{2. Child Entity: `TodoEntity`}

\begin{examplebox}{TodoEntity.java}
\begin{lstlisting}
@Entity
public class TodoEntity {
    @Id
    @GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY)
    private Long id;

    private String title;

    @ManyToOne
    @JoinColumn(name = "user_id", nullable = false)
    private UserSignupEntity user;
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

\subsection{Explanation:}
\begin{itemize}
  \item \textbf{1. `@ManyToOne`:}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item Define karta hai ki ek `TodoEntity` ek `UserSignupEntity` ke saath associated hai.
    \end{itemize}
  \item \textbf{2. `@JoinColumn(name = "user_id")`:}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item Database me `user_id` naam ka foreign key column create karega jo `TodoEntity` ko `UserSignupEntity` ke primary key se link karega.
    \end{itemize}
\end{itemize}

---

% Section 3: Explanation of Each Part
\section{3. Explanation of Each Part}

\subsection{1. `@OneToMany`:}
\begin{itemize}
  \item Yeh relationship define karta hai ki ek \textbf{UserSignupEntity} (Parent) ke paas \textbf{many TodoEntity} (Child) ho sakte hain.
\end{itemize}

\subsection{2. `mappedBy = "user"`:}
\begin{itemize}
  \item `mappedBy` batata hai ki relationship ka "ownership" kis side se hai.
  \item `mappedBy = "user"` ka matlab hai ki `TodoEntity` me ek field `user` hai jo relationship ko define karta hai.
  \item Iska matlab:
    \begin{itemize}
      \item `UserSignupEntity` relationship ko "own" nahi karta.
      \item `TodoEntity` ke `@ManyToOne` annotation ke andar `user` field relationship ke liye responsible hai.
    \end{itemize}
\end{itemize}

\subsection{3. `cascade = CascadeType.ALL`:}
\begin{itemize}
  \item Cascade ka matlab hai ki:
    \begin{itemize}
      \item Jab `UserSignupEntity` par koi operation (save, update, delete) perform hota hai, to uske saath linked \textbf{todos par bhi wahi operation chalega}.
    \end{itemize}
  \item Example:
    \begin{itemize}
      \item Agar ek `User` delete hota hai, to uske saare `Todos` automatically delete ho jayenge.
    \end{itemize}
\end{itemize}

\subsection{4. `orphanRemoval = true`:}
\begin{itemize}
  \item Orphan ka matlab hai: \textbf{A child entity that is no longer associated with its parent.}
  \item `orphanRemoval = true` ka matlab hai ki agar:
    \begin{itemize}
      \item `TodoEntity` ko `UserSignupEntity` ki `todos` list se hata diya jaye, to woh database me bhi automatically delete ho jayega.
    \end{itemize}
  \item Example:
    \begin{examplebox}{Removing a Todo}
    \begin{lstlisting}
    user.getTodos().remove(todo); // Removes the Todo from the User's list
    \end{lstlisting}
    \end{examplebox}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item Iske baad, woh `Todo` entity database se bhi delete ho jayega.
    \end{itemize}
\end{itemize}

---

% Section 4: Why Cascading in `@ManyToOne` is Not Recommended?
\section{4. Why Cascading in `@ManyToOne` is Not Recommended?}

\subsection{Problem with Cascade in `@ManyToOne`:}
\begin{examplebox}{Not Recommended}
\begin{lstlisting}
@ManyToOne(cascade = CascadeType.ALL) // ❌ Not Recommended
@JoinColumn(name = "user_id", nullable = false)
private UserSignupEntity user;
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

\begin{itemize}
  \item Iska matlab hai:
    \begin{itemize}
      \item Jab ek \textbf{TodoEntity} par operation perform hota hai, to uske associated \textbf{UserSignupEntity} par bhi woh operation chalega.
    \end{itemize}
  \item \textbf{Issue Example:}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item Ek `Todo` delete karte ho to associated `User` bhi delete ho jayega.  
      \item This is \textbf{wrong behavior}, kyunki ek task delete hone se poora user delete nahi hona chahiye.
    \end{itemize}
\end{itemize}

---

% Section 5: Real-Life Example: Parent-Child Flow
\section{5. Real-Life Example: Parent-Child Flow}

\subsection{1. Parent (`UserSignupEntity`):}
\begin{examplebox}{UserSignupEntity.java}
\begin{lstlisting}
@Entity
public class UserSignupEntity {
    @Id
    @GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY)
    private Long id;

    private String email;

    @OneToMany(mappedBy = "user", cascade = CascadeType.ALL, orphanRemoval = true)
    private List<TodoEntity> todos = new ArrayList<>();
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

\subsection{2. Child (`TodoEntity`):}
\begin{examplebox}{TodoEntity.java}
\begin{lstlisting}
@Entity
public class TodoEntity {
    @Id
    @GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY)
    private Long id;

    private String title;

    @ManyToOne
    @JoinColumn(name = "user_id", nullable = false)
    private UserSignupEntity user;
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

\subsection{Flow Example:}
\begin{itemize}
  \item \textbf{1. Delete a Parent (UserSignupEntity):}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item Jab ek user delete hota hai, to uske saare todos (`cascade = CascadeType.ALL`) delete ho jate hain.
    \end{itemize}
  \item \textbf{2. Remove a Todo from User’s List:}
    \begin{examplebox}{Removing a Todo}
    \begin{lstlisting}
    user.getTodos().remove(todo);
    \end{lstlisting}
    \end{examplebox}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item `orphanRemoval = true` hone ki wajah se woh `Todo` database se bhi delete ho jata hai.
    \end{itemize}
  \item \textbf{3. Delete a Todo Directly:}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item `TodoEntity` delete karna user ke upar koi impact nahi dalta.
    \end{itemize}
\end{itemize}

---

% Section 6: Beginner-Friendly Explanation of Terms
\section{6. Beginner-Friendly Explanation of Terms}

\begin{itemize}
  \item \textbf{1. `mappedBy`:}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item Batata hai ki \textbf{relationship ka control parent ya child me kahan hai.}
      \item Example:
        \begin{itemize}
          \item `mappedBy = "user"` ka matlab hai ki relationship ko child (`TodoEntity` ke `user` field) define kar raha hai.
        \end{itemize}
    \end{itemize}
  \item \textbf{2. `cascade`:}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item Parent ke operations ko automatically child entities tak propagate karta hai.
      \item Example:
        \begin{itemize}
          \item `CascadeType.ALL`: Save, update, delete, sab parent ke saath child par bhi chalega.
        \end{itemize}
    \end{itemize}
  \item \textbf{3. `orphanRemoval`:}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item Agar ek child entity parent ki list se remove ho jaye, to woh database se bhi automatically delete ho jata hai.
    \end{itemize}
\end{itemize}

---

% Section 7: Final Notes for Beginners
\section{7. Final Notes for Beginners}

\begin{itemize}
  \item \textbf{1. Cascading is One-Way:}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item Cascade behavior hamesha \textbf{parent se child} hota hai, reverse nahi.
    \end{itemize}
  \item \textbf{2. Parent Lifecycle Controls the Child:}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item Parent (`UserSignupEntity`) ke operations (delete, update) child (`TodoEntity`) ko impact karte hain.
    \end{itemize}
  \item \textbf{3. Avoid Cascade in @ManyToOne:}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item `@ManyToOne` me cascading mat lagao, kyunki child entity ka lifecycle parent ke control me hona chahiye.
    \end{itemize}
  \item \textbf{4. Key Annotations to Remember:}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item `@OneToMany` (Parent ke liye cascading behavior define karna).
      \item `@ManyToOne` (Child ke liye relationship define karna).
      \item `orphanRemoval = true` (Orphaned child entities ko automatically delete karna).
    \end{itemize}
\end{itemize}

---

===============================
\hrule

% Title
\begin{center}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=red!5!white,colframe=red!75!black,title=Point To Note]
  {\bfseries\Huge\color{headingblue} Object and var: Real Use Cases in Spring Boot \par}

\end{tcolorbox}
  
\end{center}

---

### **1. Using `Object`: When the Variable’s Type Is Dynamic**

\subsection{Problem:}
Suppose a user can update any field in a `TodoEntity`. Since you don't know in advance which field (e.g., `title`, `description`, `completed`) the user wants to update, the type of data could be different (string, boolean, etc.).

\subsection{Solution: Use `Object`}

\begin{examplebox}{TodoController.java}
\begin{lstlisting}
@RestController
@RequestMapping("/todo")
public class TodoController {

    @Autowired
    private TodoService todoService;

    @PatchMapping("/{id}")
    public ResponseEntity<?> updateTodoField(@PathVariable Long id, @RequestBody Map<String, Object> updates) {
        // Fetch the Todo to update
        TodoEntity todo = todoService.findById(id);
        if (todo == null) {
            return ResponseEntity.status(404).body("Todo not found");
        }

        // Iterate over the fields to update
        for (String key : updates.keySet()) {
            Object value = updates.get(key); // Object handles any type of value

            // Check which field to update
            switch (key) {
                case "title":
                    todo.setTitle((String) value); // Cast to String
                    break;
                case "description":
                    todo.setDescription((String) value); // Cast to String
                    break;
                case "completed":
                    todo.setCompleted((Boolean) value); // Cast to Boolean
                    break;
                default:
                    return ResponseEntity.status(400).body("Invalid field: " + key);
            }
        }

        // Save the updated Todo
        todoService.save(todo);
        return ResponseEntity.ok(todo);
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

\begin{importantbox}
\textbf{Why Use `Object` Here?}
\begin{itemize}
  \item The value from the `updates` map could be of any type (e.g., `String` for `title`, `Boolean` for `completed`), so you use `Object` to handle it.
  \item Later, you cast it to the correct type when updating the field.
\end{itemize}
\end{importantbox}

\subsection{Request Example:}

\begin{examplebox}{Input JSON}
\begin{lstlisting}
{
    "title": "Learn Spring Boot",
    "completed": true
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

\begin{examplebox}{Response}
\begin{lstlisting}
{
    "id": 1,
    "title": "Learn Spring Boot",
    "description": "Basic Spring Boot tasks",
    "completed": true
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

---

### **2. Using `var`: When the Type Can Be Automatically Inferred**

\subsection{Problem:}
In many cases, the datatype is clear from the context, but writing the full type makes the code longer and harder to read. For example, fetching a list of todos (`List<TodoEntity>`).

\subsection{Solution: Use `var`}

\begin{examplebox}{TodoService.java}
\begin{lstlisting}
@Service
public class TodoService {

    @Autowired
    private TodoRepository todoRepository;

    public List<TodoEntity> findAllTodos() {
        // Using var to simplify code
        var todos = todoRepository.findAll(); // Compiler infers todos as List<TodoEntity>
        return todos;
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

\begin{importantbox}
\textbf{Why Use `var` Here?}
\begin{itemize}
  \item You don't have to write `List<TodoEntity>` explicitly; the compiler knows the type from `findAll()` and infers it automatically.
  \item It simplifies the code without losing clarity.
\end{itemize}
\end{importantbox}

\subsection{Example in a Loop:}

\begin{examplebox}{TodoController.java}
\begin{lstlisting}
@GetMapping("/todos")
public ResponseEntity<?> getAllTodos() {
    var todos = todoService.findAllTodos(); // Compiler infers todos as List<TodoEntity>

    for (var todo : todos) { // Compiler infers todo as TodoEntity
        System.out.println(todo.getTitle());
    }

    return ResponseEntity.ok(todos);
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

---

### **Side-by-Side Simple Comparison**

\subsection{`Object` Example: Dynamic Field Update}

\begin{examplebox}{Dynamic Field Update}
\begin{lstlisting}
Object value = updates.get("completed"); // Value could be Boolean or String
todo.setCompleted((Boolean) value); // Cast to Boolean
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

\subsection{`var` Example: Fetching Todos}

\begin{examplebox}{Fetching Todos}
\begin{lstlisting}
var todos = todoRepository.findAll(); // Type inferred as List<TodoEntity>
\end{lstlisting}
\end{examplebox}

---

### **Key Takeaways:**
\begin{itemize}
  \item Use `Object` when the type of data is dynamic and unknown at compile time.
  \item Use `var` when the type is clear from the context, and you want to simplify the code.
  \item Both `Object` and `var` are powerful tools in Spring Boot for handling dynamic and inferred types.
\end{itemize}

---

===============================
\hrule

% End of Document


\end{document}
